# Lessons Learned — Structured Reference

This file is a decision aid for future Hew work. It is not a changelog.

Use it in this order:

1. Match the current change against a **core invariant** in the matching priority band.
2. Walk the **nuances** under that core; the trigger column tells you which apply.
3. Treat the **apply** column on each matching nuance as the minimum pre-merge checklist.
4. Start with the **P0** cores before applying any matching **P1** or **P2** nuances.
5. When two rules conflict, keep the stricter fail-closed, ownership-preserving, or parity-preserving rule.

## Two-level schema

A **core invariant** is the durable rule a future agent should remember even if every
nuance below it is forgotten. A **nuance** is a specific application, smell, or bug
class that has been seen in this codebase. Multiple nuances usually share one core.

Core block:

| Field | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| `core` | Stable short key for the core invariant. |
| `area` | Subsystem(s) where the core fires. |
| `invariant` | One-sentence durable rule. |
| `why` | The failure class the core prevents. |

Nuance row (table under the core):

| Column | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| `id` | Stable short key. **External code, docs, and specs reference these by string** — never rename a nuance id. |
| `trigger` | Smell or change pattern that should activate the nuance. |
| `apply` | Concrete check or action to take now. |
| `evidence` | Main PRs / JOURNEY workstreams that produced the nuance. |

## Priority bands

| Band | Use it for |
| --- | --- |
| `P0` | Silent wrong-code, memory safety, ownership, cleanup, or cross-language boundary risk. |
| `P1` | Parity, tests, diagnostics, toolchain, or user-surface trust. |
| `P2` | Architecture, cleanup, deduplication, and maintenance decisions that prevent repeat bugs. |

---

## P0 — Compiler/runtime correctness and boundary safety

### `boundary-fail-closed` — every cross-boundary handoff either carries the full payload or stops

- **area**: serialization, codegen, FFI, distributed surface, generated code
- **invariant**: A boundary that crosses Rust↔C++, host↔runtime, local↔remote, or generator↔repo must encode its full supported form or fail loudly with context. Silent omission, sentinel-shaped success, and emitted-but-uncounted diagnostics are bugs.
- **why**: Boundaries are where types lose their bite. Anything dropped or coerced to a sentinel becomes a silent wrong-output channel that the type system can no longer protect.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `runtime-bounds-trap-seam` | A runtime FFI entry point validates ordinary user-supplied bounds or preconditions itself instead of relying on a MIR/codegen pre-check. | Keep the check at the boundary, but route the failure through the shared trap seam (`runtime_bounds_trap` / `hew_trap_with_code`) rather than `libc::abort()`, `panic!()`, or a sentinel-shaped success. Native runtime callers must abort if `hew_trap_with_code` returns with no actor recovery context, because codegen's paired `llvm.trap` fallback is not present inside runtime functions. Classify nearby aborts before changing them: ordinary invalid input uses the trap seam; codegen-supplied metadata invariants and resource exhaustion remain distinct failure classes. Pin both actor-context isolation and main-context nonzero termination so the fix cannot become fail-open. | #2338: Vec method, bytes, and string runtime bounds failures now trap through the actor-isolating seam, with main-context exit-134 ratchets and actor-isolation fixtures. |
| `serializer-fail-closed` | A Rust-to-C++ or wire boundary must encode types, schema data, or unsupported shapes. | Reject unsupported nested forms, carry span/context through conversion, turn warning-and-skip paths into hard errors, and version or contract-test high-risk seams. | PR #812/#811/#808/#795. |
| `vec-element-width-symmetric-abi` | Adding or reclassifying a `Vec<T>` element width, constructor, method symbol, range-slice path, OR any element-ABI classification predicate (heap-owning, indirect-enum, BitCopy). | Treat the Vec element-width ABI as one contract across runtime exports, C ABI declarations, type-level method templates, HIR gates, MIR dispatch, codegen declarations/marshalling, and executable fixtures. Narrow integer and f32 values need dedicated typed symbols so push/set truncate to the storage width and get/pop sign- or zero-extend according to the Hew element type; range-slice can share one stride-generic byte-copy runtime symbol only after ownership-aware string/ptr/owned/layout paths have been selected first. The constructor's element-class decision (`layout_vec_element_needs_descriptor` or equivalent) is the AUTHORITY: every accessor — slice, range, iterator, sort — must route to the same layout tier. CRITICAL: the SAME element-ABI verdict must be reached independently by the checker (`vec_element_runtime_suffix`), MIR (`is_owned_vec_element` / `lower_vec_index` getter routing), AND codegen (constructor + `layout_vec_element_needs_descriptor`); a predicate that diverges in ONE layer (a record-layout-blind heap-owning check that misses record fields nested in a tuple; an enum-struct lookup that ignores `is_indirect`) builds the Vec under one ABI and operates it under another, and the runtime layout-aware abort fires after `hew check` passed. When two-or-more heap-owning/element-shape authorities must agree, do NOT keep them as sibling helpers that "mirror each other" — they DRIFT (one consults record fields, another does not; one has a `CancellationToken`/`Generator` leaf arm, another does not; one consults machine layouts, another does not). Collapse them onto ONE structural authority parameterised by a layout-lookup trait the MIR builder and codegen `FnCtx` each implement (record fields, enum/machine variant payloads, one builtin leaf set = `ValueClass::of_ty`'s heap classes), with thin per-layer adapters and NO re-derived leaf set. A heap-ownership fix that makes the MIR side classify MORE shapes owned (record-aware) is behaviour-CHANGING and exposes a DOWNSTREAM seed gap: a record/enum reachable ONLY as a tuple member now earns a `TupleInPlace` per-member drop whose `__hew_record_drop_inplace_<R>` thunk body is synthesised only if SEEDED — seed those tuple-member keys or LLVM verify rejects the module (`Global is external, but doesn't have external or weak linkage`). Verify parity with value-asserting fixtures (expected element values after a round-trip), NOT `.len()`-only counts; the latter gives a green gate even when the accessor misroutes to the wrong ABI variant and the program aborts on element access. The drop-correctness oracle is an absolute leak-node COUNT against a known-clean control under `leaks --atExit` + the `MallocScribble` triple, run in a helper-fn loop so the leaked buffer is unreachable at exit; a single-frame local masks the leak (the handle lingers in `main`'s stack slot). | feat/v060-vec-element-width: wired i8/u8/i16/u16/f32 Vec element-type storage, push/get truncation/extension, and stride-generic range-slice across runtime, codegen, MIR, and HIR. G5 lane (`feat/v06-vec-generic-surface`, 2026-06-22): `Vec<enum>` range-slice panicked after `hew check` passed — `ValueClass::Unknown` for enum elements fell to the layout-less `hew_vec_slice_range_ptr` path while the constructor had built a layout-vec; the mismatch aborted at runtime; surfaced by cross-ecosystem review; `.len()`-only fixtures across all existing Vec tests masked the abort entirely. #2191 (heap-owning tuple element `Vec<(Rec,i64)>`): MIR's tuple-arm heap-owning check used record-layout-blind `ty_contains_heap_owning`, mis-classifying the owned element non-owned, routing get to the layout getter on an owned-constructed Vec → runtime abort; fixed by routing the tuple arm through record-aware `named_elem_owns_heap`. #2150 (`Vec<indirect enum>`): codegen's `layout_vec_element_needs_descriptor` found the indirect enum's tagged-union struct in `record_layouts` (every enum is registered) and built a layout-vec while checker+MIR routed it to the pointer ABI → `hew_vec_push_ptr` abort; fixed by gating the codegen descriptor decision on `is_indirect_enum`. Both: anchored by value-asserting `.hew` fixtures (`vec_heap_owning_tuple_element_test`, `vec_indirect_enum_element_test`). refactor/v06-heap-ownership-authority (2026-06): collapsed the ~8 parallel heap-ownership walkers onto ONE `hew_mir::ty_owns_heap` over a `HeapOwnershipLayouts` trait (MIR + codegen adapters). Fixed TWO confirmed divergences: DIV-1 — the MIR walker `ty_contains_heap_owning` was record-field-BLIND, so a `(Boxed, i64)` tuple where `Boxed { payload: Vec<i64> }` earned NO member-drop and leaked 128 nodes (now 0 at the control floor); DIV-2 — the MIR/codegen owned-Vec element walkers (`named_elem_owns_heap`, `resolved_ty_contains_heap_leaf`) had NO `CancellationToken`/`Generator`/`AsyncGenerator` leaf arm while the drop elaborator (`ty_contains_heap_owning`) + `ValueClass::of_ty` did — a handle-bearing element's getter/ctor/free could disagree. The DIV-1 fix exposed the tuple-member seed gap (`__hew_record_drop_inplace_Boxed` dangled at LLVM verify); closed by `collect_tuple_member_inplace_drop_seeds`. Pinned by `heap_owning_record_in_tuple_leak_oracle.rs` (128→0 leak count + MallocScribble no-double-free) and codegen unit tests for the shared leaf set. refactor/v06-heap-drop-completion (2026-06): the record-aware authority is necessary but NOT sufficient — the owned-record/tuple sole-owner escape scans (`derive_owned_record_drop_allowed` / `derive_tuple_composite_drop_allowed`) must ALSO be borrow-aware. A heap-owning COLLECTION field/member (`Pair { b: Vec<i64> }`, `(Vec<i64>, i64)`) read through a borrowing method (`.len()`, `.get(i)`, indexing → `hew_vec_len` / `hew_vec_get_*`) was classified as ESCAPING and excluded the whole composite from its in-place drop → 128 leaks/scope-exit; the string side was already exempt (borrowing-string calls) but the collection side was not. Fixed by routing the field/element-binder escape scan through the SAME receiver-borrow authority the collection-LOCAL scan uses (`is_vec_receiver_borrow_symbol` / `is_collection_receiver_borrow_callee`) so a binder read only as the borrowed receiver (arg[0]) is an interior read, not an escape. Admitting those drops EXPOSED a latent double-free: a composite bound from an aliasing container getter (`let a = xs[i]` → `hew_vec_get_owned` returns an interior pointer into the still-live Vec element, NOT a fresh owner) earned its own in-place drop and double-freed a buffer the parent Vec's `hew_vec_free_owned` owns — excluded up front via `compute_collection_interior_alias_taint`. Pinned by `collection_field_binder_drop_leak_oracle.rs` (record/bare/tuple/nested/index + scalar/string/no-access controls, 128→0 + MallocScribble exactly-once). |
| `transparent-but-typed-failure` | A spec example, API signature, or distributed/reactor-suspended user surface lets remote lookup/send/ask/monitor, or a suspend-resume codegen ramp (accept/read/recv/stream-next), collapse a failure to a sentinel, zero value, or panic-shaped success. | Reject value-shaped `Node::lookup` and remote-ask documentation, require typed failure variants for not-found/partition/timeout/version/authz/decode/orphaned/stale/cancel/shutdown outcomes, grep examples for sentinel checks such as `!= 0`, and keep remote examples handling the error branch explicitly. A typed variant that EXISTS but is never RETURNED is the same fail-open — wire the producer, do not just declare the enum. Before reusing an EXISTING deposit/wake primitive (e.g. `reactor_detach_actor`'s `INVALID_CONNECTION_HANDLE` deposit) for a NEW caller, trace the RESUME-side codegen arbiter's actual branches (e.g. `emit_suspending_accept_bind` in `hew-codegen-rs/src/suspend.rs`), not just the deposit call — a binary timeout-vs-proceed arbiter built for its ORIGINAL caller silently routes any OTHER status (including an already-declared one like `AwaitCancelStatus::Cancelled`) into the success/`Ok(...)` branch. | `docs/specs/HEW-DIST-SPEC.md`; PR #1643. DIST-10 (`feat/v06-dist10-incarnation`): the `StaleRef` variant existed in `SendError`/`AskError`/`LookupError`/`MonitorError` but was never produced; the remote send/ask/monitor boundary now returns it on a superseded registration via one shared `dispatch_is_stale` gate (the captured `RemotePid` was silently routable to the replacement before). #2446 investigation (`fix/2446-drain-typed-outcome`): confirmed by direct code read that `emit_suspending_accept_bind`'s deadline arbiter only branches on `hew_await_cancel_status(reg) == TimedOut(3)`; depositing `INVALID_CONNECTION_HANDLE` (the existing actor-teardown convention) or the already-declared `AwaitCancelStatus::Cancelled(2)` both fall through to the take-handle/`Ok(_)` path — a fail-open a naive shutdown-time deposit+wake sweep would have shipped. Not yet a live bug (no caller reaches this path today); flagged before landing the sweep, not after. |
| `ctrl-frame-binds-to-authenticated-peer` | A new inbound `CTRL_*` distributed control-frame handler is added or reviewed. | Any field in the frame payload that names a node/peer (`ref_id`, `linker_node_id`, a claimed sender id) is attacker-controlled wire data, not identity. Resolve the actual handshake-authenticated peer for the connection (`authenticated_peer_node_id(mgr, conn_id, ctx)`) and reject on any mismatch — including the `authenticated == 0` case — BEFORE mutating any watcher/link/monitor state, not after. Do not trust a payload-carried node id for anything security-relevant. | Landed 3 times on the same class before this row existed: `CTRL_LINK_DOWN` (bound to authenticated peer instead of a bare `ref_id`), `CTRL_MONITOR_REQ`/`CTRL_DEMONITOR`/`CTRL_MONITOR_DOWN` (same pattern for the monitor family), `CTRL_LINK_REQ`/`CTRL_UNLINK` (any connected peer could register a phantom link claiming to be any node, zero guessing required — worse than the first two, which at least needed an enumerable `ref_id`). The first fix in the series initially missed the `authenticated == 0` case; every later fix inherited the correction. Next `CTRL_*` frame type added should check this row before it becomes a 4th instance. |
| `cli-exit-code-fail-closed` | A user-facing CLI path maps failure to exit 0, leaks an internal sentinel exit code, or has tests that only assert "non-zero" when the exact code is part of the contract. | Map CLI outcomes through one convention (`0` success, `1` error, `124` timeout), keep internal sentinels behind explicit embedding-only paths or retire them, require an explicit opt-out flag for permissive empty runs, and assert exact exit codes in e2e tests so garbage non-zero values cannot pass. | fix/v06-cli-exit-codes: `hew run`/`hew debug` compile errors now exit 1 instead of 125, `hew eval --json` exits non-zero for non-`ok`, and `hew test --allow-empty` is required to greenlight zero-test discovery. |
| `replaceable-resource-handle-is-fungible-reference` | A language handle stands for a resource OWNED-AND-REPLACEABLE elsewhere (a supervisor child, a pool member, a registry name, any restart/recreate-managed actor) whose backing pointer the owner may free and replace under the holder. Fires when an accessor resolves that handle to a raw pointer ONCE and caches it, OR when ANY send surface (tell / single-shot ask / select-ask arm) traps on a not-live resource — fixing one surface does not fix the others, since each lowers through a SEPARATE codegen path. | The handle MUST be a re-resolving `(owner, slot/key)` **reference**, not a snapshot of one instance — carry the stable key and re-resolve the current backing pointer via the owner's resolver AT EACH use (send/ask/select), never cache the resolved pointer across a yield. A snapshot dangles the instant the owner frees-and-replaces (restart) → UAF on a held-across-yield handle, or a program-killing trap when the send path can't reach the freed instance. Split the two concerns: (1) the ACCESSOR records the reference + seeds the slot but does NOT branch on liveness or trap — liveness is not the accessor's job; (2) the USE (send/ask/select) re-resolves and fail-closes a not-live resource RECOVERABLY (drop the tell / `Err` the ask / skip the select arm via the existing runtime null-guard), never a trap. EVERY send surface fails closed UNIFORMLY — audit each lowering path, not just the single-shot ask: a select-ask arm setup that treats a non-zero `ask_with_channel` status as a fatal mid-setup error traps where the single-shot ask binds `Err`; route the recoverable status to a per-arm recovery (free the channel, null its select-array slot so the first-ready dispatch + the null-guarded loser/teardown legs skip it) instead. Keep genuine internal setup errors (stream/task/channel poll-registration failures) fatal — only the send surfaces fail closed. The re-resolve-under-lock + use-within-the-same-cooperative-turn honours the runtime's "valid only this turn" borrow contract STRUCTURALLY, so no checker rule / freshness-taint is needed. The handle never owns the instance, so it earns NO scope-exit drop (the owner frees it) — do not add one. Prove with a fixture that BINDS the handle before a crash, holds it ACROSS a barrier-driven restart, and asserts an EXACT sentinel through the held reference (re-resolved to the fresh instance), plus permanently-down fixtures asserting the recoverable `Err`/drop/skip sentinel for EACH send surface (tell, single-shot ask, AND select-ask) — NOT survived-without-crash. | F-04 (`feat/v06-fungible-pid`, supersedes A180 `Option`/freshness-check designs): `sup.w` snapshotted the child `*mut HewActor` at the accessor; a tell/ask through the held handle after restart reached the freed actor → `HEW_TRAP_ACTOR_SEND_FAILED` SIGTRAP (exit 133) / UAF. Fixed by making the handle a fungible `(supervisor, slot)` ref (`FungibleChildRef` side-table keyed on the handle local) that re-resolves via `hew_supervisor_child_get` at each send/ask; tell branches on liveness (not-live → drop), ask stores the re-resolved (null-when-down) pointer and the runtime `actor_send_result_internal_reply` null-guard yields `Err(AskError::ActorStopped)`. The accessor trap is removed (`TrapKind::SupervisorChildUnavailable` retained as the codegen-bug primitive). The select-ask arm trapped INDEPENDENTLY after tell+ask were fixed: `emit_select_arm_setup` treated a non-zero `hew_actor_ask_with_channel` status as a fatal mid-setup error → `emit_select_setup_failure_trap`. Fixed by routing a non-zero ActorAsk ask-issue status to a per-arm recovery block (free the channel's caller-side ref, null its `channel_array` slot → `hew_select_first`/`hew_select_ready_index` skip it, every null-guarded loser/teardown leg treats it as absent); the shared setup helper covers the blocking + suspending select paths. Fixtures `supervisor_fungible_reresolve` (exit 7, held-across-restart) + `supervisor_fungible_dead_child` (exit 9, recoverable tell+ask Err) + `supervisor_fungible_dead_child_select` (exit 46, select-ask skips the dead arm → after-arm wins). Recover-edge heap-payload leak tracked (#2126). await-restart wait primitive deferred (#2124). Cousin: `transparent-but-typed-failure`. |
| `staleness-from-side-table-not-value` | A plan asks a captured value handle to carry a NEW identity dimension (incarnation, generation, epoch) so a boundary can detect staleness — but the handle's value representation has no room (a fully-packed integer, a bare pointer, a reused slot id) and the plan assumes "carry it in the value". Fires when the value is a bit-packed `uN` whose bits are fully consumed, or whose width is load-bearing across IR/codegen layers. | Do NOT bit-steal from an existing field (it caps the stolen field and re-tangles two axes) and do NOT reshape the value to a struct just to carry the dimension when that reshape spans many IR/codegen sites (a scope balloon) — STOP-and-report the value-reshape fork rather than silently taking it. Instead resolve staleness from a per-owner SIDE-TABLE keyed by a discriminator that is ALREADY monotonic and never reused (a serial/slot that the allocator guarantees unique): a captured handle uniquely names its original registration by that discriminator, and a supersession set (or generation map) keyed on it lets the dispatch boundary fail closed WITHOUT touching the value layout. Keep the explicit identity carrier (the ABI accessor + the struct field on the ref type) for the path that CAN carry it, and document that carrying it inside the value is a future direction gated on the reshape. Record supersession at EVERY producer that re-points the key (local register, gossip-propagated re-point, owner teardown) so all peers converge on the same verdict; consult it through ONE shared gate across every send surface. | DIST-10 (`feat/v06-dist10-incarnation`): `RemotePid<T>` is a bare packed `u64` (`node_id:16 | serial:48`, fully consumed) and i64 at every codegen/MIR/types site — the plan's "incarnation rides in the RemotePid value" was unrealizable without a 5+-site value reshape. Resolved via a `HewRegistry` supersession set keyed by the monotonic never-reused serial (`registration_record` on register + gossip ADD, `registry_supersede_serial` on teardown); `dispatch_is_stale` fails closed with `StaleRef` on send/ask/monitor. The explicit carrier (`hew_pid_make_with_incarnation`/`hew_pid_incarnation` + `HewActorRefRemote.incarnation`) landed for the path that can carry it. Cousins: `replaceable-resource-handle-is-fungible-reference`, `monotonic-epoch-single-clock`. |
| `multi-wall-fail-closed-feature-completion` | Completing a feature that was landed FAIL-CLOSED across multiple compiler layers (checker reject + MIR NYI + codegen `FailClosed`) — flipping the walls to working code. Also fires when a NEW mechanism makes an ADJACENT fail-closed guard obsolete, or when a flat snapshot buffer (memcpy of a moved-in value) starts holding OWNED heap fields. | A multi-layer fail-closed feature has MORE walls than the obvious three, and ALL must flip in dependency order or the feature is a no-op / leaks / UAFs. (1) Walk the walls bottom-up: the checker typing that stamps the discriminator into `expr_types` is the HARD PREREQ — the codegen emit is a literal no-op until the checker synthesises the init-arg expr types (gate the codegen stage on a verify-AST probe: the discriminator reaches MIR fully-resolved BEFORE touching codegen). (2) A NEW mechanism that fixes the exact hazard an ADJACENT guard defers MUST relax that guard in lockstep: a per-child init thunk that deep-clones owned state per incarnation is the structural fix the permanent-owned-heap byte-copy-aliasing wall flagged as deferred — so a child on the thunk path must be EXEMPTED from that wall (field-level: exempt an owned field covered by a reproducible init arg), or the feature stays rejected by a sibling wall it already obsoleted. (3) A flat snapshot buffer (`memcpy` of a moved-in config/value) OWNS the moved value's inner owned heap fields — consumers that only CLONE from it do not take that ownership. Freeing only the wrapper LEAKS the inner fields; register the value's `__hew_record_drop_inplace_<T>` and run it before the flat free. A type reachable from NO actor/record state field (a supervisor config struct used only as a param) must be SEEDED into the clone/drop synthesis set or its drop body is declared-but-undefined (LLVM verify reject). (4) Scope the relaxed admission to what codegen can ACTUALLY emit: admit owned `string`/`bytes` (direct clone helpers) but keep owned collections/records/enums + `#[resource]` handles walled — admitting a type whose clone path is `unreachable!`/`Err` turns a graceful checker reject into a codegen panic. PROVE each wall with the COMPILED suite + `leaks --atExit` AND the Guard-Malloc triple on an owned+restart fixture (a scalar config is 0-leak; the owned-config leak only shows on the owned path, and only with proper teardown — a never-stopped supervisor leaks everything at exit, a pre-existing exit-drain gap). | dynamic-init-c4c5 (`feat/v06-dynamic-init-c4c5`, 2026-06): `child cache: Cache(capacity: config.size)` was walled at 3 layers (checker `E_SUPERVISOR_INIT_ARG_NON_BITCOPY`, MIR `ConfigField` owned-NYI, codegen `FailClosed`). S1 checker init-arg-expr typing was the prereq; S2 codegen thunk (`__hew_child_init_<sup>_<child>`) + bootstrap config-param; S3 owned `string`/`bytes` clone-in-thunk flipped the wall to `ty_is_supervisor_init_reproducible`. TWO walls beyond the obvious three: the permanent-owned-heap guard (relaxed field-level for thunk-path children) and the config-buffer inner-field drop (`hew_supervisor_set_config_drop_fn` + `collect_supervisor_config_drop_seeds` — `leaks` caught a 32-byte owned-field leak the scalar path didn't have). Cousins: `end-to-end-before-layer-thickening`, `by-value-heap-params-are-borrows`, `replaceable-resource-handle-is-fungible-reference`, `unclonable-leaf-fails-closed-transitively`. |
| `generated-narrowing-guards` | A generator emits exact-width integer reads for the Rust→C++ msgpack boundary. | Centralize checked-width helpers in the shared generator preamble, route generic `u32` parses and special-cased schema metadata through them, and re-run both generator freshness and reader-lane tests after regeneration. | JOURNEY 2026-04-11 fix/astgen-u32-overflow-guards. |
| `llvm-intrinsic-signature-is-version-specific` | Emitting a call to ANY LLVM intrinsic (`llvm.lifetime.*`, `llvm.memcpy.*`, `llvm.coro.*`, a new overload) by hand-writing the operand list from a doc/spec/older-LLVM memory of its signature. | Spike the ACTUAL declaration shape against the pinned LLVM build BEFORE the production call: resolve via `Intrinsic::find(base_name).get_declaration(module, &[overload_ty])` (overloaded intrinsics need the overload type arg or `get_declaration` returns `None` — the `.pN`/`.iN` mangling suffix is PRODUCED, not consumed), then print the emitted declaration and match the call operands to it. Intrinsic signatures change between LLVM majors — `llvm.lifetime.start/end` dropped its explicit `i64 size` operand upstream, so on LLVM 22 the canonical form is the single-operand `void(ptr)`; a 2-operand call against the 1-operand declaration is a `Module::verify()` error, not a silent miscompile. A unit test that builds a tiny module, emits the call, and asserts both the call-site text AND `Module::verify()` Ok is the cheapest spike and the durable guard. Fail closed (`CodegenError::FailClosed`) when the intrinsic is absent from the build — a missing optimisation intrinsic is a build error, never a silent skip. | feat/v06-rc10-lifetime-markers (2026-06-21): the RC10 plan stated the `(i64 size, ptr)` lifetime signature; the Stage-1 spike caught the LLVM 22 single-operand `void(ptr)` form before any production edit (R3 mitigation). Models: the `coro_intrinsic_typed` overload-resolution path in `coro.rs`. |
| `elf-init-array-ctors` | A feature works on macOS but silently fails on Linux AND involves program-start registration or any init that runs via `@llvm.global_ctors` (codec registration, module-init, regex init, any ctor-based init). | Hew's LLVM-C `TargetMachine` has `UseInitArray=false` (no llvm-sys C setter exists), so `@llvm.global_ctors` lowers to the legacy `.ctors` section on ELF — not walked by glibc/musl and stripped by `--gc-sections`. Fix: emit constructor pointers into `.init_array` + mark the global `@llvm.used` (gains `SHF_GNU_RETAIN`, survives gc-sections) on ELF; keep `@llvm.global_ctors` for Mach-O/COFF; set the section via raw `LLVMSetSection` (inkwell `set_section` is build-host-gated and comma-mangles cross builds). Verify at the object level: `llvm-readobj --sections` must show `SHT_INIT_ARRAY`, not `.ctors`. Add a regression test asserting the ctor lands in the target-walked section (must fail without the fix). Confirm on a real Linux host, not macOS cross-inspection alone — macOS inspection masks the defect because Mach-O's `__mod_init_func` section IS walked. | PR #2246 (fix/v06-elf-init-array-ctors); obelisk Linux 8/8-fail → all-pass. |
| `field-alias-fail-closed` | A call expression passes a struct field as an arg, or a function returns a field of an owned parameter that receives a callee-side drop. | Scan call args for field-access expressions BEFORE emitting any call IR (not after — void calls swallow the rejection path); apply the same recursive field-yield scanner to wrapper expressions before print/println lowering; scan function bodies for field-of-param returns once the param-drop set is populated; always increment the error counter alongside the diagnostic so the module is rejected even when the diagnostic alone would not halt codegen. | PR #1746 (`fix/function-param-drop-alias-fail-closed`): a field passed to a void call / yielded by print / returned from a param escaped the drop without rejecting the module. |
| `drop-allowset-from-value-flow` | Deciding which heap-owning locals get a compiler-inserted scope-exit drop (COW/refcount/free elaboration), OR choosing how codegen picks the release symbol for such a drop. | Droppability must be an **allow-set derived from an exhaustive MIR value-flow proof of sole-ownership at every exit — never a HIR-shape producer-site deny-list**. A deny-list that instruments "known share sites" is fail-OPEN: any transparent/control-flow result move (block-tail, if/match-arm join, payload-destructure binder) it forgot re-opens the double-free under a different syntax wrapper. Instead: (1) scan EVERY `Instr`/`Terminator` source operand with exhaustive no-wildcard matches — any local read/aliased as a source is excluded; (2) seed alias taint on the **destination** of interior-projection loads AND any `Move` whose `src` is an interior-projection `Place` (classify every `Place` variant with a no-wildcard match so destructure binders that alias parent storage with no retain are tainted), propagate to a fixpoint; (3) default every omission/unresolved case to EXCLUSION (worst case = leak, never double-free). Classify BOTH source reads AND destination aliases — collapsing a projection `Move` src to its parent marks the parent read but does NOT exclude the binder dest. Codegen must validate `(type, release-symbol)` **congruence** (the kind-carried drop symbol equals the type-directed table's symbol for that leaf type), not mere symbol-allowlist membership, and dispatch on the builtin discriminant not the type name — else a malformed plan frees a handle through the wrong-ABI release entry. The runtime fixture often can't witness the layer-1 hole (dead-at-exit binders are masked by layer-3 liveness); the honest proof is a direct allow-set unit test with a negative control (fix-disabled → the binder is admitted). | W5.011 P3 (`27af3674`): a fail-OPEN `cow_escaped` HIR deny-list missed block-tail/if-arm/match-arm/destructure result moves → double-free; replaced by fail-closed `derive_cow_sole_owner` (exhaustive source-place scan + interior-projection taint on `Move` dests). Extensions, all the same INVERTED owner-escapes derivation for by-value composite returns: W5.020 enum composite (`7547ffc5`); single-heap-leaf `bytes` return — gate keyed on the LLVM struct-shape proxy not the semantic multi-owner property (`bytes` lowers to `BytesTriple` and wrongly hit the composite arm); W5.021 tuple/record-of-owned-handles (`Stream`/`Sink`) — first revision drove member move-out from the HIR return SHAPE (syntactic `mark_returned_binding_moved` recursion), the same fail-open class one level up, → SIGSEGV on `let pair=(s,r); pair`; replaced by value-flow `derive_returned_aggregate_member_bindings`; no runtime backstop — `hew_*_close` is an unguarded `Box::from_raw`. W3.053 generator/CancellationToken extraction + break/continue per-iteration leaks; the per-shape exclusion hops proved combinatorial (`2a47e5f5`) → replaced by a fail-closed GATE (`detect_unproven_aggregate_handle_double_free`): if exactly-once is unprovable, REFUSE with a diagnostic, never emit the double-free. W3.054 generic-record instantiation drop spine via the mangled layout key. W5.025 plain-Vec (`2026-06-10`): interior-alias getter borrows + fan-out alias groups (union-find over the Move graph). `Vec<record>` BitCopy-aggregate gap (`2026-06-19`): the plain-vs-owned ELEMENT-class predicates must be exhaustive AND disjoint — a Vec element is one of THREE classes (scalar/`string` plain, heap-owning owned, OR `BitCopy` value-aggregate record/enum/tuple); the plain filter (`binding_ty_is_plain_vec`) listed only scalars/`string` and the owned filter (`is_owned_vec_element`) only heap-owning records, so a `Vec<Point>` (`type Point { x: i64, y: i64 }`) matched NEITHER and earned NO drop → backing-buffer leak (no double-free, per the fail-closed default). Fixed by admitting a `Named`/`Tuple` element whose `ValueClass::of_ty == BitCopy` (the exact complement of `is_owned_vec_element`, agreeing with the `hew_vec_new_with_layout`/`hew_vec_get_layout` constructor routing) into the plain `hew_vec_free` arm. macOS `leaks --atExit` MASKS this single-frame leak (the handle lingers in a stack `alloca` → traced reachable); the loop+helper-fn oracle (stack slot reused per call → leaked buffers unreachable, the shape Valgrind catches) exposes it against a scalar-Vec control floor. Oracle lesson: behavioural/leak green is NON-EVIDENCE for ownership provers (wrong frees pass under allocator luck); the honest oracle is a `drop_plans`-level / release-call-COUNT assertion (`== 1`) per admitted AND excluded shape, with `MallocScribble` making freed-reads deterministic — NOT a presence test (`ir.contains`) or `leaks --atExit`. String `r.field`/`t.0` field-load double-free (`2026-06-19`, `fix/v06-string-field-load-double-free`): issue #37 retained fresh-PRODUCED string temps (`a + b`, `hew_vec_get_str`) but a `string` READ out of a still-live record/tuple (`RecordFieldLoad`/`TupleFieldLoad`) was emitted as a raw no-retain alias of the parent's field buffer; consumed into a sink (`hew_hashmap_insert` vacant-slot key-move, or a duplicate tuple-element read) it double-freed against the parent's own drop. The fix is TWO-SIDED and the two sides MUST land in lockstep: a codegen `hew_string_clone` retain at the field-load site REVERSES the no-retain premise, so the MIR side must ALSO (a) register the dest as a fresh `+1` producer (`string_field_load_producer_dest`) and (b) EXCLUDE it from the projection-alias taint seed (`compute_projection_alias_taint`, type-gated on the dest's `ResolvedTy` threaded as a `locals` table) so the existing `derive_cow_fresh_borrowed_owner` admits its one balancing `hew_string_drop` — exactly the `hew_vec_get_str` (`xs.get(i)`) retained-interior-load class. A codegen retain WITHOUT the MIR admission does NOT re-double-free; it INVERTS the bug into a leak (the `+1` has no drop). Scope is `string`-ONLY: non-string managed field loads (`bytes`/`Vec<T>`/nested record) are NOT retained (`cow_value_leaf_drop_symbol` returns `None`, never schedules their drop), so retaining them without a balancing drop would invert their SAFE leak too — leave them un-retained until the retain-on-share spine lands. Oracle-isolation trap: a `leaks --atExit` floor CANNOT witness this leak-inversion for a no-escape transient field read, because reading a string field SUPPRESSES the parent aggregate's own in-place field drop (the parent becomes a live operand) AND the retained value shares ONE refcounted buffer with the parent's field — so balanced vs un-balanced leaves the SAME single leaked buffer (a higher refcount, not a distinct node); that parent-field-drop leak is itself a pre-existing out-of-scope spine, equal pre/post-fix (verify by measuring the baseline SHA). Prove the no-escape balance by a `--dump-mir elab` retain==drop count (one `hew_string_drop` per field load on every exit + loop-back edge) plus a `MallocScribble` no-OVER-drop pin with an EXACT-output assertion (the parent drop and the retain drop both act on the shared buffer — a mis-balance over-decrements → sentinel abort or scribbled value), NOT a leak-node floor. Cousins: `field-alias-fail-closed`, `static-classification-vacuates-refcount-and-sanitizer`, `unclonable-leaf-fails-closed-transitively`. F-01 (`fix/v06-f01-actor-spawn-uaf`, 2026-06-23): `let t = Vec::new(); spawn Actor(field: t)` — MIR records the spawn aggregate operation as `AliasedIntoAggregate` (not `Consumed`/`MaybeConsumed`), so a classify-by-consumed-status escape scan admitted `t` as non-escaped and emitted a scope-exit drop → double-free (SIGSEGV at actor shutdown, deterministic under `MallocScribble`). One-function swap to `derive_local_collection_drop_allowed` at `hew-mir/src/lower.rs:24319` excludes `t` by finding it as a source operand of the spawn aggregate. Aggregate-into-spawn is a distinct taint class; the exhaustive source-operand scan covers it without enumerating each aggregation mode. #1942 (`fix/v06-match-vec-drop-fixpoint-hang`, 2026-06-27): the whole-value alias-propagation fixpoint that seeds these scans must be **monotone or it does not terminate** — `alias_of.insert(dl, root)` REPLACES a slot's root, so when one slot receives `Move`s from two distinct roots (a `match`/if-join result slot fed by two arms each constructing a fresh local collection) the two roots OSCILLATE, `changed` never clears, and lowering spins until SIGKILL (`hew check` hung at ~9.6s CPU on a 2-arm `Vec<i64>`-returning match — a compile HANG is worse than a clean reject). A propagation step may only ADD an entry or EVICT a conflicted one: a candidate adopting another group's root for the FIRST time (slot still self-seeded — the `let b = a;` merge) takes it once; a slot already carrying a DIFFERENT non-self root that sees a second distinct root is reachable from two groups, so EVICT it and bar re-entry (`conflicted` set). Each slot then transitions at most twice (self-seed/vacant → merged → conflicted), bounding the fixpoint at O(locals). Eviction is the conservative drop direction: an evicted slot reads as a non-member in the escape scan, so a `Move` into it EXCLUDES the source's root — fail-closed (the ambiguous group leaks, never double-frees), matching the layer-3 default. Extracted the five copies of the loop (enum/record/collection/bytes/tuple `derive_*_drop_allowed`) into one shared `propagate_whole_value_alias_roots` so every scan converges identically. Indirect-enum heap-node free (`feat/v06-drop-elaboration`, 2026-06-28, gap #46): an `indirect enum` (spec §3.7.4) node leaked, but a scope-exit drop arm ALONE could not reach 0 — the dominant leak root was UPSTREAM of any drop. The codegen eager-allocation prologue minted a `hew_alloc` node for EVERY non-parameter indirect-enum local, but move-temps (`_t = move _ctor`) and match destructure binders (`l = move mvar.payload`) immediately OVERWRITE their slot with a received pointer, orphaning the eager node — a leak no scope-exit drop can reclaim (the original pointer is gone by the time any drop runs). LESSON: when an over-eager ALLOCATION site mints storage a later instruction overwrites, the fix is at the allocation site (gate it), not (only) at the drop site; freeing the binding's resting slot never recovers the orphaned mint. Fix part 1: gate the prologue on a construction-site scan (a local written through a tag/variant place — `Move { dest: MachineTag/MachineVariant/EnumTag/EnumVariant(local) }`); under-allocating crashes loudly (use-before-alloc on the first tag GEP), never corrupts — so the conservative error allocates too FEW, surfacing immediately. Fix part 2 — the allow-set twist: indirect enums are `intent=Read` on EVERY by-value use (the move-checker treats them as borrows per `by-value-heap-params-are-borrows`), so NEITHER a return NOR a call-argument marks the binding `Consumed` — the consume-dataflow alone cannot prove sole ownership, and a return is INDISTINGUISHABLE from a borrow-pass at the `_X = move _src` MIR level. The fail-closed proof (`derive_indirect_enum_drop_allowed`): admit a binding iff its resting local (forward-propagated from a construction site through whole-value `Move`) owns a freshly-constructed node AND is NOT moved into a parent node's variant payload (`Move { dest: MachineVariant/EnumVariant{parent}, src: child }` — the parent's recursive free owns the child) AND survives the existing `returned_aggregate_members` skip + `Consumed` filter + fan-out union-find collapse. The recursive free is a synthesised `__hew_indirect_enum_free_<Enum>(ptr)` thunk: null-check, tag-dispatch, recurse into owned child indirect-enum pointers FIRST (post-order), then `hew_dealloc`; the block skeleton is appended BEFORE recursing into child thunks so a mutually-recursive `A`↔`B` pair short-circuits at the `count_basic_blocks()>0` re-entry guard instead of looping forever in synthesis (a compile-time stack overflow otherwise). Residual fail-closed leak: a node returned to the caller, whose call-result binding is not a construction site, is not admitted → leaks (tracked caller-side-ownership follow-on), never double-frees. Negative control proven: a NAMED child nested into a parent (`let left = Node(..); let t = Node(left, ..)`) frees exactly once under MallocScribble+libgmalloc (the parent's recursive free owns `left`); 4-leaf tree 19→0, single leaf 3→0, mutual `A`↔`B` chain 0; oracle `indirect_enum_drop_leak_oracle.rs`. #2387 (`048b7fcc9`, 2026-07): when a composite-drop prover excludes an owner through match-bound byte-copy hop attribution, the sibling-discharge compensator must carry the same immediate-parent chain (`alias -> parent field -> owner`) or deliberately keep the leak; never add a sibling drop from owner-only attribution.<br><br>Drop-tranche Stage 3 (2026-07-02, `54ebe8ab8`): the direct-prover exclusion rule consulted `alias_of` (whole-value Move aliasing) but never `field_binders`/`elem_binders` provenance, so `let inner = outer.field; match inner {..}` — the compiler's OWN suggested workaround for projection-scrutinee matches — double-freed the record case (masked by plain `leaks --atExit` reading 0; only Guard-Malloc's `free_cstring` sentinel abort / SIGSEGV exposed it) and leaked the tuple case. No tranche fixture covered the nested-extraction shape (the positive fixture matched the root directly — correct-by-luck). Missed by 7 same-family stage-verifies; caught first-pass by GPT cross-eco. Fixed by provenance-resolving exclusion in both provers + an enum-prover check + 4 regression shapes (red-before/green-after). A second, unrelated instance of the same family (two-level extraction / exclude-every-root blanket rule) was found in the SAME re-hunt at promote time and filed #2375 — the blind spot recurs within one incident, reinforcing that fixture-shape coverage for this row's pattern must be adversarially widened, not just re-verified. |
| `by-value-heap-params-are-borrows` | Considering whether to drop an owned-by-value heap param (`Vec`/record/enum/tuple/`bytes`/`string`) at the CALLEE's scope exit, or attempting to "fix" a value-class leak by inserting a callee-side param drop (`lower_params` → `owned_locals`). | Heap-bearing by-value params in Hew are `IntentKind::Read` **borrows, not moves** — only `#[resource]` args are `Consume` (`arg_move_intent`, `hew-hir/src/lower.rs:4762`); the CALLER retains ownership (the std relies on this: `copy_ints(v)` reads borrowed `v`, caller keeps the buffer). A callee that drops such a param **double-frees the caller's live buffer → UAF**. The value-class leak (`derive_local_collection_drop_allowed` excluding a fresh local once it escapes into a `Read` call because it cannot prove the callee doesn't retain the borrow) is CORRECT caller-side conservatism (worst case = leak, never double-free), NOT a missing callee drop. Closing it is a CALLER-side fix gated on **interprocedural param-escape analysis** (a per-callee "does param K escape: returned / stored in field-or-collection / sent / passed-on as `Consume`?" summary, serialized across separately-compiled modules incl. std) — never a callee-side drop, and there is NO sound callee-side subset (records/enums/`Vec` params are all borrowed identically). VALIDATE drop-safety on the **E2E ratchet** (`make test-hew-ratchet`), NOT unit suites — `cargo nextest -p hew-mir/-codegen-rs/-runtime` were all green while the change double-freed real programs. Any probe matrix MUST include borrow-RETENTION cases (`copy_ints`-shape: read-only param + caller reads after), not just last-use move-ins (which give false-green). | v056 owned-by-value-arg drop-gap (2026-06-16): the discovery's plan (drop params at callee exit via `lower_params`→`owned_locals`) was implemented, passed all 3 unit suites, then the E2E ratchet caught **59 UAF/double-free** failures (sort 27→15 with `PANIC: Vec index out of bounds`, CSV, line-scanner, string-template, vec first/last); minimal repro `dbg_copy_retained.hew` under `MallocScribble=1` printed `0` not `28`. EXIT-CLAUSE reverted, nothing shipped, #1967 resource drop-flag untouched. The caller-side fix needs the interprocedural escape summary (v0.6.0 ownership work), or explicit `consumed`/`borrowed` param annotations (a language/ABI feature). Cousins: `drop-allowset-from-value-flow`, `field-alias-fail-closed`. |
| `inline-collection-param-aliases-by-pointer` | Adding a collection/aggregate VALUE type whose runtime carrier is an INLINE by-value struct (`bytes` = the 16-byte `{ptr,i32,i32}` `BytesTriple`) rather than a heap HANDLE (`Vec` = `*mut HewVec`, `HashMap`, `string`), and deciding how a USER-FUNCTION parameter of that type is passed — OR changing a collection's carrier between heap-handle and inline-value — OR touching the user-fn collection param-passing ABI in codegen `declare_function` / `lower_function`. | A heap-HANDLE collection param shares its backing store under a plain by-value copy FOR FREE — the copied handle still points at the same allocation, so a callee mutation (`b.push`) is visible to the caller. An INLINE-value collection param does NOT: a by-value copy hands the callee its own `{ptr,len}`, so a callee mutation updates a DISCARDED copy and the caller silently sees nothing — no diagnostic, compiles and runs, wrong result (the silent-wrong-code class, inconsistent with `Vec`/`HashMap`/`string` params). To give the inline type the SAME shared-handle semantics, pass it BY POINTER (the address of the caller's carrier) and ALIAS the callee's local slot to the incoming pointer with NO copy-in store, so every `place_pointer(Local(param))` addresses the caller's carrier and push/pop/set write through (a forwarded param passes the same caller address → transitive write-back). Gate aliasing on ALL of: (1) the param is NEVER REASSIGNED in the body — a `var b: bytes; b = ..` lowers to a `Move` into the param local, and aliasing would clobber the caller's slot, so fall back to the by-value copy (no write-back, but no regression vs. today's pass-by-copy); detect reassignment with a FAIL-CLOSED scan over EVERY instruction AND terminator write place (any uncertainty → treat as written → by-copy); (2) `Default` call convention + non-coroutine, so the call site flows through the generic `Terminator::Call` by-pointer branch — actor / lambda / closure / coroutine ABIs deliver the carrier BY VALUE, and aliasing there reinterprets value bits as a pointer. Derive the DECLARED param LLVM type AND the prologue's alias-vs-copy choice from ONE predicate so they can never disagree. Drop-safe precisely because the param is a borrow the callee never frees (`by-value-heap-params-are-borrows`), so the alias can never double-free the caller's buffer. VALIDATE with a callee-mutates-then-caller-OBSERVES behavioural fixture per inline collection type (incl. transitive forwarding); a compiles-and-runs or `.len()`-only check is FALSE-GREEN for the lost-mutation class. | `fix/f2-bytes-byref` (RC1 dogfood F2): `fn fill(b: bytes){ b.push(1) }` mutated a discarded copy — caller's `bytes` unchanged, no warning. `bytes_param_is_aliasable` (codegen `llvm.rs`) gates Default-callconv + non-coroutine + `ResolvedTy::Bytes` + `!hew_mir::local_is_written_in_body`; the never-reassigned `bytes` param is declared `ptr`, its `locals[param]` rebound to the incoming pointer, copy-in skipped. `local_is_written_in_body` (new fail-closed `hew-mir/src/dataflow.rs` helper) scans every instr write (`instr_reads_writes`) + every terminator write place (`terminator_write_places`). Caller side unchanged (the by-pointer arg branch already keys off the declared `ptr` param); `BytesTriple` repr + runtime ABI untouched. Fixtures: callee push visible incl. transitive forward (`Hi! len=3`), parity with Vec under the same shape (`vec_len=1 bytes_len=1`), drop-safe write-back onto a non-empty buffer (`hello world`). Cousins: `by-value-heap-params-are-borrows` (drop-axis sibling — same by-value collection params, opposite concern), `aggregate-abi-by-classifier-not-per-symbol` (a by-pointer ARGUMENT convention is a deliberate correct ABI, not a per-target trap). |
| `borrow-classifier-completeness-or-leak` | An escape scan classifies Vec (or other owned-element collection) receiver-method calls as borrow-vs-escape through an allowlist (e.g. `is_vec_receiver_borrow_symbol`), and a new owned-element operation is added whose runtime symbol is absent from that allowlist. | The receiver-borrow allowlist MUST be exhaustive over the owned-element method surface: every method that does NOT transfer ownership of the collection handle (element clone, element at, element read, length query, etc.) must appear in the allowlist. A missing symbol is classified as an escape → the collection's drop is suppressed at scope exit → LEAK (not a double-free — conservative fail-closed is the correct default, but a leak from a classifier gap is still a defect). **Prove completeness by enumerating the actual MIR callee symbols the lowering can emit, NOT by reading the base `resolve_vec_method` method→symbol table alone.** Many Vec methods have owned-element upgrade overrides: e.g. `.clone()` on a `Vec<owned>` lowers to `hew_vec_clone_owned` (not the base `hew_vec_clone_layout`); the lowering selects the override based on element class, so the base table may list only the layout symbol while the emitted symbol is the `_owned` variant. The classifier must cover BOTH the base symbol AND every `_owned`/`_layout`/`_str` override the lowering can select for the same logical method. Audit procedure: for each method in `resolve_vec_method`, trace every branch of the lowering that calls it and collect the full set of emitted symbols; diff that set against the classifier allowlist — the diff must be empty. Add a unit test that proves: (a) with the entry present, the collection earns a drop; (b) with the entry absent, the collection's drop is suppressed. The test must drive `derive_local_collection_drop_allowed` directly — a behavioural/leak oracle on the compiled binary is NON-EVIDENCE for this layer (the allocator may recycle the leaked handle before the oracle can observe it). | F-01 (`fix/v06-f01-actor-spawn-uaf`, 2026-06-23): the primary fix swapped the escape scan to `derive_local_collection_drop_allowed`; BOTH the GPT cross-eco review and the independent security review found that `hew_vec_clone_owned` (the owned-element upgrade override) was absent from `is_vec_receiver_borrow_symbol` (`hew-mir/src/lower.rs`) while the base clone symbol was present — the owned-upgrade override was emitted by the lowering but invisible to the classifier, so cloning an owned element was classified as an escape, suppressing the Vec's own drop → silent leak on the clone path. Two independent reviewers catching the same gap in the same session is the signal that base-table-only audits are structurally insufficient. Cousins: `drop-allowset-from-value-flow`, `by-value-heap-params-are-borrows`. |
| `move-out-result-contract-or-leak` | A runtime symbol is added (or re-routed to) whose RESULT transfers heap ownership to the caller — a move-out (`pop`/`remove`-class) or clone-out (`get`-class) returning an owned string/blob — and its `callee_ownership_contract` row carries `ResultOwnership::Untracked`. | The result-ownership contract is the RESULT-side twin of the receiver-borrow allowlist: drop elaboration schedules the caller's balancing drop ONLY for tracked result contracts (`FreshOwnedString` seeds `fresh_string_producer_dest`), so an `Untracked` result on an ownership-transferring symbol silently suppresses the moved-out value's drop → per-call LEAK that no unit test, ratchet run, or `cargo test` observes (the value is live-reachable until scope exit; only an at-exit leak oracle sees it). Move-out (sole owner, runtime keeps no copy) and clone-out (+1 owner, runtime keeps its copy) carry the IDENTICAL caller-side contract — the caller owes exactly one drop either way — so a new move-out symbol must copy the existing clone-out getter's contract row, never the scalar sibling's `Untracked` row. Scalar/ptr variants of the same logical method legitimately stay `Untracked` (no heap in the result): the contract is per element class, not per method. | Proving a new move-out/clone-out ABI requires the macOS `leaks --atExit` slope probe (LOW/HIGH frame counts, tolerance ~5 nodes) + the MallocScribble/PreScribble/GuardEdges no-double-free run on an owned-element (`string`) instantiation, in the SAME lane that adds the symbol. Audit: grep the contract table for every `_str`/`_owned` symbol whose runtime moves or clones heap out, and require a tracked result row. | auditE-PR-B (2026-07-08): `hew_vec_pop_str` had shipped with `Untracked` — every `let x = v.pop()` on `Vec<string>` leaked the moved-out string on main, invisible to the full test suite; found only because the new `hew_vec_remove_at_str` (which copied pop's contract) failed the lane's mandatory leak-slope probe (60/60 nodes). Fix: both symbols joined `hew_vec_get_str`'s `FreshOwnedString` arm; slope 0 after. Cousin: `borrow-classifier-completeness-or-leak` (receiver-side twin). |
| `error-count-exit-code` | A new error path emits a diagnostic in C++ codegen or a CLI/doc command. | Whenever you add `emitError` or other diagnostics, increment the owning error counter or propagate failure immediately, then add a reject test where that error fires alone and must exit nonzero. | PR #808/#746. |
| `unit-return-canonical-zero` | Codegen lowers Hew `Unit` to an ABI stand-in such as `i8`, especially for `main` or any function whose result can reach a process exit status. | Emit a canonical zero return value for unit-returning functions instead of loading the MIR return slot. Add or run an executable fixture that has observable stdout and a unit `main`, then assert both output and exit status. | refactor/inprocess-llvm-emission. |
| `mir-assert-implies-verify-hir-gate` | Adding or modifying an `assert!` / `panic!` / `unreachable!` in `hew-mir/src/lower.rs` (or any MIR lowering file) whose precondition depends on HIR shape — binding topology, ownership, actor handle placement, payload-type wiring. | Every MIR lowering assertion encodes an HIR invariant; if `verify_hir` does not enforce that invariant, the assert is a latent panic on user-reachable code. Before landing: (1) identify the HIR invariant the assert assumes; (2) grep `verify_hir` for an existing check that covers it; (3) if absent, add a `verify_hir` check that returns a typed `HirError` for the violating shape, then gate the MIR assert path with `debug_assert!` or remove it in favour of HIR-level rejection. Reviewers must enumerate new MIR asserts in their checklist and verify each has a matching `verify_hir` check. | MIR fuzz crash on link+monitor+spawn at `hew-mir/src/lower.rs:10910` (`build_lifo_drops invariant: binding BindingId(7) is in owned_locals but missing from binding_locals`); root cause at `lower.rs:3730-3732` — `owned_locals.push` was gated by type-class while `binding_locals.insert` was gated by the `Some(src)` arm, creating divergent gates. Fix: `6c92d8bb` (`fix(mir): wire binding_locals atomically with owned_locals for non-BitCopy bindings`). |
| `builtin-enum-variant-mirror-discipline` | Adding a new entry to `builtin_enum_specs()` (synthetic-builtin enum like `SendError`, `LookupError`, `AskError`), OR adding/renaming any variant on such an enum — including choosing a variant name that already exists on another builtin enum. | A new builtin enum's variants live in FOUR coupled places that MUST agree in the same commit: (1) `builtin_enum_specs()` `variant_names` (HIR, `hew-hir/src/lower.rs`); (2) `BUILTIN_ENUM_VARIANT_BARE_NAMES` (HIR pre-pass); (3) the monomorphic registry `BuiltinMonomorphicEnumVariant` list in `hew-types/src/builtin_enums.rs`; (4) the `std/builtins.hew` surface enum. Plus any enum-layout-count test that filters builtins by name (`l.name != "LookupError" && ...`) must add the new enum. Two failure modes: (a) **omission** — a variant missing from `BUILTIN_ENUM_VARIANT_BARE_NAMES` silently overwrites user bare-name entries in `machine_ctor_registry`, `hew check`-clean / `hew run`-rejected; (b) **collision** — a new variant whose bare name DUPLICATES an existing builtin variant (e.g. naming a sentinel `None`, which already belongs to `Option`) makes that bare name ambiguous in the variant registry, so EVERY unqualified use of the existing variant (every `None` in every program) fails `UnresolvedSymbol`. Bare names must be UNIQUE across all builtin enums; pick a non-colliding name (`NoError`, not `None`) and keep the ABI discriminant by POSITION (the runtime↔Hew projection is index-based, so the Hew-surface name may differ from the Rust enum name and can be renamed freely as long as position is preserved). Companion rule: `lower_identifier` bare-name resolution MUST consult `expr_types` (checker authority) before falling through to `UnresolvedSymbol`; on ambiguous-or-missing, fall back to qualified `{type}::{name}`. `mir-assert-implies-verify-hir-gate` cousin — check/run divergence is the smell. | A14 v0.5 audit (2026-05-24): OMISSION mode — `SendError`/`LookupError` specs added without the bare-names mirror (`ee92674c`) → `variant 'Full' struct-literal` + `UnresolvedSymbol "Closed"`; fixes `077bd1e8`/`3ece5ef5`. COLLISION mode: S6 `AskError` (`a9584624`) named its sentinel `None`, colliding with `Option::None` → every `Option`-using program failed `UnresolvedSymbol "None"`; fixed by renaming `None`→`NoError` across all four sites + three layout-test filters, discriminant position preserved. |
| `intrinsic-stub-fail-closed-every-path` | Adding or relying on a bodyless declaration whose body is meant to be skipped or synthesized later — `#[intrinsic]` floor fns, protocol/trait stubs, any "the real body comes from elsewhere" marker — OR adding a new lowering path (module-graph, closure, imported-fn, method) alongside an existing root-item path. | A bodyless stub that is body-skipped or fail-closed on ONE lowering path is fail-OPEN on every path you forgot. Enumerate ALL lowering paths for the construct (root-item, module-graph/imported-fn, closure, method) and confirm each either skips the body the same way or routes through the same fail-closed authority; an unknown/unhandled id MUST become a hard `CodegenError`/`unreachable!`, never a defined empty function returning an uninitialized/zero value. Carry a typed id (not a re-mangled string) from HIR→MIR→codegen so the authority is keyed on a resolved value. Add a regression test that drives the construct through the NON-root path and asserts the unknown-id case fails closed. | W5.005/D343 (2026-05-29): `#[intrinsic]` body-skip existed only on the root-item path (`hew-hir/src/lower.rs:1611-1637`); floor modules always lower via the module-graph path, so `mem.alloc` emitted a defined empty `mem$alloc` returning an uninitialized pointer over raw heap. Fix `45e757f0` (typed `intrinsic_id` HIR→MIR→codegen + central fail-closed `FloorIntrinsic` authority; unknown id → `CodegenError`). Cousin of D341 (match-arm variant of the same fail-open class). |
| `codegen-offset-mirror-drift` | Codegen (or any consumer that must not link the runtime crate) hand-copies a runtime `#[repr(C)]` struct's field byte-offsets as literal constants, OR a runtime struct that has such mirrored offsets is reordered / gains / loses a field. | A hand-copied ABI offset literal silently desyncs the moment the source struct's layout changes (field add/remove/reorder), and the failure is invisible at compile time — generated code loads the wrong field and corrupts memory at runtime. Make the runtime the single source of truth: export each mirrored offset as an `offset_of!`-derived `pub const`, and add a fail-closed parity test that asserts every codegen literal equals the runtime-derived value. The two sides MUST be independent (codegen literal vs `offset_of!` over the real struct) so the test is non-tautological and goes red on drift. Reviewers verify the parity test is independent (not value-compared-to-itself) and spot-run it. Never trust an un-guarded mirrored offset. | Native actor hang (2026-05-29): `4ae3d29a` removed `HewActor.pid`, shifting `state` offset 24→16 and fixing the runtime `offset_of!` asserts + WASM mirror but MISSING codegen's un-guarded literal `HEW_ACTOR_OFFSET_STATE = 24`; handlers then dereferenced `0x8` → SIGSEGV → actor Crashed → `ask` stranded → caller hung forever in `hew_reply_wait` (a hang, not a crash). Fix `17e79075`: `offset_of!`-derived `HEW_ACTOR_OFFSET_*` exports + `abi_offset_parity.rs` parity test. |
| `ffi-abi-width-mirror` | An LLVM `extern` for a runtime C function is declared from the **Hew-facing** type (stdlib catalog `BuiltinTy`, or a user `extern` whose call passes a wider local) rather than the runtime's **true C-ABI integer width**, OR a runtime FFI function's return/param integer width differs from what the catalog declares. | The LLVM `declare` MUST match the runtime function's real C signature, not the Hew type the checker sees. A `-> i32` C function declared `-> i64` reads undefined high bits (the `-1` not-found sentinel surfaces as `4294967295`, so `if idx < 0` guards never fire — silent data corruption); an `i64` argument handed to an `i32`-declared param makes LLVM verification reject the module (hard crash on every call). These are ONE family: reconcile width at the extern call boundary in BOTH directions with **signed** semantics — truncate wide args down to the declared param width, sign-extend narrow results up to the Hew dest width (Hew scalar ints and sentinels are signed; a narrow `-1` must stay `-1`). For catalog shims whose runtime width is narrower than the Hew type, declare the extern at the runtime-true width (a symbol→ABI-width table is the bridge until `BuiltinEntry` carries the width). Loosen any `dest_ty == return_ty` fail-closed call check to reconcile int↔int width while still failing closed on incompatible shapes (int vs struct). Pin exec tests (`hew run`, assert stdout): a not-found sentinel round-trips as `-1` (not a huge unsigned), the corrupting daily-use primitive (split/lines last element) is intact, and the crashing call (from_char) returns the right value. | fix/i32-i64-ffi-width (2026-06-02): `hew_string_find`/`length`/`char_at` return `i32` but the catalog declared them `i64` → `string.split` lost its last elem, `find("zzz")`→`4294967295`, `from_char` crashed (inlining dropped the `code as i32` cast). Fix: `runtime_ffi_{return,param}_abi_bits` tables declare externs at runtime-true width; `reconcile_int_width_signed` truncates args / sign-extends results at the `Call` `FnSymbol::Real` arm. Cousin of `codegen-offset-mirror-drift` and `generated-narrowing-guards`. #2328 (`6c3057055`, 2026-07-02): `to_string_u16`/`to_string_u32` route through the shared runtime symbol `hew_uint_to_string` (`extern "C" fn(u32)`); catalog FFI redeclaration cached the first-processed entry's type, declaring the symbol `(i16) -> ptr` and silently truncating every u32 call site — an O0/O2 differential run caught `to_string(4000000000u32)` printing `10240`. Fixed by declaring `hew_uint_to_string` at its true `i32` param width via the runtime FFI width table and making catalog FFI redeclaration fail closed on a disagreeing cached signature (`ensure_catalog_ffi_signature_matches`). #1884 generalized the single hand-picked redeclaration test into `catalog_ffi_symbols_agree_across_all_shared_symbol_entries`, an exhaustive gate over every shared-symbol catalog group. |
| `codegen-call-matches-callee-arity` | A codegen site emits a `build_call` to a SEPARATELY-emitted generated function (an actor `__init`/`__on_start`/`__on_crash`, a state clone/drop thunk, a wrapper) with a FIXED argument list, while the callee's real signature varies with source shape (an `init` with vs. without parameters, a handler with a varying payload). Especially when a new call site reuses a body pattern proven on the zero-arg case. | A generated call MUST match the callee's ACTUAL parameter count, not an assumed shape — emitting a fixed arg list against a signature that varies with source is wrong-code that `cargo test` (Rust crate) never sees: it surfaces only at LLVM-verify when the compiled `.hew` runs (`Incorrect number of arguments passed to called function`). Before emitting the call, read the callee's real arity (`FunctionValue::count_params`) and branch: call it only in the arity shape you can satisfy, or thread the missing args from their real source. When the missing args come from an as-yet-unthreaded carrier (a SHIM), gate the call on the satisfiable arity and let the existing path (e.g. template-seeding) cover the rest — never call with the wrong count. The proving test is a COMPILED `.hew` exec of the varying shape (the parameterized-`init` actor), not a Rust unit test; pin both the satisfiable shape (runs) and the SHIM shape (compiles + the alternate carrier still initialises correctly). | fix/v06-lifecycle-under-supervision (2026-06-19): the supervised-actor lifecycle wrapper called `__init(ctx)` unconditionally, but an `init(value: i64)` actor's `__init` is `(ctx, i64)` — the supervised `supervised_actor_init_block` fixture (param-bearing `init`) failed LLVM-verify "Incorrect number of arguments passed to called function". The zero-arg showcase passed, hiding it until the param-init fixture ran. Fixed by gating the wrapper's init call on `count_params() == 1` (ctx-only); a parameterized init's fields stay covered by the spawn-arg template seed (the existing SHIM). Cousin of `ffi-abi-width-mirror` (both are call-boundary signature-shape mismatches the Rust suite cannot see). |
| `coroutine-handle-must-be-driven-or-fail-closed` | A codegen call site emits a `build_call` to a generated function that MAY lower as an `llvm.coro` presplitcoroutine ramp (its body can carry a `sleep`/`await`/`Suspend`) — an actor `#[on(start)]`/`init`/`#[on(stop)]` lifecycle hook, a periodic handler, any new call path to a function whose suspendability varies with source. The smell: the call result (the `coro.begin` handle `ptr`) is captured into an SSA name and then ignored, AND the call works for the run-to-completion case so a quick test passes. | A presplitcoroutine ramp RUNS the body only to its first `coro.suspend` and RETURNS the `coro.begin` handle; discarding that handle silently truncates everything after the suspension point (later statements AND state writes), with no error — the worst failure class. A call site to a possibly-suspending generated fn MUST drive the handle, never discard it: poll it (`hew_cont_poll`), and on Ready reclaim the frame (`hew_cont_destroy`) — on Pending PARK it so the scheduler's resume re-entry (`resume_park`/`resume_suspended_activation` via `has_live_parked_cont`) drives it to completion across every suspension, exactly the way the actor dispatch trampoline drives a suspending `receive fn`. The discriminator is the callee's LLVM return type (`ptr` = ramp, traced via `declare_function`'s `is_coroutine_function`→`ptr`-return rule to the MIR `Terminator::Suspend` carrier — NOT a name heuristic). Park ordering mirrors the dispatch suspend edge: RELEASE the actor state lock before parking (a suspended actor holding its lock deadlocks senders — FG2/R2 P0); install the actor's execution context as the current context across the ramp call so a suspend's `hew_actor_self()`-keyed readiness source (the sleep timer) arms against the RIGHT actor; ZERO-init the context carrier so a resumed `cancel_token`/pointer read is null not stack garbage. If the hook genuinely CANNOT be resumed in its context — teardown (`#[on(stop)]` runs after the actor is terminal, no activation to park into) or two sequential coroutines on one actor (suspending `init()` + `#[on(start)]`, only one continuation can park at a time) — FAIL CLOSED at compile with a clear diagnostic, never emit the discard. Cover BOTH the direct-spawn and supervised-restart lifecycle sites, on native AND wasm (the wasm scheduler is a parallel module needing its own `_park_lifecycle_cont` export under `#[cfg_attr(not(test), no_mangle)]` to avoid a native-test symbol clash), and classify any new runtime export in `jit-symbol-classification.toml`. The proving gate is a COMPILED `.hew` exec asserting the post-suspend state (the receive-path / Rust-crate suite is green over the discard — `cargo test` never runs `hew build`'s output); the memory-safety proof is a per-actor leak-slope oracle (frame reclaimed exactly once, flat slope under `MallocScribble`). | fix/v06-on-start-suspension-resume (#2269): `emit_actor_spawn_lifecycle` (`hew-codegen-rs/src/llvm.rs` ~12183) called `__on_start` with a plain `build_call` and discarded the returned coro handle; a `#[on(start)]` with `sleep(50ms)` printed `before`/`0` instead of `before`/`after`/`99` (everything after the sleep, incl. `value=99`, dropped). The receive-fn path worked because the dispatch trampoline (`thunks.rs` `emit_actor_dispatch_trampoline`) already drives its coroutine. Fixed by driving the hook via the trampoline's poll/park pattern + a new `hew_actor_park_lifecycle_cont` (native `scheduler.rs` + wasm `scheduler_wasm.rs`) that parks the lifecycle continuation `Idle→Suspended` so the existing resume re-entry drives it; suspending `#[on(stop)]` and suspending-`init()`-with-`#[on(start)]` fail closed at codegen. Same discard existed for `init()` and the supervised `emit_actor_lifecycle_wrapper`; all fixed in lockstep. Cousin of `codegen-call-matches-callee-arity` and `intrinsic-stub-fail-closed-every-path` (codegen call-boundary defects the Rust suite cannot see). |
| `aggregate-abi-by-classifier-not-per-symbol` | Crossing the C-ABI boundary with an aggregate (struct/tuple/`bytes`/`#[repr(C)]`) larger than a register — declaring how it is returned or passed — OR adding a per-symbol allowlist / hand-encoded register-pair declaration / `_raw` out-pointer twin to make one symbol's aggregate ABI work on one platform. | Per-target aggregate passing is a latent-trap class: SysV/AAPCS return a ≤16-byte aggregate in a register pair while Windows x64 MSVC returns EVERY non-{1,2,4,8}-byte aggregate indirectly via a hidden `sret` pointer, and a hand-encoded `{i64,i64}`/`[2 x i64]` declaration that dodges LLVM's own ABI logic on one platform miscompiles on the other (the trap-206 / `_raw`-family origin). The divergence is NOT only over-threshold: LLVM lowers a bare multi-field struct return per-FIELD (one register each) while the C ABI packs per-EIGHTBYTE, so an 8-byte `{i32,i32}` or a 16-byte `{i64,i32,i32}` bare-struct return silently corrupts every field after the first eightbyte boundary even though it is 'under the sret threshold'. Classify the aggregate ONCE keyed on `(LLVM struct type, target triple)` and attach the matching LLVM attribute (`sret(T)`+`noalias` on indirect returns, `byval(T)` on indirect args) so LLVM's target lowering does the work — never a per-symbol allowlist, a hand-picked register-pair return, or a duplicate `_raw` void+out-pointer symbol. The classifier MUST fail closed on an unmodelled target (never guess an ABI). The declared carrier and the emitted attribute MUST always agree (declaring the field-accurate struct WITHOUT a matching attribute is what let LLVM pick indirect-sret while the caller read a register pair → trap 206). The host (SysV/AAPCS register-pair) CANNOT prove the MSVC sret path — gate any `_raw`-deletion on the Windows leg; the host run-parity green is non-evidence for the indirect class. The module must declare its target triple even at in-process emission time (no machine), or the classifier reads an empty triple and fails closed on the host. NOTE the asymmetry: a `_raw` RETURN twin IS a real MSVC-sret workaround the classifier replaces; a by-pointer ARGUMENT convention (`*const BytesTriple` borrow) is NOT — a plain pointer has no per-target ambiguity, so the by-pointer / struct-expansion arg allowlists encode deliberate correct ABIs, not latent traps, and stay as the fail-closed gate for unknown `bytes`-arg externs. | feat/v06-r5-sret-byval: replaced the hand-encoded `hew_supervisor_child_get` `{i64,i64}` return + the `_raw` out-pointer twins for `hew_supervisor_child_get`/`hew_bytes_slice`/`hew_read_slot_take` with `classify_aggregate(struct_ty, &TargetData, triple)` (`abi_class.rs`) → `[2 x i64]` register-pair on SysV/AAPCS, `sret(T)` on MSVC. Verified on aarch64-darwin: trap-206 supervisor-child-after-restart fixture exits 7, bytes_slice (non-zero offsets) + read-deadline fixtures keep exact exit+stdout. fix/extern-sret-returns (#2399): wired the classifier into the GENERIC user-extern path (`classify_extern_record_return` + `ExternRecordRet` on `FnSymbol::Real`, `llvm.rs`) — previously only 3 hardcoded runtime symbols were classified and every user `extern "C"` record return got a bare `fn_type_for_return` struct (over-16-byte: sret never attached, caller left x8 unset, callee faulted; 8/16-byte multi-field-per-eightbyte: fields after the first eightbyte read garbage). The recordret probe matrix (tests/pkg-import/recordret_*.hew, distinct non-zero sentinels per field) proved 4 of 6 classes red on main and pins all 6 green: sret + hidden-pointer arg-index shift (big_mixed), [2 x i64] and coerced-iN carriers, Natural single-field control. Float/SIMD-bearing records, wasm32 record returns, and sub-eightbyte-tail RegisterPairs fail closed; `.real()` consumers reject sret externs loudly. Cousins: `ffi-abi-width-mirror`, `codegen-offset-mirror-drift`, `codegen-call-matches-callee-arity` (all call-boundary ABI-shape mismatches the Rust suite cannot see). |
| `builtin-discriminator-survives-source-shadow` | A builtin type whose real identity is the compiler `BuiltinType` discriminator ALSO has a source `type X {}` carrier decl (stdlib zero-field types like `Stream`/`Sink`/`Duplex`/`Vec`/`HashMap`), AND the checker's bare-name resolution chooses source-decl binding vs builtin form. Also fires when a checker-registered builtin constructor (no AST `fn` item) must be callable from compiled source. | The builtin discriminator (`Ty::Named.builtin`) is the load-bearing payload that survives checker→HIR→MIR; the MIR boundary (`push_unknown_type_diagnostics`) recognises substrate handles ONLY by `builtin.is_some()`. A local source `type X {}` decl that shadows a builtin must NOT strip the discriminator for the families whose identity IS the builtin — gate the source-decl-wins branch on a SEMANTIC predicate (`is_collection() \|\| is_substrate_handle()`), never an ad-hoc name list that silently omits a sibling family (omitting `Stream`/`Sink`/`Duplex` shipped `builtin: None`, and the type only failed at the MIR boundary as `unknown type Sink`, never at the checker). Do NOT seed a constructor whose runtime/MIR producer does not exist (pretend-support that passes verify but fails closed at MIR). Pin the discriminator with a probe at the consuming boundary, and the constructor with a `verify_hir`-INVOKING test (a `lower_program`-only test hides the seam). | feat/stream-duplex-surface-lowering (2026-06-02): `local_source_type_def` excluded only `Vec`/`HashMap`/`HashSet`, so the stdlib `type Sink<T>{}`/`type Stream<T>{}` carrier decls stripped `builtin` from `pipe`'s return type → `pipe(16)+send/recv` failed `E_MIR: unknown type Sink` while sibling occurrences carried `builtin: Some(_)`. | `unclonable-leaf-fails-closed-transitively` | An actor-state clone / drop / layout-witness decision is being made for a type that may TRANSITIVELY contain a leaf with no clone-dup helper (an `#[opaque]` runtime handle — `json.Value`, `cron.Expr`; the same shape applies to any future no-dup leaf). The leaf may sit directly in the field, inside a generic container type-arg (`Vec<T>`/`Option<T>`/`Result<T,E>`/`HashMap<K,V>`/`HashSet<T>`), inside a record field, inside an enum-variant payload, or nested arbitrarily. | A no-clone-dup leaf must fail the WHOLE containing composite closed through ONE transitive authority consulted at EVERY clone/witness seam — never a per-shape patch. A managed-collection clone (`hew_vec_clone_managed`) or a `plain` element layout-witness selected for a container REGARDLESS of element identity will shallow-copy the leaf's pointer and double-free / UAF on supervisor restart, even though the bare-field case already fails closed. Per-shape fixes are fail-OPEN: each new container/nesting the enumeration forgot reopens the UAF under a new shape (the bare-opaque, enum-payload, and generic-container holes were three successive rounds of the SAME bug). The enum-payload case stays covered by the tag-aware clone TRAP (a `Result<opaque,E>`/`Option<opaque>` actor-state field compiles but its synthesized enum-clone helper traps at restart) — the container authority and the enum trap together cover all shapes; pin a `Vec<opaque>`→fail-closed test, a `Result<opaque,E>`→trap-in-emitted-IR test, AND a `Vec<non-opaque record>`→compiles negative control (the check keys on the per-reference identity discriminator, never container shape, so legitimate owned-element containers are unaffected). | Opaque-type-identity clone seam, 2026-06-04 (three successive rounds of the SAME bug, each a forgotten shape): bare `#[opaque]` field; `Vec<json.Value>` actor state shallow-copied via `hew_vec_clone_managed` (double-free on restart) because the layout witness ignored element kind; enum-payload (`Result<json.Value,E>`). Cousin of `drop-allowset-from-value-flow` and `container-abi-ctor-op-agreement`. |
| `no-live-borrow-across-opaque-callback` | A runtime FFI function (`hew_rc_drop`/`hew_arc_drop`/any `hew_*` entry that owns a header before the payload) holds a live `&mut`/`&` reference INTO an allocation across a call to an opaque caller-supplied callback (a `drop_fn`/destructor/visitor `extern "C" fn`), OR reads more header fields AFTER such a call through the same reference. | The callback is opaque and may reach back into the SAME allocation (read or write), so any reference into that allocation held live across the call aliases the callback's access — undefined behaviour under both Stacked and Tree Borrows, latent until a non-null callback that touches the allocation is wired. Before the opaque call: snapshot EVERY header field the post-call path needs (`drop_fn`, `weak`, `data_size`, `data_align`, …) into locals inside a scoped block, END the `&mut`/`&` borrow (let the reference go out of scope), THEN call the callback and do all post-call bookkeeping (destructor, dealloc) using ONLY the locals and the raw pointer — never re-borrow the header across or after the call. The sibling Arc/Rc/weak entries share this shape; audit each (`arc.rs` had the identical pattern).
