PROVE it under Miri with a fixture whose callback READS and WRITES the same allocation (a no-op callback cannot witness the bug); the honest negative control is the pre-fix body, which is UB at the post-call field read under both borrow models — a leak-floor or behavioural-green test is NON-EVIDENCE (the aliasing UB executes correctly under a real allocator). | FND-01 (`fix/v06-fnd01-rc-drop-aliasing`): `hew_rc_drop` held `let inner = &mut *header` live across `drop_fn(ptr)` and across the subsequent `inner.weak`/`inner.data_size`/`inner.data_align` reads; a non-null Rc `drop_fn` reaching the allocation (the owned-state trigger) makes that aliasing UB. Fixed by snapshotting `(strong, drop_fn, weak, data_size, data_align)` into locals in a scoped block that ends the borrow before `drop_fn`, then running drop+dealloc from the locals + raw `header`. Proved with a write-aliasing `drop_reads_self` fixture: UB on the old body under both Stacked Borrows (`tag does not exist in the borrow stack` at the `weak` offset) and Tree Borrows (`state Disabled ... foreign write access`), clean under both on the fix; `cargo +nightly miri test rc::tests` green (12/12). Cousin of `drop-allowset-from-value-flow` and `by-value-heap-params-are-borrows`. |
| `recursive-admission-needs-indirection-witness` | Relaxing a type-admission gate (RcFree / collection-element / drop-derivation) to admit a recursive user type, OR adding a structural marker/heap-ownership walk over a type graph that can be self-recursive. | A recursive type is representable ONLY when a heap indirection breaks the value-size cycle: admit a cycle whose back-edge passes through a `Vec`/`HashMap`/`HashSet` (or other heap-allocated) field (`enum R { A(Vec<R>) }` — finite value size, drop terminates at the heap buffer); STILL REJECT a direct value back-edge (`enum E { V(E) }` — infinite size). The admit/reject test is whether the recursive back-edge is reached through a heap-indirecting builtin's type args (admit, the indirection is the witness) vs a direct value member (reject). Pin BOTH directions as tests — the negative (`enum E { V(E) }` rejects) is load-bearing: over-admitting pushes an infinite-size value type to codegen → unbounded layout recursion / stack overflow. SEPARATELY, ANY structural recursion over a type graph that the relaxed gate now admits MUST carry a visited-set (or depth bound) guard: a marker-derivation / heap-ownership / clone-classification walk with no guard diverges (stack overflow) the moment it meets a `Vec<Self>`-bearing type — and the overflow fires at `hew check`, not run. **The guard's key must NOT grow with the walk.** A walk that recurses THROUGH generic substitution (instantiating each level's fields with the parent's type args) and keys its visited-set on the substituted `(name, args)` pair is still fail-OPEN: a diverging polymorphic self-reference — `Wrap<T> { w: Wrap<Wrap<T>> }` — substitutes to a strictly LARGER arg vector at every level (`Wrap<i64>` → `Wrap<Wrap<i64>>` → …), so the `(name, args)` key never collides and the walk expands without bound (heap OOM, not a stack overflow). Key the bound on a NON-growing discriminator instead — the bare type NAME on the active expansion path (record the type→type edge before descending, then skip re-descent into a name already active, since its outgoing edges are already owned by the outer frame), or a hard depth bound. Keep the admission gate fail-closed for any admitted-but-not-yet-lowerable shape (e.g. a recursive enum whose nested owned-Vec field clone/drop synthesis does not exist yet): admit at the boundary ONLY what the full lowering pipeline can handle, or keep it rejected with a clear diagnostic (never a codegen-front error or overflow). | W5.016 F4 (2026-06-02): `implements_rc_free` admits an indirection-broken cycle (a `Recursive(name)` back-edge through a `Vec`/`HashMap`/`HashSet` arm) but the general `Named` walk keeps a direct value back-edge rejected. `implements_marker` gained a visited-set (`implements_marker_guarded`) — before it, a `Vec<Self>`-bearing enum overflowed the stack deriving Copy. `Vec<RedisReply>` stayed fail-closed at the owned-element gate (recursive enum-clone synthesis is a follow-on). Both directions pinned: admits Vec-indirected recursion, rejects direct value cycle, marker derivation terminates. v0.5.3 F5 (`94311e6e`/`49c61c62`): TWO sibling holes in the same family. (1) The HIR layout occurs-check over-REJECTED finite concrete nesting — any field naming the origin record with type args `!=` the current instantiation was refused, so `Box<Box<i64>>` (shrinking args) failed `RecursiveGenericTypeUnsupported`; narrowed to reject only when a current-arg appears as a strict subterm of an occurrence arg (args GROWING = diverging). (2) The value-type cycle detector (`hew-types/src/cycle.rs::detect_recursive_value_type_cycles`) keyed its expansion visited-set on `(name, args)` and OOM'd on `Wrap<Wrap<T>>` (8 GB+ RSS on a 3-line program) — bounded by an active-name set so the detector terminates and rejects `Wrap` as infinitely sized. |

### `checker-authority` — checker output is authoritative, downstream consumes, no re-inference

- **area**: typecheck, enrichment, serialization, codegen
- **invariant**: Whatever the checker resolves — receivers, types, generics, visibility, assignment targets, ABI choices, pattern legality — must survive the boundary into serialization and codegen. Downstream phases consume those facts; they do not rediscover them by AST fallback or span-keyed lookup.
- **why**: Re-inference at codegen time is racy with checker order and stale across function scopes, and span-keyed lookups can be absent or contradict metadata the lowering pass already tracked. Once an authority loses its monopoly, two phases disagree and silently produce wrong code.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `type-info-survival` | A later phase is tempted to re-infer receiver, type, visibility, or stdlib catalog facts that the checker already resolved; OR the checker's side-table producer is recorded at only SOME of the syntactic sites a downstream phase consumes (e.g. records inferred calls but skips the explicit-turbofish form). | Thread inferred call args, receiver authority, `Self` generics, visibility, module-aware names, and catalog-driven resolution through side tables or serialization; seed both HIR and the checker from the catalog, and fail if a downstream phase cannot see the authoritative answer. The producer must record at EVERY site the consumer reads — a per-site recording gate keyed on surface syntax (turbofish-vs-inferred) is fail-open: the skipped site starves the pipeline and trips the downstream NYI/unresolved arm, while the recorded site works, so the bug looks like a missing downstream feature when it is really a missing producer entry. The fix is to widen the producer (records unconditionally, fail-closed at the value boundary on residual inference vars), never to re-infer downstream. 'At the value boundary' means the `check_program` OUTPUT boundary, AFTER inference fully settles — NOT a guard inside the `synthesize`-time recorder: a return-type-polymorphic call (`Stack::new()` / `new_stack<T>()`, whose `T` is fixed by the expected return type) binds its type params only AFTER `synthesize` returns, when `check_against`/`expect_type` unifies the annotation, so a record-time 'all args concrete' guard is itself fail-OPEN — it drops the entry while `T` is still `Ty::Var` and re-trips the NYI arm, even though argument-driven and turbofish forms (concrete by record time) work. Snapshot the substitution representative unconditionally and let the output boundary re-resolve + prune (`validate_call_type_args_output_contract`), exactly as the record-init surface already does. Before believing a "downstream lowering is unimplemented" report, check whether the inferred-arg control already works end-to-end — if it does, the gap is the recording gate, not the lowering arm. | PR #814/#806; stdlib-resolution slice 5. F4 turbofish generic-call (2026-06-14): both generic-call application sites in `hew-types/src/check/calls.rs` passed `type_args.is_none()` as the `call_type_args` record flag, so an explicit `id<i64>(5)` was never recorded and MIR fell through to "function call NYI" — while `let y: i64 = id(5)` compiled and ran. Fixed by recording at every generic call site (`true`); the existing `record_concrete_call_type_args` inference-var guard keeps the boundary fail-closed. The report framed it as "generic call lowering not implemented, the largest item"; the inferred control proved the MIR arm already worked. F7 return-type-poly generic ctors (feat/f7-generic-ctor, 2026-06-29): the very `record_concrete_call_type_args` inference-var guard F4 trusted as 'fail-closed at the boundary' was fail-OPEN for return-type-polymorphic calls — it ran inside `synthesize`, before `check_against` unified the expected return type, so `Stack::new()` / `new_stack()` dropped their still-`Ty::Var` `T` and hit the function-call NYI while argument-driven (`singleton(99)`) and turbofish (`Stack::<i64>::new()`) worked. Fixed by making the recorder defer/snapshot unconditionally (matching `record_concrete_record_init_type_args`), relocating the residual-inference-var prune to the `check_program` output boundary. |
| `checker-output-boundary` | A checker-owned type or metadata table is about to cross into serialization or codegen. | Reject or strip unresolved signature, type-def, and expr-type entries in `check_program`, emit the boundary diagnostic there, and make serialize/codegen consume checker-authoritative metadata instead of re-inferring from AST fallbacks. A `synthesize`/`synthesize_inner` arm that early-`return`s MUST still flow through `record_type(span, &ty)` — otherwise the span gets no `expr_types` entry, the boundary resolve has nothing to finalize, and a downstream AST fallback fabricates a bare type (e.g. builtin `None` → bare `Option` → codegen D10). | PR #838/#848/#849/#852/#853/#1721; W4.042 (builtin `None` checker record). |
| `target-constant-from-threaded-arch-not-host-cfg` | A MIR/codegen value depends on the COMPILE TARGET (pointer width, ABI width, signed-MIN/-1 trap constant, shift-range bound, enum tag width) and is computed from `cfg!(target_pointer_width)`/`#[cfg(target_arch=…)]` on the COMPILER HOST, OR a classification helper returns `None`/fail-closed for a platform-sized type (`isize`/`usize`) "because the width is not knowable here". | The constant MUST derive from the target threaded through the pipeline (the checker's `wasm_target`/`pointer_width`, HIR's `TargetArch`, a MIR `PointerWidth` field on the Builder), NEVER a host `cfg!`: a cross-compile (`--target wasm32` on a 64-bit host) computing the host width emits a width-64 shift bound / `i64::MIN` guard into a 32-bit module → out-of-range shifts silently admitted and the wrong signed-MIN trap = a fail-OPEN soundness hole, invisible to a host build/test. Thread the target fact (free helpers take a width param sourced from the checker/Builder; the per-fn Builder carries `pointer_width`, child builders inherit it via the shared-tables helper, and EVERY construction site is audited — a `..Default()` site silently defaults). Pin a cross-target parity test that lowers the SAME source for both widths and asserts the 32-bit module emits the width-32 bound and `i32::MIN` and NOT 64/`i64::MIN` (a host-width leak); the native vertical-slice proves width-64 (`1<<64` traps, `1<<63` does not). And: when a downstream HIR/MIR gate fail-closes a platform-sized op as "not lowerable until target-width is threaded", that gate is usually ALREADY DEAD CODE — the checker's integer-classification helper rejected the operand first because `is_integer()` admitted `isize`/`usize` while `integer_type_info` returned `None` (a fail-open/late-reject inconsistency); fix the upstream classification (add the platform arm, threaded width), then the downstream gate becomes reachable-but-correct and gets deleted. Platform-sized types combine only with themselves + `IntLiteral`; do NOT let a same-width fixed type (`isize` vs `i64` both 64-bit) fall into the wider-type rule, or `isize op i64` is wrongly admitted. | W60.040 platform-int-arith (2026-06-17): `isize`/`usize` `+ - * / % << >> & | ^` and comparisons all rejected at the checker (`common_integer_type`→`integer_type_info` `None`), while the NYI audit located the surface at the HIR `PlatformSized{DivRem,Shift}` gates — which were dead code (checker rejected first). Fixed by threading the target pointer width (32 on wasm32, 64 native; checker `wasm_target` and a MIR `PointerWidth` field), adding the platform arms to the four checker helpers + MIR `integer_bit_width`/`signed_min_value`, then deleting the now-reachable HIR gates. codegen `primitive_to_llvm` still lowers `isize`→i32/i64 via host `#[cfg(target_pointer_width)]` (a marked SHIM, sound because host==target on the native path); the MIR guard width MUST match that LLVM width per target. |
| `assignment-target-authority` | Codegen assignment lowering is tempted to rediscover field/index target validity after the checker already classified the target. | Keep checker-owned assignment kind/shape data authoritative, turn impossible field-lowering fallbacks into fail-closed invariant diagnostics, and add regression tests by mutating typed AST metadata directly instead of re-testing the frontend path. | fix/field-assign-codegen-invariant. |
| `module-qualified-rewrite-authority` | An imported stdlib module call can be rewritten directly to a runtime C symbol. | Record direct-call rewrite metadata during `check_method_call`, consume it in `enrich_method_call` before any registry fallback, and test that the rewrite preserves the original argument list without receiver injection. | JOURNEY 2026-04-10 module-qualified stdlib rewrite metadata lane. |
| `stdlib-wrapper-collapse-extern-only` | The stdlib loader collapses a `pub fn` wrapper onto its single inner callee (`clean_names`) so `module.fn` rewrites straight to that callee — gated only on arity. | A wrapper may only collapse onto its inner callee when the callee is a declared **extern C symbol** (exists at link time). A `pub fn encode(s) { encode_impl(s) }` forwarding to a private same-module **Hew** helper must map to ITSELF (identity), so the wrapper is compiled and called by its qualified `module$fn` name; collapsing to the private helper's bare name yields a callee the importer cannot resolve (`IndirectCallUnsupported` / `resolved HIR contains an unresolved binding reference` at the call site, while sibling extern-forwarding wrappers like `url.parse → hew_url_parse` resolve fine). Pre-collect the extern-block fn names and gate the collapse on membership. | fix/net-trait-wrapper-lowering (2026-06-04): `url.encode`/`decode`/`encode_query` (each forwarding to a private `_impl` helper) failed on import; sibling `url.parse` (extern) did not — the asymmetry is the tell. |
| `codegen-import-path-consistency` | A new codegen pass, pre-registration table, or lookup map handles imported items. | Audit every name-keyed codegen table for imported-item lookups, swap to defining-module paths where required, and add focused regressions for each independent pass that builds or consumes such tables. Specifically: MIR keys monomorphic enum/machine layouts by the bare HIR `decl.name`, but a `Place` at an importer carries the module-qualified `ResolvedTy::Named` (`fs.IoError`) — every type-derived `machine_layouts.get(name)` site must mirror the generic-enum branch's `short_name` fallback or it fails closed (`E_NOT_YET_IMPLEMENTED: machine fs.IoError ... not in IrPipeline.machine_layouts`). The honest proof emits `.o`/runs, not just `hew check`. | PR #386. fix/fs-ioerror-importer-codegen (2026-06-04): `machine_layout_for_local`'s monomorphic (`args.is_empty()`) branch used the qualified name verbatim with no fallback while the generic branch already stripped it; constructing/matching imported `fs.IoError`/`json.ParseError` round-trips after the fix. |
| `per-module-type-identity` | A type/method registry, duplicate gate, or name-resolution arm keys a user/std `pub type` or `pub actor` (or its `Type::method` / receive-fn sig) by **bare name** against a single global map. | A `pub type`'s identity is `(defining-module, name)`, not bare `name`: scope the duplicate-definition gate to the current module (root/flat = `None`), so two modules may each declare a same-named type while a second declaration *within one module* still errors. Builtins stay global. Resolve a bare reference local-first; a bare name exported by 2+ imported modules is a typed `AmbiguousType` error (never silent first-wins). Critically, `fn_sigs["Type::method"]` and `TypeDef.methods` are also last-write-wins across modules — an impl body must read its return type from the module-local qualified type def (`{short}.Type`), not the bare key, or one module's `impl Trait for T` silently clobbers another's (witnessed: websocket+http both `impl ServerMethods for Server` → `expected Request, found Conn` inside websocket). The collision can be silent when the colliding sigs happen to coincide (json/toml/yaml `Value` methods all return primitives) — assert qualified resolution binds to the right def, do not trust a clean check. Shortening a module qualifier is sound for LAYOUT-KEY agreement (find the bare-registered layout) but UNSOUND for IDENTITY comparison: a `strip-known-module-prefix-then-compare-bare` canonicalization is fail-OPEN — it collapses two distinct modules' same-bare-name types (`closableerr.CloseError` vs `closableerr2.CloseError`) into one and ACCEPTS a wrong-module impl, deferring to a later codegen-front failure instead of rejecting at the type boundary. Compare DEFINING-MODULE identity (qualify a bare trait-side name against the trait's owner module via its `{module}.Trait` registry alias); never strip-then-compare-bare. The trait-side canonicalization must be SIDE-SPECIFIC: a bare name in the TRAIT DECLARATION always qualifies to the trait owner (the importer's local type names cannot change what the trait requires), while a local-shadow carve-out (keep the bare name so a local type correctly mismatches) applies ONLY to the IMPL/actual side. A SHARED local-shadow filter over both sides is itself fail-OPEN: when the importer has a local `CloseError`, it leaves the trait side's bare `CloseError` bare too, so it compares EQUAL to the impl's local type instead of the owner's required `closableerr.CloseError`, falsely accepting a wrong-module impl. And ambiguity is decided over PUBLISHED bare bindings, not over every module that EXPORTS the name: a plain `import` that exported but did not opt the name in must not contribute, or it poisons an explicit named import of the same bare name. A bare ref published by exactly one module binds to that owner's QUALIFIED identity so a sibling exporting the same bare name cannot collapse them downstream; the same fail-closed gate guards the bare record CONSTRUCTOR, not only type positions. For ALIASED imports (`import m::{ T as U }`) the published-bare map must carry SOURCE identity (`binding U -> owner.OriginalName m.T`), never reconstruct `m.U` from the binding name — reconstruction either fails closed or binds the wrong nominal type when `m` also exports a real `U`; and named-import opt-in matches by SOURCE NAME only (the alias affects only the binding, never which source export the spec selects), or a distinct export literally named `U` is falsely opted in under `U`. A SUPERTRAIT edge has a DIFFERENT resolution scope than a primary trait reference: `Base` in `trait Sub: Base` is spelled in `Sub`'s DECLARING module, so it must resolve through THAT module's import bindings (the re-export chain to the original owner), never the final importer's same-name trait — and never the local-shadow step (a declaring-module super is never the importer's local trait). When the declaring module RE-IMPORTED its super (`import other::{ Base }; trait Sub: Base`), there is no same-module `{declaring}.Base` def, so a `{declaring}.Base`-only qualifier falls back to the bare name and binds whatever `Base` the importer has — a collision-unsafe fail-OPEN that accepts a wrong-signature inherited method. Record each module's own trait imports in a `(declaring_module, binding) -> {owner}.Source` table (aliases included: `B -> other.Base`) and resolve the super edge through it; self-register the module's own pub traits so a chain terminates at the origin. Route EVERY trait reference (primary, bound, supertrait edge) through ONE resolver scoped Current-vs-Declaring, so identity is keyed by owner not bare spelling; an unresolved super then fails CLOSED against an absent method set, never accept-all. Stdlib obeys the same qualified-by-default gate — a plain `import std::…` does not expose a type bare; only genuine prelude bootstrap surfaces (always-in-scope, no user import) publish bare. The owner-qualified key must also flow to the IMPL-SIDE associated-type / default-method machinery, NOT only the conformance method-set check: the required-associated-type ENFORCEMENT, the default-associated-type collection, and the default-method registration each read `trait_defs` for the impl's `trait_bound` — keying those on the bare `tb.name` lets a same-name trait imported by a DIFFERENT module overwrite the global bare `trait_defs[name]` (last-write-wins, HashMap-order-dependent) so an impl that omits a required `type` is ACCEPTED whenever the empty same-named trait wins the write. Route them through the conformance resolver (`resolve_trait_conformance_identity` → `trait_defs_key_for_identity`, exposed as `trait_defs_key_for_bound`). EXCEPTION — the projection-binding POPULATION (`impl_assoc_type_bindings`) must STAY on the bound spelling: its `(target, trait, assoc)` key and the carrier `trait_name` that `substitute_trait_sig_for_impl` / `project_assoc_types` build are all keyed on the bound AS WRITTEN, so re-keying its `trait_defs` read on the owner-qualified identity makes the lookup SUCCEED for an aliased bound where the bare alias has no entry, writing a binding that was previously absent and firing the projection collapse asymmetrically (trait side collapses to the concrete assoc, impl side written `Self::Item` does not) — a false signature-mismatch on a sound impl. The `dyn`-trait subsystem (`apply_trait_object_bound_substitutions`, `validate_dyn_trait_bound`, the vtable-slot lookup, `actor_satisfies_handler_trait`, the dyn assoc-binding-completeness check) is internally consistent on the BARE trait name across BOTH its write side (`record_trait_impl` keys `trait_impls_set` on bare `tb.name`) and read side, so routing one member in isolation desyncs it — owner-qualifying the dyn family means moving its WRITE keys together, a separate reshape; the family probed sound under same-name + swapped-method-order collisions (verified by `hew run`, correct vtable slot). | W5.018 per-module-type-namespace (R313): cleared Conn/Value/Server/Message/ParseError/StreamPair std collisions; witnessed websocket+http both `impl ServerMethods for Server` → `expected Request, found Conn`. feat/v050-qualified-actor-identity (2026-06-10): closed the ACTOR instance end-to-end — checker tables dotted-primary (dotted key AUTHORED, never copied from the bare winner), spawn/ask identity is the `LocalPid<module.Actor>` inner name, bare refs resolve local-first with typed `AmbiguousActorReference`, every native symbol through one `$`-mangle authority (root actors stay bare = zero ABI churn). Latent residual RESOLVED (PR #1880): the downstream HIR `type_classes`/`record_registry` + MIR/codegen `short_name` fallbacks that left distinct same-name imported types aliasing are closed — module-qualified type-args normalize through ONE enforced layout-key shortening authority per crate (`hew_hir::shorten_named_arg_qualifiers` → `mangle_with_shortened_args` / `mangle_layout_key` / `find_enum_layout`), applied at every producer registration AND consumer lookup, with self-scan structural guards (model.rs whole-file + llvm.rs `resolve_ty`-scoped) that fail CI if a future caller reintroduces a raw-args layout key. PATTERN (specialization of `codegen-import-path-consistency`): when a name-qualifier carrier flows into pre-existing bare-keyed registries, enforce ONE shortening authority + a self-scan guard, and prove it with the COMPILED `.hew` ratchet — a static site-sweep missed layout-key sites across 5 review rounds; the dynamic 0/0 ratchet + the guard were the convergence. feat/c2-import-surface (2026-06-14, C2 soundness): fixed a fail-OPEN strip-then-compare-bare in the trait-sig comparison (cross-module same-bare-name impl now rejected with `TraitImplSignatureMismatch`, not codegen-front); moved use-time ambiguity to PUBLISHED-bare bindings (plain import no longer poisons a named opt-in); bound published bare names to their owner's qualified identity at both type position AND the bare record constructor; closed the stdlib bare-publication bypass. 3rd revision (cross-eco re-review, ALIASED-import soundness): made the trait-sig local-shadow carve-out SIDE-SPECIFIC (`preserve_local_shadow` per side — a local `CloseError` now correctly mismatches the trait's `closableerr.CloseError` instead of being conflated, closing the shared-filter fail-open); made the published-bare map carry SOURCE identity (`U -> m.T`) so an aliased opt-in binds the real source type, not a phantom `m.U`; matched named imports by SOURCE NAME so a distinct same-named export is not falsely opted in under the alias. Oracles: `cross_module_trait_sig_reject`, `local_shadow_trait_sig_reject`, `published_bare_no_poison` / `_two_optin_ambiguous` / `_two_plain_rejected` (pkg-import); `alias_import_resolves_bare_binding_to_source_identity` / `alias_import_does_not_conflate_with_same_named_export` (checker unit). KNOWN FOLLOW-UP (separate HIR-lowering layer, same as the `bd2d1810` layout-key hardening): an aliased `StructInit` (`Tag { … }` from `Payload as Tag`) still reaches HIR lowering keyed on the bare binding name, not the checker-resolved source identity, so end-to-end construction through an alias is unresolved until the record/variant registry carries alias bindings — the resolver/checker half is sound and proven at unit level. C2 unified resolver (2026-06-15, re-exported supertrait edge): closed the RE-EXPORTED supertrait fail-open — a supertrait reached via the declaring module's OWN import (`import other::{ Base }; trait Sub: Base`) had no same-module `{declaring}.Base` def, so the edge qualifier fell back to the bare name and bound whatever `Base` the FINAL importer had in scope, accepting a wrong-signature inline supermethod. Collapsed the per-reference patchwork onto ONE `resolve_trait_ref(name, scope)` (Current for primary/bound, Declaring for super edges); `resolve_trait_conformance_identity` is now a thin Current shim, `resolve_super_trait_edge` replaces the bare-fallback `qualify_super_trait_edge` with Declaring-scope resolution + no bare fallback, and the duplicated qualified-key derivation collapsed onto `trait_defs_key_for_identity`. New `trait_import_bindings` table records each module's own trait imports (aliases included) — NOTE the importer-keyed `published_bare_trait_owners` does NOT hold the declaring module's binding (it is keyed by the root importer's `current_module`, verified `None` for `(reexsub, Base)` by probe), so the declaring-scope table is genuinely required, not derivable from the published map. Oracles (pkg-import, all 10x-deterministic where collisions exist): `reexport_super_inline_supermethod_accept` / `_aliased_super_inline_supermethod_accept` / `_chain_inline_supermethods_accept` (accept direct/aliased/two-hop), `reexport_super_wrong_collision_reject` / `_aliased_super_wrong_sig_reject` / `_chain_intermediate_wrong_sig_reject` / `_deep_chain_base_wrong_sig_reject` (reject at each chain level). C2 impl-side associated-type path (2026-06-15): closed the H12 fail-OPEN — the required-associated-type enforcement (`enter_impl_scope`), the default-associated-type collection (`build_impl_alias_entries`), and the default-method registration all read the impl `trait_bound` from the bare `trait_defs[tb.name]`; two non-root modules importing different same-named `Source` traits (one with `type Item`, one empty) let the empty one overwrite the global bare entry, so an `impl Source for W` omitting `type Item` was ACCEPTED on most HashMap orderings (verified order-dependent: ~8/10 accept pre-fix, BOTH import orders). Routed the three through `trait_defs_key_for_bound` (= `resolve_trait_conformance_identity` → `trait_defs_key_for_identity`); now rejects deterministically. The projection-binding population was deliberately LEFT bare (routing it regressed a sound aliased-projection impl — the asymmetric-collapse exception above). The `dyn` family was left bare + documented (sound, isolation-route unsafe). Oracles (pkg-import, 10x-deterministic): `missing_assoc_type_collision_reject` / `_reversed` (reject both orders) + `missing_assoc_type_collision_accept` (a complete impl still accepted under the same collision). C2 redeclared-supertrait method set (2026-06-15): the impl-site method-set check over-rejected the SEPARATE-supertrait-impl pattern — a sub-trait that REDECLARES its supertrait's methods (`trait ValueMethods: CanonicalValueMethods { fn stringify(self) -> string; … }`, the stdlib json/toml/yaml shape) made those methods bodyless-REQUIRED on the sub, so `impl ValueMethods for Value` was forced to re-provide every redeclared method and rejected with "is missing required method(s)" even though a separate `impl CanonicalValueMethods for Value` supplied them. The `required` set was already own-trait-only (correct), but the MISSING computation never accounted for the sub REDECLARING inherited methods. Fix: in `check_impl_method_set_against_trait`, drop methods also declared by a transitively-reachable supertrait (`collect_super_trait_method_names`) from `missing` — supertrait conformance is resolved LAZILY at the call site (`no method X on T` if no impl supplies it), exactly as a non-redeclared inherited method already was, so redeclared and non-redeclared inherited methods behave identically. The sub's OWN required methods stay required, and the per-method signature check still validates any inline copy. Two stdlib trait decls the check correctly surfaced as inconsistent: `CanonicalValueMethods` was private (supertrait edge could not resolve it cross-package → made `pub`); `RequestMethods` provided `free` in its impl but never declared it (every sibling lifecycle trait declares `fn free(self);` → declared it). Oracles (pkg-import): `imported_redeclared_super_separate_impl_accept` (accept + e2e `tag 105 base 5`), `imported_redeclared_super_missing_own_reject` (own `tag` still required). KNOWN benign diagnostic gap: a trait reached ONLY through an `impl Trait for T` bound or a supertrait edge does not mark its import used, so its `import` draws a false `unused import` warning (pre-existing; lint keys `used_modules` and supertrait/impl-bound resolution never marks it; benign — ratchet keys on exit code, not warnings). |
| `codegen-abi-authority` | A lowering helper selects an ABI variant (bytes vs. string) by querying a span-keyed type map built by the checker. | Route ABI selection through an explicit authority hierarchy: type annotation → known C-call name → chained combinator propagation → tracked binding → safe default. Remove `resolvedTypeOf` calls from ABI decision paths and add tests that erase the relevant `expr_types` entries to prove the explicit path is load-bearing. | fix/bytes-stream-abi-authority. |
| `checker-side-table-built-before-its-reader` | A coercion, method-resolution, or check predicate reads a checker side-table (descriptor/registry/satisfaction map) that is populated by a LATER pass in `check_program` (e.g. built after the body-checking loop, or only at the output-boundary). | Build the side-table BEFORE the pass that consumes it: if body-checking reads it, populate it right after `collect_functions` (signatures are final there) into a `Checker` field, then read that field at the output boundary instead of rebuilding — a rebuild re-runs collision/diagnostic emission and can diverge from what the consumer saw. Verify the builder's inputs (program + registered sigs) are all available at the earlier point; for concrete declared signatures the pre- vs post-substitution build is identical. Separately, a satisfaction predicate that consults `trait_defs` only matches traits that were REGISTERED — a non-`pub` stdlib module trait is skipped (`register_stdlib_hew_items` gates on `visibility.is_pub()`), so the handler/marker trait a coercion keys on must be `pub`. Prove it with a `hew check` that exercises the coercion, not just a unit test on the predicate. | feat/active-mode-conn-attach-surface (2026-06-02): `LocalPid<Actor>`→`LocalPid<ConnectionHandler>` coercion read `actor_protocol_descriptors`, which was built after body-checking → always-empty during the coercion; moved the build before body-checking into a `Checker` field. `ConnectionHandler` had to become `pub` or it never entered `trait_defs`. The coercion deliberately leaves the recorded expr type concrete (does not rewrite it) so codegen still recovers the actor for msg_id synthesis — `checker-authority` in reverse: a coercion may widen the *accepted* type without erasing the *recorded* one. |
| `container-abi-ctor-op-agreement` | A heap-allocated value has two mutually-exclusive element/payload ABIs (owned vs BitCopy descriptor, retained vs inline, …) chosen per shape, and the choice is computed independently at the constructor and at one or more operation sites (push/get/set/pop/free, or a desugar that synthesizes the op symbol). | The owned-vs-BitCopy (or any per-shape ABI-variant) verdict MUST come from ONE structural authority threaded to the constructor AND every operation site; a constructor that uses a different predicate than the operations builds a handle under one ABI that the op then aborts on (`hew check` passes, `hew run` aborts — `check-pass-does-not-imply-run-pass`). Concretely: (1) the constructor and every op site call the same predicate (do not let the bitcopy-probe omit an enum/tuple arm that the heap-ownership walk handles); (2) a HIR/marker-only desugar that bakes an op symbol from `ValueClass` cannot see structural heap-ownership — finalize the symbol downstream (MIR) through the same authority the other ops use, never trust the marker-only guess; (3) pin BOTH an emission test (constructor stays on the expected ABI for the no-heap shape) AND a `hew run` exec test (the round-trip does not abort) for each shape class (payload-free enum, all-scalar-payload enum, owned enum/tuple/record, array-literal of each); (4) classify a pointer-shaped builtin handle (`LocalPid`/`ActorRef`/`Actor`) by its STRUCTURAL `builtin` discriminant, NOT a `TypeDef` flag the handle leaves at its default — these handles have `TypeDef.is_indirect == false`, so an `is_indirect`-keyed op classifier routes them to the layout-descriptor ABI while the constructor (seeing the resolved pointer shape) builds the plain-ptr ABI; the op classifier must match by builtin kind so both pick `ptr`. (5) A `machine` is a tagged union at the value-class layer — it projects into an enum-layout VIEW (`machine_enum_views`) so a machine field classifies via `classify_enum`, BitCopy-iff-every-variant-payload-BitCopy, exactly as an enum. That view is ONE authority and MUST reach EVERY aggregate classifier consumer, not only the site whose bug you are chasing: when the view was chained into the classification list for the actor-state classifier but the user-function/handler/machine-step builders got the bare `enum_layouts`, a machine held as a user-record field missed the enum-view lookup and the record rejected (`UnsupportedUserRecordValueClass` "value class Unknown") while the same machine worked as actor state. Thread the augmented view to every function-body builder; keep the bare view flowing to codegen layout registration (machines register separately). Do NOT instead add a `machine ⇒ BitCopy` (or machine arm) to `ValueClass::of_ty` — that is a SECOND divergent authority lacking the payload registry, wrong for payload-bearing machines, and re-opens the MIR-admits/codegen-refuses seam. Mirror against the enum control to find the TRUE invariant: a payload-free enum-in-record is `CowValue` + `RecordInPlace` (it DOES synthesize a clone thunk), so a "payload-free machine should be BitCopy / no thunk" expectation is a divergence FROM the proven path, not parity — verify the sibling shape's actual behaviour (`--dump-mir elab` + emitted `.ll`) before assuming the gate. (6) The heap-ownership WALK ITSELF (`ty_contains_heap_owning`, the MIR `named_elem_owns_heap`, codegen `resolved_ty_contains_heap_leaf`) must treat a `Vec`/`HashMap`/`HashSet` builtin as a heap-owning LEAF for ANY element type — even `Vec<i64>` owns its buffer — so a record/enum/tuple FIELD of a collection type makes the whole composite heap-owning. These walks historically only treated `string`/`bytes` as leaves and recursed into a collection's type-args, so `type Boxed { payload: [i64] }` classified non-heap-owning and a `Vec<Boxed>` fell through BOTH the owned-element arm (`is_owned_vec_element` false) AND the plain-vec arm (`ValueClass::of_ty(Boxed)` correctly `CowValue` ≠ BitCopy) — into NO drop class, leaking the whole chain (`indexing it via xs[0] made it observable`). The walks MUST agree with `ValueClass::of_ty`, which already classifies these builtins as `CowValue` for any element. (7) An array-literal of owned-element records (`[Boxed {..}, ..]`) constructs each element as a FRESH single-use `record_init` temp (even a named-binding element is re-built into a throwaway first) — its owned push must be a MOVE-in (`hew_vec_push_owned_move`: byte-copy + heap transfer, no clone thunk), NOT the COPY-IN clone `hew_vec_push_owned`. COPY-IN assumes the source is a tracked binding that RETAINS its own scope-exit drop (`container-ingress-ownership-is-per-container`); a transient temp has no binding and no drop, so the deep-cloned-from original leaks. A user `v.push(existing_owned)` keeps the COPY-IN clone (its source lives on). | W5.016 (2026-06-02): `Vec<payload-free-enum>` aborted — the constructor's bitcopy probe had no enum arm so it over-routed every enum to owned while push/get stayed BitCopy; `Vec<owned> = [..]` aborted — the array-literal desugar baked the op symbol from marker-only `ValueClass`. Fixed by routing the constructor through the same heap-ownership authority push/get/free use, and upgrading the array-literal op in MIR. `Vec<LocalPid<T>>`: `vec_element_runtime_suffix` keyed on `TypeDef.is_indirect` (false for actor handles) → push/constructor ABI disagreement → abort; fixed by classifying actor-handle builtins via the structural builtin discriminant. Three disagreeing authorities collapsed to one. fix/hewbot-1906-machine-field (2026-06-15, #1906): machine-in-user-record rejected while machine-as-actor-state worked — the `machine_enum_views` classification view reached only the actor-state classifier; threaded it into every function-body builder so the user-record classifier (`owned_aggregate_record_field_kinds_for_key`) resolves a machine field via `classify_enum`. Oracles: 3 Rust classifier units (payload-free/i64/string, each fails unfixed with the exact reject diagnostic) + a compiled-`.hew` exec ratchet reading the field back with exact-value assertions (non-zero tag, i64 payload `99`, string payload round-trip). KNOWN FOLLOW-UP (separate seam): a GENERIC-machine field (`Lifecycle<i64>`) needs the all-`i64`→bare-name canon (mirroring actor-state `normalize_machine_field_ty`) AT the MIR gate AND the machine view threaded into CODEGEN's `state_clone` re-synthesis — the gate-only canon admits but codegen re-classification then fails closed late ("could not resolve `RecordLayout` for nested user record"); a second classifier consumer still on the bare view, exactly this row's "every consumer" warning. v0.6-generic-direct-call (2026-06-19): a `Vec<record-with-collection-field>` (`type Boxed { payload: [i64] }`, exposed by the cross-module generic free-fn `first<T>(xs:[T])->T` indexing `xs[0]`) leaked its entire chain under Valgrind (`304 (120 direct, 184 indirect)` from `hew_vec_new_with_layout` + the per-element payload buffers). Root cause was NOT the generic-call lowering — the monomorphic and inline-index baselines leaked identically. Three layers: (a) the heap-ownership walks omitted the `Vec`/`HashMap`/`HashSet` collection-field leaf arm (point 6) → `Vec<Boxed>` fell through every drop class; (b) once classified owned, the array-literal COPY-IN `hew_vec_push_owned` deep-cloned each element and leaked the fresh `record_init` temp (point 7) → added `hew_vec_push_owned_move`; (c) a separate pre-existing f-string interpolation leak (`to_string_<ty>` catalog producer unrecognised by `is_fresh_owned_string_producer`, which only keyed the `hew_<ty>_to_string` runtime names) — see `drop-allowset-from-value-flow`. Verified leak-clean (`0 bytes in use at exit`, `0 errors`) under Valgrind on Linux x86_64 across fixture/mono/inline/trivial + macOS `leaks` + MallocScribble; `nested_vec_push_leak_oracle`, `owned_string_temp_drop_canary`, `vec_owned_element_routing_exec`, and `run_e2e` (125) all green. |
| `imported-impl-method-lowering-parity` | A HIR pre-pass or body-emission arm for **imported** modules gates impl-block methods on per-method `pub`, OR an "import X works" lane decides to eagerly lower every imported impl method. | Impl methods in Hew carry no independent visibility (bodies never write `pub fn`; access is governed by the trait/type), and the checker registers EVERY imported impl method into `fn_sigs` / emits `RewriteToFunction { c_symbol: "<Type>::<method>" }` with no `pub` filter — so a `pub` gate on the imported `fn_registry` pre-pass or `lower_impl_block(pub_only=true)` drops ALL of them, and any non-trivial builder method (void C call then `return self`, which the runtime handle-method pass-through path does NOT capture) fails closed at the boundary (`IndirectCallUnsupported` / `CallableUnsupportedInMir`). Mirror the root path (no `pub` filter) and thread the same-module fn-rewrite map into impl bodies. But do NOT lower eagerly: eager lowering unmasks pre-existing per-module cross-module-resolution gaps that the drop-everything path hid (`std::channel` recv → codegen-intercepted `hew_channel_recv` not extern-declared; `std::net::websocket` `attach: LocalPid<WebSocketHandler>`; `fs.IoError` dotted refs). Skip a method whose body calls a bare name resolvable in neither the rewrite map nor `fn_registry`, OR whose signature names anything beyond primitives/builtins + the impl self type. But scope each skip predicate to GENUINELY-unresolvable cases, else ADT-returning methods (`Result<_, fs.IoError>`, `Option<T>`) are dropped too: (a) exempt builtin variant ctors (`BUILTIN_ENUM_VARIANT_BARE_NAMES`: `Ok`/`Err`/`Some`/`None`/…) from the body-unresolvable scan — they resolve via `machine_ctor_registry`, not `fn_registry`; (b) admit a dotted `module.Type` in a signature when its decl was registered at the MIR boundary by the imported-module pre-pass (`enum_variants_by_name`/`type_classes`/`record_registry` carry both bare and dotted keys) — `fs.IoError` resolves through MIR+codegen, proven by emitting `.ll`/`.o`, not just `hew check`; (c) seed the imported private-fn closure from impl-method bodies too, not only pub-fn bodies, so a helper reachable only via a method (`net.set_read_timeout` → `net_result_from_status`) is pulled in. Verify with a base-vs-branch import-compile sweep over EVERY stdlib module (`import M; fn main(){}`) — net set of FAIL modules must not grow. | feat/json-import-opaque-resolve (2026-06-02): a `pub` gate on the imported pre-pass dropped opaque `Value` builders. fix/net-trait-wrapper-lowering (2026-06-04): the same skip predicate over-skipped ADT-returning methods (http `try_respond*`, smtp `try_send*`, url `port`, net `set_read_timeout`). Cousin of `intrinsic-stub-fail-closed-every-path` (root↔imported path asymmetry) and `per-module-type-identity`. |
| `checker-codegen-pattern-contract` | A new kind of `if let` / `while let` pattern is permitted by the parser but not yet lowered by codegen. | Pre-validate at the checker call site (not in `bind_pattern`, which is shared with match arms) and reject unsupported patterns there; in codegen, increment the error counter and emit an explicit error rather than silently skipping. Wildcard and identifier patterns are trivially supported without a tag-test; only delay dereferencing the scrutinee to the constructor branch. | fix/iflet-whilelet-pattern-contract. |
| `desugar-emits-checker-accepted-forms` | A parser/AST-level desugar expands a sugar form (composite/hierarchy block, parent-level rule, `for`-over-iterator, any "one authored line → N flat nodes") into the flat IR the type-checker then walks. | The desugar MUST emit the **concrete** forms the downstream checker accepts, never a placeholder the checker rejects. Specifically: a parent-level machine rule over `_` MUST expand to N transitions with a concrete `source_state = "Sk"` (one per member), NOT a single literal `_`-source clone — because `self.field` inside a `_`-source body is rejected at the type-checker (`hew-types/src/check/expressions.rs` `check_machine_transition_self_field_access`, backstopped at `hew-hir/src/lower.rs` `try_lower_machine_self_field_access`): a wildcard source has no single source-state payload, so its `self.field` cannot resolve. Stamping concrete sources gives each clone a real `src_state_idx` so `self.field` resolves against `Sk`. The field-layout error (parent rule reads `self.X` but some `Sk` lacks `X`) must then point at the composite + name the offending substate, not the anonymous expansion site. Gate with a parser unit test asserting the expansion's sources are concrete (never `_`) AND a `hew run` oracle exercising `self.field` in a parent body. | machine-syntax-redesign Slice 4 (2026-06-02): depth-1 composite `on E: _ => T` parent rules desugar to per-member concrete-source transitions in `parse_composite_block`; `composite_parent_rule_expands_to_concrete_source_transitions` asserts no `_` source survives; `run_connection_lifecycle` is the runtime oracle. |
| `alloc-align-from-type-not-runtime-proxy` | A heap allocator (Arc/Rc/box/vec/any header-prefixed payload) computes its payload **alignment** (or any layout fact: size, padding) from an INCIDENTAL runtime value — the source pointer's `(addr).trailing_zeros()`, the byte `size.trailing_zeros()`, or a capped `max_align_t` guess — instead of the type's authoritative ABI alignment. | The allocation alignment MUST come from the type's real ABI alignment threaded from codegen (which knows the LLVM layout: `target_data.get_abi_alignment(&ty)`), never inferred from a runtime proxy. A source address's trailing zeros reflect where the *current* copy happens to sit, not the type's requirement; a byte size's trailing zeros never prove alignment (a payload of any size may be `align(64)`); a `min(align_of::<u128>())` cap silently UNDER-aligns every over-aligned type (SIMD vectors, `#[repr(align(N))]`/cache-line-padded structs) → misaligned access = latent miscompile/UB the day such a type is shared, invisible because the common case (`i32`/`string`) lands aligned by luck. Thread an explicit `align` ABI param (`hew_*_new(data, size, align, drop_fn)`); the runtime only normalises it to a valid `Layout` alignment (non-zero power of two; `0` = no payload → `1`). Prove the regression test has TEETH: pick a type whose true alignment EXCEEDS the old cap AND is unrecoverable from its size (`#[repr(align(64))] struct { [u8;64] }`, `align_of > size_of::<u128>()`), assert `header.data_align == align_of::<T>()` and `ptr % align_of::<T>() == 0` — it must FAIL on the old heuristic (records 16, asserts 64) and PASS after. For ABI/codegen changes the proving gate is the COMPILED `.hew` exec (the closure-env Rc path via a `scope`/`fork` closure with a heap capture), not just the Rust unit test. | RC11 (2026-06-17, `fix/arc-rc-data-align`): `hew_arc_new`/`hew_rc_new` derived `data_align` from `(data as usize).trailing_zeros()` capped at `align_of::<u128>()` (16) — an `align(64)` payload Arc/Rc-shared got a 16-aligned allocation. Threaded `align` from codegen's `get_abi_alignment(&env_struct)`; runtime drops the heuristic for `normalise_align`. Tests: `arc/rc_honours_overaligned_data_align` (align-64, has teeth — proven to fail the old cap via a standalone probe), `arc/rc_normalises_zero_and_non_power_of_two_align`; e2e `tests/vertical-slice/accept/fork_args_spawn.hew` exercises the closure-env Rc path with a heap-string capture. Sibling of `target-constant-from-threaded-arch-not-host-cfg` (layout fact from the threaded authority, not an incidental proxy). |
| `variant-detection-by-resolution` | Classifying a pattern identifier as a variant/constructor vs a fresh binding (in `let`, `match`, `if let`, `while let`), OR any name-vs-builtin classification in the checker where a syntactic heuristic (uppercase-first-letter, keyword membership) is used to decide whether a name is a binding introduction or a reference to a known construct. | Classify by RESOLUTION: a name is a variant/constructor/handler-pattern only if it resolves to a known variant, constructor, or handler in the current scope — never by a syntactic case-heuristic (uppercase-first-letter or similar). The classification MUST also agree between the binding/declaration site and every use site — a let-side/use-side split makes a binding that exists (introduces a local) but is unusable (the use site misclassifies it as a variant reference and fails unresolved). Apply checklist: (1) match `let`/`match`/`if-let`/`while-let` pattern identifiers against the scope's variant/constructor registry; (2) verify the binding-site decision (bind-fresh vs pattern-match) and the use-site decision (read binding vs match variant) agree; (3) add a test for an uppercase non-variant binding (`let INF = 999`) AND a test for a known-variant pattern with the same spelling (`let None = expr else { … }`). The heuristic CANNOT be saved by checking "is this a value type": a value-type check on the scrutinee side splits from the use side in a different way (`let None = 5` introduces a binding at the let site because `i64` has no `None` variant, but the use site still fails because it was not registered as a binding). | PR #2115 error-prop: the uppercase case-heuristic wrongly rejected `let INF = 999` (broke dijkstra, `E_LET_ELSE_DOES_NOT_DIVERGE` on a plain binding); fixing via a value-type check split let-side from use-side (`let None = 5` bound at let but unusable at use); the resolution-based fix matching `expressions.rs` variant lookup closed it correctly. Same class: A178 `send`-handler masked by a reserved-name early-return (use-site misclassification); #2116 the still-open match-arm uppercase-heuristic (`match x { INF => … }` for `x: i64`). |
| `dispatch-proof-before-projection` | Resolving a generic trait method on a builtin/primitive receiver (`Vec`, `HashMap`, `string`, `bytes`) via the primitive-trait-impl side-table (`try_dispatch_primitive_trait_method` / `lookup_primitive_trait_method` in `hew-types/src/check/methods.rs` and `registration.rs`), especially when impl registration keys on the outer constructor name while the receiver carries concrete type-args. | Before projecting a trait method's return or associated type, the dispatch MUST bind the impl's type-params from the CONCRETE receiver and structurally prove the impl applies: same constructor, matching arity, concrete-leaf equality. A non-matching impl MUST fail closed to "no method" — never project its return or associated type as authoritative for the mismatched receiver. The canonical dispatch key (e.g. `"Vec"`) erases element type, so `lookup_primitive_trait_method` can return a `Vec<string>` impl's sig for a `Vec<i64>` receiver: without applicability proof the projected return type (`string`) or `Self::Item` is wrong — a spurious authoritative type that leaks past the checker boundary (or a `Ty::Var` escaping inference). Applicability proof and type projection are inseparable: project only on a proven-matching impl, never from the first key-matching entry regardless of element. | PR #2185 (`fix(types): project generic trait-method returns on builtin receivers`); `try_dispatch_primitive_trait_method` + `lookup_primitive_trait_method` (`hew-types/src/check/methods.rs`, `registration.rs`); over-application negatives — a `Vec<i64>` receiver dispatched to a `Vec<string>` impl — produced wrong projected return types; canonical-key-only registration erased the element type and returned the wrong impl. Cross-ecosystem review caught the gap after the canonical-key registration landed. |
| `erased-newtype-binary-result-from-checker` | Adding or completing arithmetic on a builtin newtype that the checker keeps DISTINCT but a lower IR ERASES to its backing scalar (`instant`→i64, and any future `Named{builtin}` that canonicalises). The HIR binary-expr lowering (`hew-hir/src/lower.rs` `binary_ty`) recomputes the result type from the lowered OPERAND `ResolvedTy`s, which are already erased. | When the checker admits an operation whose RESULT type differs from what the erased operands imply (`instant - instant → duration`, but both operands lower to `ResolvedTy::I64` so `binary_ty(Sub, I64, I64) = I64`), the operand-derived result is WRONG and silently mistypes the value — it then routes to the wrong Display arm / loses the newtype's accessor methods, with NO error (a fail-OPEN wrong-type, not a reject). `binary_ty` over erased operands cannot recover the distinct result; prefer the checker's recorded `expr_types[mk_key(span)]` result type when it disagrees (adopt the checker's `Duration` only when `binary_ty` did not already produce it, so genuine scalar arithmetic is untouched). A literal-operand fixture (`10ms + 5ms`, operands already `Duration`) PASSES and masks the bug — the failing shape is the COMPUTED-operand case where erasure happens (`(b - a)` with `a,b: instant`). Assert the rendered/round-tripped result of a computed-operand expression, not just a literal one. This is the `checker-codegen-pattern-contract` invariant one layer down: checker and HIR must agree on the EXACT result type, and any IR helper that RE-DERIVES a type the checker already decided is a divergence risk for every erased newtype. | cap07-duration-instant-arith (`feat/v06-duration-instant-arith`, 2026-06): `to_string(b - a)` for `a,b: instant` rendered `5000000` (i64 raw, no `ns`) while `to_string(10ms - 5ms)` rendered `5000000ns` — `binary_ty` typed the instant-subtraction result i64 (erased operands) instead of the checker's `duration`. Fixed by preferring `expr_types` Duration at the binary span. Cousin: `checker-codegen-pattern-contract`, `multi-wall-fail-closed-feature-completion`. |
| `assoc-type-carrier-flag-discipline` | Editing the condition that decides when to emit a deferred `Ty::AssocType` carrier vs collapse `Self::Item` to the impl's concrete type — specifically the `Self::Bar` resolution branch in `resolve_ty_inner` / `resolve_annotation_ty` (`hew-types/src/check/resolution.rs`). Also fires when adding a new trait with associated types. | A deferred `Ty::AssocType` carrier — emitted when resolving a trait method's declared signature so downstream call sites can collapse `Self::Item` once `Self` is concrete — MUST be gated ONLY on the `current_trait_for_self_projection` flag (set only while resolving a trait method's signature from raw AST), NEVER on `impl_alias_scopes.is_empty()` or any other impl-body scope state. Gating on impl-alias-scope presence collapses `Self::Item` during impl-body re-resolution: when the checker re-enters an impl body to check an inner call (e.g. `it.next()` inside `impl Iterator for Map { fn next(&self) -> Option<Self::Item>; }`), the impl's `type Item = B` alias scope is active and suppresses the carrier path, so `Self::Item` collapses to `B` — mistyping the inner iterator's item and producing a spurious "expected A, found B" across the whole program. The gating conditions are orthogonal: `current_trait_for_self_projection` tracks whether we are resolving a TRAIT METHOD SIG from raw AST (carrier needed); impl-alias scope state tracks whether an impl's concrete assoc-type binding is in scope (irrelevant at sig-resolution time). | PR #2175 (`fix(types): keep Self::Item deferred in impl-body check`); `current_trait_for_self_projection` flag in `hew-types/src/check/resolution.rs`; symptom: `it.next()` inside an `Iterator` impl body typed `Self::Item` as the impl's own concrete type → spurious type-mismatch on the caller's element; `self_item_projection` test family: fail-pre (carrier suppressed by active alias scope), pass-post (carrier gated on projection flag only). |
| `structural-equality-is-reflexive-bitwise-float` | Choosing the equality/hash semantics for a float (`f32`/`f64`) leaf inside a STRUCTURAL context — a record/enum/tuple field, a `Vec` element, a `HashMap`/`HashSet` key/element — OR deciding whether floats satisfy the `Eq`/`Hash` markers. Also fires when an eligibility gate rejects a leaf "because NaN != NaN". | Structural equality MUST be REFLEXIVE (`x == x` for every `x`, including `NaN`), because it drives dedup, `contains`, and HashMap/HashSet key identity — `x == x → false` is a correctness hole (a value cannot find itself). Reflexivity FORCES bitwise/total float semantics: the eq thunk bit-casts each float to a same-width integer (`f32→i32`, `f64→i64`) and integer-compares the bit patterns (so `NaN == NaN` when the bits match, `+0.0 != -0.0`), NEVER IEEE `fcmp oeq` (which is non-reflexive). The hash thunk MUST hash the SAME bit pattern (bitcast + zext + the shared integer mix) so `==` IMPLIES an equal hash — the eq basis and the hash basis are ONE decision; a mismatch (bitwise eq + numeric hash, or vice versa) silently breaks every map lookup. This is DISTINCT from scalar numeric `==` (a bare `f64 == f64` expression), which stays IEEE (`NaN != NaN`, `+0.0 == -0.0`) and lowers through MIR `FloatCmp`, not the thunk — keep the two paths separate. Floats therefore DO satisfy `Eq` + `Hash` (bitwise/total) but NOT `Ord` (ordering stays IEEE-partial; a total bitwise order is a separate decision). The eligibility gate, the eq thunk, and the hash thunk are THREE consumers of the same verdict and must all agree: a checker that admits a float-bearing aggregate while the thunk fails closed is the cliff this fixes; prove the full chain with a COMPILED `.hew` exec asserting `NaN==NaN` (same bits) is TRUE, `+0.0 == -0.0` is FALSE, and a float-bearing-key HashMap round-trips (insert+get) — value-asserting, not `.len()`. | feat/v06-f64-bitwise-equality (2026-06-27): removed the checker float-eq BLOCK (`eq_eligibility`/`hash_eligibility` `IneligibleFloat` verdict deleted), flipped the `Eq`/`Hash` markers on for floats (Ord stays partial), replaced the `eq_thunk`/`hash_thunk` float fail-closed (`hew-codegen-rs/src/thunks.rs`) with the bitwise compare + bit-pattern hash via `float_bits_int_type`. The same change uniformly enables `Vec<float-record>::contains`, `HashSet<f64>`, bare `HashMap<f64,V>`, and a generic `fn same<T>(a:T,b:T)->bool { a==b }` over a float-bearing T (former eq-thunk bypass) — all route through the one bitwise thunk. Proof gate: a compiled `.hew` exec asserting `NaN==NaN` (identical bits) is true and `+0.0 == -0.0` is false, plus a float-bearing-record-key HashMap insert+get round-trip. |

### `exhaustive-coverage` — no wildcard fallthrough in dispatch or lowering

- **area**: analysis, codegen, match
- **invariant**: Visitors, dispatch chains, and match lowerings must enumerate every supported variant and every operation×type pair. Wildcard or default branches in semantic positions hide gaps as silent wrong code; cross-enum fallback and guarded wildcards count as gaps.
- **why**: Adding a new AST variant or operand type without an exhaustive matrix lets the new shape silently take the default arm. The compiler keeps producing output, but the output is wrong for the new case.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `exhaustive-traversal-and-lowering` | A new AST variant, lowering branch, or supported type is added — **including a new variant on a self-recursive type enum** (e.g. `Ty`) handled by structural walkers. Also fires when a MIR `lower_value` match has a wildcard `_ => None` catch-all that silently swallows an identifiable-but-unimplemented case. | Maintain explicit variant/type lists, build an operation × type matrix for typed lowerings, cover narrow widths and uncommon shapes, and prefer errors over warnings when a case is unsupported. **For a new variant on a recursive `Ty`-shaped enum, audit every self-recursive walker** (`map_children`, `any_child`/`contains_var`, `substitute`/`substitute_named_param` and peers): a pre-existing `_` arm silently treats the new variant as a *leaf*, so `substitute` stops rewriting through it and `contains_var` returns `false` — letting an unresolved `Ty::Var` inside the new variant **escape inference into codegen** (type-inference-boundary breach). This failure is **invisible to a diff-grep** because the offending `_` arms are pre-existing (not `+` lines); only exhaustive matches (no `_`) or cross-ecosystem review catch it. Prefer deleting the `_` wildcard in structural `Ty` walkers so the compiler forces every future variant to be handled. **For `lower_value` wildcard arms:** a `HirExprKind::BindingRef { .. } => None` catch-all is a fail-OPEN class. A `BindingRef { resolved: Item(_), ty: Function }` case falls through silently — `lower_value` returns `None`, the argument is missing, the call emits no output and exits 0. Every MIR `lower_value` catch-all arm must either (a) emit a `NotYetImplemented` diagnostic before returning `None`, or (b) have an explicit comment naming exactly what cases it still covers. **When the new variant is a single-operand borrowing read** (carries one sub-expr the walker just recurses into, e.g. a codec/intrinsic node), the exhaustiveness pass forces an arm at every walker but then `clippy::match_same_arms` (pre-push gate) REJECTS a standalone arm whose body duplicates a sibling — merge it into the existing `Unary { operand, .. }` (or other identical-body) arm via an or-pattern rather than adding a separate arm; expect this at ~8-10 walkers per IR layer (HIR `node.rs` exhaustive matches + MIR `Instr` def/use/source/alias classifiers). | PR #798/#786/#797; `e1fe0c37` (added `Ty::Borrow`; `map_children`/`any_child`/`substitute_named_param` swallowed it via pre-existing `_` until each got an explicit pointee-recursing arm + 3 unit tests proving `contains_var(&Var)`/`&T→&string`/`&Vec<$v>→&Vec<i32>`; caught by cross-eco GPT-5.5 review, not by the diff). `feat/named-fn-as-value` (lower.rs:5496 `BindingRef { .. } => None` swallowed `ResolvedRef::Item(_)` + `Function` type — named fns as values produced silent exit 0, no output; fixed by adding an explicit arm before the wildcard and annotating the wildcard with a comment naming surviving cases). |
| `match-fail-closed` | Match checking or lowering changes. | Forbid cross-enum fallback, treat guarded wildcards as non-exhaustive, exclude `Never` and `Error` from result inference, wrap `HashMap.get()` at the expression boundary, trap on runtime fallthrough, and emit `MirStatement::Bind` (not just `Instr::Move`) at the entry of every arm body that introduces a payload binding — the move-checker dataflow keys on `Bind` to lift the binding from `Uninit` to `Live`, so a bare `Move` into the binding's local trips `InitialisedBeforeUse` on the first arm-body read. **The runtime-fallthrough trap must be UNREACHABLE for any match the checker accepted as exhaustive — a reachable trap on valid input is a silent-wrong miscompile (`check`-green, `run`-exit-1, no output).** When a lowering collapses several arms into a single representative (e.g. "the first `Binding`/`Wildcard` arm is the catch-all"), it silently drops every later arm — including the real `_` default — and the dropped-default path then hits the trap. A `Binding`/`Wildcard` arm is a catch-all ONLY when it has no guard; a guarded binding arm (`x if p => …`) must fall through to the next arm on guard failure. Lower literal/binding/wildcard arms as ONE ordered chain in source order (mismatch OR guard-failure → next arm; final fall-through → trap), never as `leading_literals + Option<single_catch_all>`. Exec-validate (`hew run`, assert stdout) the fall-through path: a `check`-only or MIR-shape test cannot catch a dropped default arm. | Original match correctness audit; `feat/mono-mixed-enum-payload-ctor`; `fix/match-default-arm` (2026-06-02): `lower_match_literal` collapsed all non-literal arms into one `wildcard_arm`, dropping every arm after the first guarded `Binding` (incl. the real `_`); fall-through emitted `Trap{ExhaustivenessFallthrough}` so `match n { 0 => …, x if x>100 => …, _ => … }` on `n=5` exited 1 with no output. Fixed by lowering all arms as one ordered chain; pinned by `match_literal_guard_default_exec.rs`. |

| `arity-escape-sentinel-needs-a-real-elsewhere-validator` | A table-driven method/call descriptor (e.g. `collection_method_desc`) uses a sentinel value (`None`, a wildcard, an "unchecked" marker) on an arity/argument-shape field to mean "this method's arguments are validated somewhere downstream, not by this table" — and a new entry, or an entry copied from a sibling method, adopts that same sentinel. | Before using the escape sentinel on a new or copied table entry, name and verify the ACTUAL downstream validator that will run for THIS method — do not assume "some other method in the family uses `None` safely, so this one can too." If no downstream validator exists (or the downstream site is codegen reaching the construct for the first time, not a dedicated checker pass), the escape sentinel is fail-OPEN: bad input is admitted past type-checking and only surfaces later as an ungraceful codegen-front failure instead of a clean check-time diagnostic. Prefer an explicit arity (`Some(0)`, `Some(n)`) matching the method's real shape; reserve the escape sentinel for methods with a NAMED, verifiable elsewhere-validator (cite it in the same table entry or its comment). | `clear()` descriptor gap (2026-07-03, `09fe1feeb`, caught by GPT cross-eco as the sole blocker across 5 behavioural lanes): `HashMap.clear`/`HashSet.clear` used `desc(None, ...)`, copied from sibling zero-arg entries where `None` IS legitimate (`len`, `is_empty`, `set`, `append` are validated elsewhere) — but nothing validated `clear`'s arity, so `m.clear(123)` type-checked clean and failed only at codegen-front. Fixed by explicit `desc(Some(0), ...)` matching `Vec.clear`'s existing arity; 4 regression tests assert check-time rejection with an arity diagnostic. |
### `lifecycle-symmetry` — every setup has a matched teardown on every exit path

- **area**: control flow, codegen RAII, FFI handles, runtime shutdown, concurrent test cleanup
- **invariant**: Allocations, opened handles, locks, mailboxes, profiler state, and partial select/join setups must be released on every exit path — return, panic, timeout, cancel, shutdown — with exactly one canonical release path per owned thing. Manual `close()` / `free()` and automatic drop must agree on who is canonical.
- **why**: Cleanup paths that only handle the happy case leak under failure; double-cleanup paths free twice. Both are silently catastrophic — the first as accumulating debt, the second as memory corruption.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `cleanup-all-exits` | Code stages setup work or mutates side-channel state before success is guaranteed, OR a checker/elaborator is built against a scaffold whose CFG is structurally flat (single basic block) and will widen later. | Evaluate return expressions before drops, reset pending state on failure, deactivate all intermediate loops, and clean partial select/join/ask setup before panicking, timing out, or returning early. When bounded teardown cannot wait for a live worker, transfer ownership to a reaper that performs the final join and free path; treat an outstanding join handle as the worker-liveness authority even if task state already says `Done`. **Teardown that races an in-flight reply must DRAIN the reply send before the close/free barrier, not after.** A graceful `node_stop` that zeroes its `CURRENT_NODE` use-after-free barrier (or sets a "stopping" flag the reply path bails on) BEFORE draining in-flight inbound-ask workers abandons replies those workers already computed: the worker reaches `send_reply_envelope`, sees the barrier tripped, drops the reply, and the peer's reader observes the connection close mid-ask → a spurious `ConnectionDropped` even though the node is still ALIVE and the reply existed. The fix is ordering, not a new lock: close the SPAWN gate (a flag distinct from the UAF/teardown guard so it does not also make in-flight sends bail), drain the per-manager worker counter to zero so earned replies flush while the transport is still up, and only THEN trip the close barrier and free. The drain ceiling must remain (a straggler past it bails fail-closed at the still-present UAF guard), and the spawn gate must be a SEPARATE flag from the reply-bail flag — collapsing them re-introduces the abandon. For runtime-level reset: register every subsystem's cleanup in a session hook registry at init so it fires from every shutdown path. **Resolved gap**: when a Ready/Suspended task is cancelled via `mark_done(Cancelled)`, user-code Drop previously never fired; resources held in those stack frames leaked until process exit. Fixed by adding `HewTask::cancel_cleanup_fn: Option<unsafe extern "C" fn(*mut c_void)>` — a compiler-registered callback invoked (with `env_ptr` as the borrowed argument) before `mark_done(Cancelled)` in both `hew_task_scope_cancel` and `hew_task_scope_cancel_one`. The field is taken (cleared) before the call for idempotence under double-cancel; `env_ptr` deallocation via `hew_rc_drop` in `hew_task_free` is unchanged. Compiler codegen must emit this function to call `@resource close()` and `@linear consume()` for task-captured resources. Regression tests: `scope_cancel_fires_cancel_cleanup_fn_for_ready_and_suspended_tasks`, `cancel_one_fires_cancel_cleanup_fn_for_ready_task`, `cancel_cleanup_fn_fires_at_most_once_on_double_cancel`. For IR-level move-checkers and drop elaborators: a forward-scan that walks a flat `MirStatement` stream is degenerate-correct only under a single-block CFG; the moment `if`/`match`/loop lowering produces real basic blocks, the checker must run as a per-block dataflow over a path-sensitive lattice (in v0.5 the four-state `Uninit \| Live \| Consumed \| MaybeConsumed` lattice on `BindingId`) and drop plans must be enumerated per `Terminator::Return` block — not function-wide. `MaybeConsumed` at any Return exit on a `@linear` binding is a hard `MustConsume` rejection, not a "drop on some paths" recovery. Pin both the lattice meet rules (commutativity + associativity + idempotence) and the per-Return-block drop narrowing as property tests before the CFG-aware lowering merges, so the scaffold-correct-under-flat-MIR substrate cannot regress silently. | PR #801/#794/#1271 (hew_sched_shutdown reset gaps); task-scope cancelled-worker reclamation; fix/fix-task-scope-cleanup-cancel (`HewTask::cancel_cleanup_fn`, taken-before-call for double-cancel idempotence); `hew-mir/src/dataflow.rs` — four-state `Uninit\|Live\|Consumed\|MaybeConsumed` lattice + per-block worklist + per-Return-block drop narrowing replaced the pre-CFG flat-stream scan. fix/v060-connection-lifecycle: `hew_node_stop` drained in-flight inbound-ask reply sends only AFTER zeroing its `CURRENT_NODE` barrier + `mark_stopping`, so a worker that reached `send_reply_envelope` after the barrier dropped its computed reply → spurious `ConnectionDropped` (the two-process remote-ask tests flaked ~5-15% under load, T-01/T-02). Reordered to a Phase-1 drain behind a NEW `HewConnMgr.inbound_spawn_closed` spawn gate (distinct from `reconnect_shutdown`) before the barrier; proven 100/100 under concurrent load on a 32-core host with `--retries 0`, retiring the test-side retry shim. |
| `cyclic-cfg-worklist-rpo` | A dataflow worklist pass is added or changed on a CFG that now contains back-edges (loop lowering, or any new `Terminator::Goto` that targets a lower-ID block). | Seed the worklist in Reverse Post-Order (RPO), not block-ID order. Use a visited-only meet: skip predecessors whose exit-state has not yet been computed when computing the entry state of the current block. Run diagnostics in a separate sweep after the fixpoint converges, using the stable exit states from the fixpoint pass — never emit diagnostics inside the fixpoint loop itself. ID-order iteration on cyclic CFGs processes a block's successor (body_bb) before some of that block's predecessors (overhead blocks allocated by checked-arithmetic such as overflow_trap_bb have IDs higher than body_bb), so the body block's entry state is computed with stale or absent predecessor states, injecting false Uninit contributions that survive in the dedup set and surface as false-positive `InitialisedBeforeUse` diagnostics. RPO guarantees that on the first sweep every forward-edge predecessor is processed before the block it feeds; true back-edges are the only unvisited predecessors on first pass and are correctly handled by the visited-only filter. | feat/for-while-lowering commits 0b03e2c9 (HIR) and f5206a01 (MIR+dataflow); `hew-mir/src/dataflow.rs:350` (`compute_rpo`), `:230` (`meet_predecessors` visited-only filter), `:652` (`analyze` two-pass fixpoint + diagnostic sweep). |
| `death-signal-fires-on-every-terminal-cause` | Building or extending a terminal-signal delivery path — actor DOWN/EXIT, monitor/link notification, supervisor death callback, cross-node MonitorLost — that must fire when a watched thing reaches a terminal state. Fires especially when the same logical signal is reachable through MORE THAN ONE finalize path (a crash trap vs a clean self-stop finalize vs a connection-drop/partition fan-out). | A death-signal is fail-OPEN until it is proven to fire on EVERY distinct terminal cause, because the causes usually flow through SEPARATE finalize code paths and fixing one leaves the others silent. Enumerate the terminal causes for the watched thing (clean exit, crash, unreachable/partition at minimum) and confirm each routes through a site that emits the signal — do NOT assume one finalize path (e.g. the crash trap `notify_monitors_on_death`) covers a sibling (e.g. the scheduler's `Stopping → Stopped` self-stop finalize, which historically notified the actor-group condvars but NOT monitors). When the signal is one-shot and reachable from a definitive cause AND a weaker fallback (a real exit DOWN vs a connection-drop MonitorLost), arm a single per-registration slot that only transitions `Pending → Delivered` so the fallback fan-out is a no-op once a definitive signal landed (exactly-once; a drop after a clean exit must deliver NO second signal). PROVE it with a fixture that exercises ALL THREE causes and asserts a DISTINCT reason per cause PLUS a negative no-duplicate guard (a second observe must time out) — a fixture that only proves clean-exit fail-OPENs on the drop/crash case and a single-cause green is non-evidence. | Cross-node monitor (`feat/v06-dist-6-cross-node-monitor`): cross-node `monitor(RemotePid)` delivered the crash DOWN (via `hew_actor_trap` → `notify_monitors_on_death`) and the connection-drop MonitorLost (via the retire / SWIM-DEAD fan-out) but NOT the clean-exit DOWN — `hew_actor_self_stop`'s `Stopping → Stopped` scheduler finalize ran `notify_actor_death` (condvars) and `call_terminate_fn` but never `notify_monitors_on_death`, so a monitor of a cleanly-stopped actor (LOCAL or cross-node) observed nothing. The three-cause two-process fixture forced the gap visible (clean-exit `reason=-2` timeout while crash + drop were green); fixed by adding `notify_monitors_on_death(id, Stopped)` to both self-stop finalize sites. Exactly-once is anchored by the distributed table's `Pending → Delivered → Consumed` slot. Cousin: `cleanup-all-exits` (every setup has a teardown on every exit; this is every terminal cause has a signal on every finalize path). |
| `failure-detector-verdict-resolves-every-waiter-kind` | A failure-detector verdict (SWIM-DEAD, connection-drop, node-leave) fans out to wake things blocked on a now-unreachable peer, and the runtime holds MORE THAN ONE kind of per-peer waiter (a blocked `recv` on a recv-queue, a monitor registration, a pending remote ask in a reply table, a pending lookup, …). Fires when adding a new waiter kind keyed by peer, or extending the DEAD/drop fan-out. | A failure-detector verdict that resolves SOME waiter kinds but not ALL of them fails OPEN on the unresolved kind: the recv-queue side waking to `PartitionDetected` while the reply-table side never gets touched means a blocked `recv` resolves but a pending `ask` to the SAME dead peer hangs to its caller deadline. Each waiter kind has its OWN per-peer table and its OWN fan-out call — fixing one does not reach the siblings. Enumerate every per-peer waiter table at the DEAD/drop escalation site and confirm EACH has a fan-out call there (recv-queue `force_partition`, monitor `MonitorLost`, reply-table `Partition`, …); the typed cause must match the verdict (SWIM-DEAD → `Partition`, socket-drop → `ConnectionDropped`, both distinct from `Timeout`). Drain-then-fail each waiter UNDER ITS TABLE LOCK so a verdict racing a socket drop resolves the waiter exactly once (the second fan-out finds an empty map). Keep the failure-DETECTION substrate (the cluster registry) transport-agnostic and fan out from the node side, mirroring the sibling waiter kinds. PROVE the new kind with a test that injects the verdict WITH THE SOCKET LEFT OPEN (so only the detector verdict, not a TCP drop, can resolve it) and asserts the exact typed cause + bounded-time (a hang would blow the deadline) + exactly-once (empty table after, repeat fan-out is a no-op). | Partition-policy lane (`feat/v06-dist-7-partition-policy`): `PartitionRegistry::on_member_dead` (`cluster.rs`) walked the recv-queues (`force_partition` → `recv` resolves `PartitionDetected`) and the cross-node monitor lane added the `MonitorLost` fan-out at the same site, but the reply table was never touched — so a pending remote ask to a SWIM-declared-DEAD peer whose socket was still open hung to the caller deadline (`AskError::Partition` (14) was defined but produced nowhere). Fixed by `fail_remote_asks_for_node` (node-side, routing-table → `ConnectionKey` → `fail_connection_with_reason(Partition)`) called next to the monitor fan-out at both MEMBER_DEAD sites; `fail_connection_with_reason` drains under the table lock for exactly-once vs the connection-drop path. Proven by `swim_dead_wakes_pending_remote_ask_with_partition` (socket left open, asserts Partition not ConnectionDropped/Timeout, bounded, exactly-once).
