Quarantine extension (`feat/v06-dist-8b-quarantine-incarnation`): the quarantine set (`node_id → incarnation`) is the NEXT per-peer table reacting at the same MEMBER_DEAD site — routed through one node-side wrapper `fail_remote_and_quarantine` so it cannot insert without also failing the asks; unlike the other waiter kinds it is also EVICTED at the strictly-higher-incarnation readmission (see `buried-identity-returns-only-at-strictly-higher-incarnation`). Sibling of `death-signal-fires-on-every-terminal-cause` (that row: ONE signal across terminal CAUSES; this row: ONE cause across waiter KINDS). |
| `replacement-conn-ask-reason-label` | A SWIM-DEAD verdict resolves pending asks via `fail_remote_asks_for_node`, which reads the routing table at verdict time to find the current `conn_id` for the dead node. | When the routing table has already swapped to a replacement conn_id (old socket retired, new connection established) by the time the verdict fires, the lookup returns the NEW conn's id; pending asks on the OLD conn are not reached by this fan-out and instead resolve via the old reader's cleanup as `ConnectionDropped` rather than `Partition`. This is fail-closed (no ask hangs), but the reason label is wrong. The proper fix — keying the reply table on `(node_id, conn_generation)` so a DEAD verdict can reach a retired conn's draining asks — is deferred because it requires a reply-table schema change and an exactly-once proof. When adding ask-resolution logic: do NOT assume the routing-table lookup returns the same conn_id the pending ask was registered under; a replacement can swap in at any time. Document this window at the lookup site (`hew-runtime/src/hew_node.rs` in `fail_remote_asks_for_node`). | Partition-policy cross-ecosystem review; comment added to `hew_node.rs` `fail_remote_asks_for_node` in the monitor-hardening lane (`feat/v06-dist-8-monitor-hardening`). |
| `cross-node-link-delivers-mailbox-exit-not-recv-slot` | Building a cross-node LINK (fail-together) delivery path on top of a cross-node MONITOR (observe-death) substrate that shares the same per-peer table, terminal sweep, and connection-drop / SWIM-DEAD fan-out. The smell: a link DOWN reusing the monitor's recv-slot delivery (`deliver_to_ref` → a value `recv_down` polls). | A cross-node monitor and a cross-node link diverge at the DELIVERY shape, not just the registration: a monitor DOWN arms a recv slot a program polls; a `CrashLinked` link DOWN must synthesize a `SYS_MSG_EXIT` (103) into the LOCAL linked actor's MAILBOX and CRASH it (the OTP fail-together semantic). A link that lands in the monitor recv slot fails-OPEN — the linked actor never crashes, because nothing polls a link's slot. Key the cascade by the LOCAL actor id stored in the link entry (the remote peer has no `*mut HewActor` here) and replicate the in-process `send_exit_signal` exactly (same `SYS_MSG_EXIT` + `CrashKind` projection + Idle→Runnable wake) so supervision / exit-trapping behaves identically to a local link. Carry the per-link `PartitionPolicy` in the TABLE ENTRY, never the send/ask execution-context slot, or a `CrashLinked` policy leaks into a subsequent send/ask read and fail-closes it. Keep the table pure data — return the cascade action (`{local_actor_id, reason, policy}`) to the runtime layer rather than reaching into actor code from the table. Make a non-`CrashLinked` policy NON-fatal (the discriminator must have teeth). The cascade is exactly-once across all FIVE terminal seams (clean exit, crash, terminal sweep, connection-drop, SWIM-DEAD) via a one-shot `Pending → Consumed` slot. For the drop-side locality split (`MonitorRef::close` reaching a cross-node ref), namespace cross-node ref ids into a high disjoint range (`DIST_REF_ID_BASE = 1<<48`) so `hew_actor_demonitor` routes a local-table miss to the cross-node teardown without ref-id collision. PROVE the headline by LOCALLY observing the linker actor reach terminal `Crashed` (a probe ledger surviving the actor's free), NOT by a bare exit code: a "the link registered" green is non-evidence; only "the local actor DIED" proves the mailbox-EXIT cascade fired rather than a silently-dropped recv slot. ALSO: a packed actor id (`node<<48 \| serial`) is NEGATIVE as i64 when the node id has bit 15 set — a fixture testing `id < 0` for a failure sentinel is FLAKY on node-id assignment; use `== 0` (0 is never a valid id) and pass the id to id-keyed probes as a `u64`. | Cross-node link (`feat/v06-dist-9-explicit-links`): `link_remote(RemotePid<T>, PartitionPolicy)` is the first `CrashLinked` producer + first cross-node mailbox-EXIT cascade. `connection.rs` `handle_link_down_frame` → `hew_node::handle_inbound_link_down` → `dist_monitor::deliver_link_down_to_ref` (one-shot) → `link::deliver_cross_node_link_exit` (resolves the local actor by id, reuses `send_exit_signal`). Policy carried in `WatcherEntry::action` (`WatcherAction::Link { local_actor_id, policy_tag }`), never the context slot. Bidirectional via a `reciprocate` flag on `CTRL_LINK_REQ` (one bounded round trip). Two-process fixtures (`link_remote_crash_cascade_on_{clean_exit,crash,partition}`, `link_remote_non_crashlinked_policy_no_crash`) assert the linker reaches `Crashed` (probe ledger) on each terminal cause and SURVIVES under a non-CrashLinked policy. Siblings: `death-signal-fires-on-every-terminal-cause` (signal across CAUSES) and `failure-detector-verdict-resolves-every-waiter-kind` (cause across waiter KINDS); this row is the DELIVERY-SHAPE divergence (link EXIT-crashes the mailbox, monitor arms a recv slot). |
| `buried-identity-returns-only-at-strictly-higher-incarnation` | Building or redesigning a rejoin/readmission admission gate for an identity the system has buried (a SWIM DEAD/LEFT member, a fenced epoch, a revoked session) where a later "alive" claim about that identity arrives over an untrusted channel (replayed gossip, a stale frame, a reconnect). The smell: an unconditional `DEAD→ALIVE` reject (fails-closed but cannot represent a genuine rejoin) OR an unconditional admit (fails-OPEN — stale gossip resurrects the dead). | A buried identity must return ONLY when it proves a STRICTLY-HIGHER monotonic token (incarnation/epoch/generation); an equal-or-lower token is stale and MUST be inert — it can never resurrect the buried identity. Equal is explicitly NOT a revival (a node DEAD at incarnation N stays dead for any ALIVE-at-N; only N+1 returns), so reuse the SAME strictly-`>` comparator the live-path LWW already uses rather than inventing a parallel `>=` rule. Apply the gate UNIFORMLY across every terminal state (DEAD and graceful-LEFT both readmit by the same branch — a third special case is a bug surface). CRITICAL: distinguish a genuinely peer-ANNOUNCED token from a LOCALLY-SYNTHESIZED one — a TCP reconnect that fabricates `incarnation+1` is NOT proof the peer restarted with a fresh identity and must NOT readmit (thread a `gossip_announced`-style flag so only real announcements are readmission-eligible; the locally-bumped reconnect path keeps un-suspecting a SUSPECT peer but can never resurrect a DEAD one). The buried identity also gets a per-peer QUARANTINE entry inserted at the verdict (a sibling of `failure-detector-verdict-resolves-every-waiter-kind`) and EVICTED exactly once at the readmission dispatch, keyed on `old_state ∈ {DEAD,LEFT} && new_state == ALIVE` (an ALIVE→ALIVE bump has `old_state == ALIVE` and evicts nothing). The send/ask consult compares the peer's LIVE token against the quarantined one (fail-closed if the live token is unknown). PROVE it with a truth table asserting the EXACT post-state (state AND token) for higher→admit / equal→reject / lower→reject across BOTH terminal states, a reconnect-does-not-readmit case, AND a cross-process replay where a stale ALIVE gossip is injected and the identity is asserted to stay buried (the `resurrected-by-stale` line must NEVER fire) — a single-direction "higher is rejected" or "higher is admitted" test is non-evidence for the boundary. | Quarantine + rejoin-admission (`feat/v06-dist-8b-quarantine-incarnation`): `stage_member_transition_locked` (`cluster.rs`) unconditionally rejected `DEAD→ALIVE` before the incarnation LWW, so a genuine higher-incarnation rejoin could not even be represented; redesigned to readmit a DEAD/LEFT node only at a strictly-higher peer-announced incarnation (`gossip_announced` flag gates the locally-synthesized reconnect bump out, preserving `connection_established_dead_member_stays_dead`). The quarantine set (`node_id → incarnation` in `NodeSlot`) is inserted via `fail_remote_and_quarantine` at both MEMBER_DEAD seams and evicted at the readmission dispatch; `PartitionPolicy::Quarantine` send/ask consults it. Proven by the in-process truth table (`dead_member_revived_only_by_strictly_higher_incarnation` + the LEFT sibling + `reconnect_bump_does_not_readmit_dead_node`), the in-process block-then-clear (`quarantine_blocks_send_under_policy_then_clears_on_evict`), and the compiled two-process `quarantine_rejoin` fixture (asserts BOTH `stale-rejected` AND `readmitted-at=6`, forbids `resurrected-by-stale`). Sibling of `failure-detector-verdict-resolves-every-waiter-kind` (the quarantine set is the per-peer table that reacts at the verdict AND clears at readmission) and `boundary-fail-closed` (the `≤`-incarnation reject is the fail-closed boundary). |
| `ffi-ownership-contracts` | A boundary returns pointers, diagnostics, reply-channel status, an opaque handle with a user-visible `close()` / `free()` method, or a thread-local last-error slot. | Return owned strings instead of internal pointers, expose thread-local last-error APIs, surface ask submission failure directly, cancel select losers, document who frees what, and when a stdlib handle exposes manual `close()` / `free()`, keep that as the only release path unless the lower layer is provably idempotent and regression-tested against double free. Audit every Hew call site before removing an `impl Drop`, then add Hew-level tests that exercise explicit release followed by scope exit. When a resource owns a write buffer, `Drop::drop` must distinguish observable flush failure (callable via explicit `Closable::close()` returning `Result<(), CloseError>`) from silent auto-cleanup. Document the silent-drop contract on the type's public docstring so users know they must call `close()?` explicitly to observe flush errors (`hew-cabi/src/sink.rs:160-163`). For C ABI release functions called from `Drop` impls (such as `hew_actor_demonitor` and analogues): specify whether each is idempotent before shipping; document that the unknown-id, already-exited, and double-call paths all return `Ok(())`/zero without panicking or producing spurious messages; pin the contract with discriminator regression tests covering zero-guard, unknown-id scan, double-call, and stale-ref paths. Thread-local last-error slots (`LAST_ERRNO` and analogues) must be cleared on the success path, not only set on the failure path; a stale errno from an earlier failure that persists across a successful call is a silent false-error channel. Call `hew_clear_error()` (runtime LAST_ERROR) and `hew_cabi::sink::take_last_error()` (cabi LAST_ERROR/LAST_ERRNO) unconditionally before returning on the success branch when the runtime function wraps a cabi-layer call; do not use `set_last_error_with_errno("", 0)` as a clear because that stores `Some("")` rather than `None` and leaves the string representation wrong. For C-ABI handles that are closed/released by callers (not by `Drop`), guard against double-free UB using the leak-on-close pattern: wrap the inner resource in `ManuallyDrop<T>` alongside an `AtomicBool released` inside a `#[repr(C)]` outer struct; on close, `swap(true, AcqRel)` — if the old value was `true` return `SendError::DoubleClose` (= 4), otherwise call `ManuallyDrop::drop` to run the inner resource's Drop without freeing the outer allocation. The outer allocation leaks permanently; this is the intentional tradeoff — freeing it would cause UAF on the second call. For consuming split operations (e.g. `into_send_half`), use `ManuallyDrop::take` to move the inner value out without running Drop. All handle structs in a C-ABI boundary must have `#[repr(C)]` consistently. | PR #1281/#1314; issue #1310 (`http.Request`/`json.Value` explicit-release migration); PR #1727 (`hew_actor_demonitor` silent-Ok idempotence); PR #1728 (errno-clear on success path); fix/duplex-double-close-guard (leak-on-close `ManuallyDrop`+`AtomicBool` for `hew_duplex_close`/`hew_lambda_actor_release`). |
| `stdlib-borrowed-param-return-guard` | A stdlib function takes a borrowed `String` or bytes-like parameter and can return that value, or a slice/derived alias of it, as the function result. | Until compiler ownership analysis proves the return is a safe move or borrow, make every such return path produce a fresh owned allocation (`"" + param` for `String`), audit sibling branches in the same function for direct parameter returns, and add Hew tests that pass heap-built inputs so the runtime drop path is exercised. | PR #1765; issue #1756. |
| `raii-null-after-move` | Adding drops, auto-close behavior, or ownership transfer for owned values. | Store owned handles in dominating slots, null them after consuming calls, returns, match destructuring, or explicit close, null-check before drop, and classify consumers by the runtime-visible function name (not a rewritten alias). A terminal consuming method must be REGISTERED into the checker's consume set so the receiver lowers with `IntentKind::Consume` (move-checker marks `Consumed` → MIR suppresses the duplicate scope-exit drop): a `#[resource]` type's inherent `close(self)` registers keyed on the **resource marker** (the bare inherent `close` is NOT a trait impl, so the `Closable::close` trait-walk never matches it); a `Closable::close` registers when the trait loads. For a method that **rewrites to a runtime symbol** (`MethodCallRewrite::RewriteToFunction`), the receiver's `IntentKind::Consume` is derived in HIR from `RuntimeCallFamily::consumes_receiver` (the catalog), NOT from the checker's `method_call_consumes_receiver` side-table — these are TWO authorities that must agree. A method whose checker path marks the call consuming (e.g. a Duplex `.send_half()`/`.recv_half()` extraction that moves the unified handle out) will STILL lower the receiver as `IntentKind::Read` — leaving the parent handle in the scope-exit drop set to double-close a direction the extracted half now owns — unless its `RuntimeCallFamily` is ALSO listed in `consumes_receiver`. When adding a consuming runtime-rewrite method, update the family catalog's `consumes_receiver` set (and its literal-anchor parity test), not only the checker side-table. Restrict the match to by-value `self` (a `var self`/mutable-receiver method is in-place mutation, not an ownership-transfer move). NOTE the rejection layer: a `#[resource]` struct whose fields are all `Copy` is structurally `Copy` to the checker, so `mark_expr_moved_if_non_copy` is a no-op and no checker-level `UseAfterMove` fires — the use-after-close is rejected at MIR (`UseAfterConsume` via the `AffineResource` value-class); assert the MIR-level rejection + a `drop_plans`-level resource-drop-exclusion, not a checker `UseAfterMove`. For container consuming calls (`Vec::push` and friends), null the source slot after the consuming op when the element type has a non-empty drop function and the argument is a bare identifier — but see `container-ingress-ownership-is-per-container`: the null-after-move is correct only for MOVE-ingress containers. When hoisting a guard slot for a parameter/handler receiver, place the null-init at the owner block's entry, never at the consuming-call site, so the store cannot precede the slot's defining op. KNOWN GAP (`cleanup-all-exits` territory): a handle consumed on ONE branch is `MaybeConsumed` at the join, but `mark_binding_moved` removes it from `owned_locals` path-insensitively at the consume site, so the not-consumed branch leaks (the implicit drop never fires) — affects every consume mechanism (`#[resource]` close, `Closable`+`Drop`, channel handles); a correct fix keeps the binding in `owned_locals` and lets the per-exit `MaybeConsumed`-aware filter narrow it with a runtime closed-flag guard. | Stream/sink RAII rollout and parameter-drop follow-up; PR #1697 (Vec::push null-after-move); #1295 (`fix/resource-close-consume-drop`): `#[resource]` inherent `close(self)` registered into the consume set keyed on the resource marker → unconditional double-close fixed (use-after-close rejected, single close); conditional-branch `MaybeConsumed` leak surfaced as a pre-existing shared-machinery gap. |
| `drop-kind-classification-runs-every-ritual` | A drop-kind classifier routes an owned value to a teardown path chosen for ONE of its properties (it owns heap → free the bytes) while the value ALSO carries a second teardown obligation (a `#[resource]` RAII `close()`, a registered finaliser) the chosen path does not run. Fires when a value matches more than one drop-relevant trait and the dispatch is first-match-wins. | A drop kind selected for the heap-ownership property must STILL run every OTHER teardown ritual the value owes — freeing the bytes is not the whole destructor. A field-bearing `#[resource]` record owns heap (so it is admitted to the owned-aggregate-record set and routes to the recursive `__hew_record_drop_inplace_<R>` thunk) AND owes its user `close(self)`; the thunk that only frees fields silently drops the RAII contract (spec §3.7.3: "close() runs exactly once per value") — and a nested `#[resource]` field is skipped the same way, one thunk layer deeper. Run the user `close(self)` as the FIRST step of the recursive drop thunk, before the reverse-order field teardown (spec §10(d)): close fires, then fields drop, and a nested resource field's close fires through ITS own thunk reached by the field-drop step — so a single recursive change covers outer + arbitrary nesting depth. The close is a side-effect on the external resource, NOT a heap free, so it composes with the unchanged field teardown (each heap leaf still freed exactly once — no double-free). An explicit `o.close()` consumes the value (the move-checker drops it from the scope-exit set), so the thunk close is suppressed there — close fires exactly once. The defect of a SKIPPED ritual is semantic, not a byte leak (the teardown already freed the bytes), so the non-vacuous oracle is the close SIDE-EFFECT firing (pre-fix absent), paired with a no-double-free pin over a genuinely heap-allocating field (`Vec::new()`+`push` moved into the record) under the poisoned-allocator triple. The resource-marker→close-symbol registry must be consulted at EVERY thunk-synthesis point (the up-front pass AND the on-demand tuple/array-element synthesis) or the two diverge on whether close fires. **The single-slot `#[resource] #[opaque]` HANDLE field is the layout-less sibling this recursion does NOT reach**: it classifies as no-op-drop `OpaqueHandle` (not `RecordInPlace`), is EXCLUDED from `resource_record_close` (which keys on a record LAYOUT), and a record embedding it is rejected at MIR admission (W3.029 `value class that MIR cannot lower yet`) — that exclusion IS the leak, one classification deeper than the nested-record case. Close it with a COMPLEMENTARY `resource_opaque_close` registry (opaque-type → `<Type>::close`; builtin C-ABI runtime-descriptor closes excluded) built IDENTICALLY at the MIR admission `Builder` AND at `IrPipeline` so admit-vs-drop cannot drift, routing the field to a new `StateFieldCloneKind::Resource` leaf whose drop calls `<Type>::close` and whose clone is REFUSED (fail-closed in every container, per `unclonable-leaf-fails-closed-transitively`). **Admitting that record MUST ship, in the SAME change, a fail-closed gate refusing BOTH unsupported field operations** — `detect_opaque_resource_field_misuse` scanning `Instr::RecordFieldLoad` (dest type in the registry: `let d = h.dq`, `h.dq.close()`, `f(h.dq)`) AND `Instr::RecordFieldStore` (stored-value type in the registry: `h.dq = src`). A load-only gate is INCOMPLETE — it leaves reassignment as a second silent escape: the EXTRACTION byte-copies the pointer-width handle with NO null-after-move on the source slot, so the `__hew_record_drop_inplace_<R>` thunk AND the extracted consumer / scope-exit drop both free the one context (a double-free, abort under MallocScribble); the OVERWRITE raw-stores over the slot so the OLD handle leaks (its `close` never runs) while the stored value becomes a second owner of the new context (a double-owner). Refuse both (reuse the `OwnedHandleAggregateExtractionUnsupported` diagnostic with an `overwrite` flag selecting the remediation wording) until overwrite-release + source-slot null-after-move land. The general rule: when a fail-closed gate keys on the instruction that READS a dangerous value out of an aggregate, gate the instruction that OVERWRITES it in place too. Construction (`RecordInit`), whole-record move, and the codegen-synthesised thunk never load or store the field via `RecordFieldLoad`/`RecordFieldStore` (the admit oracle proves construction does not trip the store gate), so the auto-drop spine is untouched — only a user projection OR reassignment of the resource leaf trips it. Key the gate on the loaded-dest / stored-value resolved-type NAME against the registry, NOT the MIR local's `is_opaque` flag: `is_opaque` is NOT propagated to a field-load dest (it arrives `false` even for an `#[opaque]` type); the registry is already opaque ∩ resource ∩ user-close, and within a compilation a name resolves to exactly one type (a cross-module short-name twin only over-refuses — fail-closed). | feat(codegen) run user close() on field-bearing #[resource] record drop (gap #58, `feat/v06-drop-elaboration`): `ValueClass::of_ty` classifies a `#[resource]` Named type `AffineResource` (close path), but a `#[resource]` record with an owned field is admitted to `owned_record_drop_allowed` FIRST and routes to `RecordInPlace`, whose `__hew_record_drop_inplace_<R>` thunk freed the heap leaves and skipped `<R>::close`. Fixed by seeding the thunk synthesis with `IrPipeline::resource_record_close` (record name → `<Type>::close`, built in lowering from the resource-marker table) and emitting the close call at the top of `emit_aggregate_drop_inplace_body_with_close` before the field-drop loop; threaded through both `emit_state_clone_drop_synthesis` and the `FnCtx`-side on-demand `emit_aggregate_recursive_drop` UserRecord arm. Pinned by `resource_record_close_leak_oracle.rs` (outer-then-inner close on drop, single-close on explicit close, no-double-free of a `Vec<i64>` field under the poisoned triple, exact zero leaks). Cousin of `raii-null-after-move` (that row: the CONSUME side suppresses the duplicate drop; this row: the IMPLICIT drop must run the full ritual) and `lifecycle-symmetry` (close is the teardown matched to the `#[resource]` setup). `feat/raii1-record-resource-field` (resource-completeness RAII) extends this row to the opaque-handle field — a single-slot `#[resource] #[opaque]` handle excluded from `resource_record_close`, closed via the complementary `resource_opaque_close` registry + `StateFieldCloneKind::Resource` leaf, paired with `detect_opaque_resource_field_misuse` (refuse projecting the handle out of the record AND overwriting it in place; fail-closed until overwrite-release + source-slot null-after-move land). Pinned by `raii1_record_resource_field_leak_oracle.rs` (scope-exit close-once exact stdout, forked-task close-count==1, no-double-free under the MallocScribble triple, exact zero leaks, extraction-via-bind/method rejected, overwrite-reassignment rejected, admit-no-W3.029, actor-shutdown + async-cancel drop-spine reach close). |
| `container-ingress-ownership-is-per-container` | Migrating a container's element ownership to refcounted/header-aware values, or deciding a container's ingress (`push`/`insert`) and the codegen consume-handling for heap-owning elements. Fires especially when tempted to mirror a sibling container's ingress strategy ("do it the same way as Vec"). | The ingress ownership strategy — **MOVE** (store the caller's pointer, transfer ownership, no copy) vs **COPY-IN** (allocate a fresh owned buffer) — is **per-container, derived from the container's *actual producer set*, never mirrored from a sibling**. A container fed only already-owned header-aware values (e.g. codegen passing header-aware Hew strings) uses MOVE: store the pointer, and codegen **must** null-after-move the source so exactly one owner remains. A container with headerless/borrowed/throwaway producers (e.g. `hew_string_split`/`lines`) uses COPY-IN: allocate a fresh owned copy, do **not** free the source, and codegen **must not** null-after-move (the source stays caller-droppable). Mismatching is catastrophic and silent: COPY-IN + null-after-move **orphans/leaks** the moved source; MOVE + no-null **double-frees**. This means the blanket "`Vec::push` ⇒ `nullOutDropSlot`" rule in `raii-null-after-move` is *container-specific* — the drop elaborator must derive consume semantics per container ingress contract, including *conditional* consume (map `insert` consumes the key on a vacant slot but the caller retains its duplicate on overwrite). Document the MOVE-vs-copy-in contract and any conditional-consume at the ingress sites so the drop/move-checker derives it correctly. Add non-vacuous refcount-ladder tests asserting MOVE does *not* bump rc while clone does. For COPY-IN specifically, retaining the source is **not** automatic once function-scope drop elaboration runs: a fail-closed drop-derivation *escape scan* that treats a `push`/`set` element operand as an ownership escape will exclude the retained source from the drop-allow set and silently leak it one-inner-collection-per-iteration in a reused/loop-carried accumulator (the source is byte-distinct from the deep clone the container now owns). Exempt the copy-in element stores (`hew_vec_push_owned`/`hew_vec_set_owned`) from that scan so the source keeps its own scope-exit drop — the clone the container holds is an independent allocation freed by `hew_vec_free_owned`, so the source dropping once is correct, not a double-free. Prove it with a low-vs-high **leak-slope oracle** on a loop-carried accumulator, using **literal strings only** (historically f-string interpolation in a loop leaked ~1 alloc per interpolated value and contaminated the measurement — fixed in v0.6 by recognising the `to_string_<ty>` catalog producers in `is_fresh_owned_string_producer`; literal strings remain the safest oracle input regardless). | W5.011-P2b: vec (`cabffcd3`) chose COPY-IN (it has headerless producers like `hew_string_split`); maps (`e210ecbd`) chose MOVE (codegen feeds already-header-aware strings, ZERO headerless producers — copy-in would orphan the source). Discovery initially recommended copy-in "on the same grounds as vec"; the planner corrected it on producer-set evidence. Resolved for nested-collection Vec elements (#1722, `fix/nested-vec-push-ownership`): `Vec<Vec<…>>`/`Vec<HashMap>`/`Vec<HashSet>` route through the owned-descriptor copy-in ABI and the local-collection drop-derivation escape scan now exempts `hew_vec_push_owned`/`hew_vec_set_owned`, so the retained source drops exactly once — pinned by `hew-cli/tests/nested_vec_push_leak_oracle.rs` (leak slope) + `tests/hew/nested_vec_push_test.hew` (copy-in contents). The plan had assumed copy-in would *automatically* stop the alias-group pass from suppressing the source free; it did not — the escape scan needed the explicit exemption. #2033 (`fix/v06-vec-iter-hashmap-overwrite-leaks`): the conditional-consume the rule names is now MATERIALISED in codegen — `HashMap/HashSet.insert` return an `i1` (vacant=true / overwrite=false); the move-checker still statically consumes the key (suppressing its scope-exit drop) and codegen branches on that `i1` to release the caller's duplicate key ONLY on the overwrite path (`hew_string_drop` for string keys, `__hew_record_drop_inplace_<R>` for string-bearing record keys) — freed exactly once (vacant by the map, overwrite by the codegen release), pinned by `hashmap_overwrite_key_leak_oracle.rs` (slope + vacant/overwrite scribble exactly-once). #1949 (same lane): the `for x in vec` cursor and its source vec are a SECOND escape-scan-vs-source-free seam — `hew_vec_get_str`/`hew_vec_get_owned` RETAIN the element into the loop var, which the body can MOVE into another owner (`for w in words { map.insert(w,…) }`); freeing the source `Vec<string>`/owned-element vec then runs the per-element release over a value the downstream owner also frees (double-free, caught only under MallocScribble — `leaks` reports 0). The boundary is element-class: the for-in source/cursor vec drop is admitted ONLY for `BitCopy`-element vecs (no retain-and-consume hazard); owned/string-element for-in source vecs stay undropped (leak, fail-closed) pending element-escape accounting. Pinned by `for_in_vec_iter_leak_oracle.rs` (BitCopy slope + owned-element-consumed-into-map scribble no-double-free). LESSON: ANY new "free this collection at scope exit" authority must ask whether its elements are extracted-and-consumed elsewhere, not just whether the handle escapes. |
| `overwrite-release-alias-neutralise` | A store site (state-field re-store, slot overwrite, container value replace) gains an old-value release for a value whose loads are byte-copies at refcount unchanged — especially embedded aggregates (records, enums) where the incoming value can alias old heap leaves. | A single pointer-inequality guard only works for single-pointer values (string/bytes/collection handles). For aggregates, neither a whole-value compare (functional update aliases SOME leaves while other bytes differ) nor a per-position leaf compare (swap shapes alias ACROSS positions) is sound. Release per leaf, guarded by comparing the old leaf against EVERY owned heap leaf of the incoming value (enum variants via tag switch into a reserved slot set); neutralise (null) matched leaves and let the existing null-tolerant drop spine remain the sole release authority. Pin with three fixture shapes: functional update (`r = R { a: r.a, n: r.n + 1 }`), whole-value self-store (`r = r`), and cross-position swap (`p = P { a: p.b, b: p.a }`) under the poisoned-allocator triple, plus a low-vs-high leak-slope oracle for the pure-replacement shape. | fix/v050-collection-overwrite-release: `emit_record_overwrite_release_body` / `emit_enum_overwrite_release_body` + `lower_actor_state_field_store` arms in `hew-codegen-rs/src/llvm.rs`; oracles in `hew-cli/tests/state_overwrite_leak_oracle.rs`. Probe evidence: `prof.name` in a record initialiser loads with NO `hew_string_clone` — the byte-copy alias is the common case, not the corner. |
| `silent-leak-on-timeout` | A runtime loop with `Instant::now() < deadline` or equivalent falls through on timeout to "leak until process exit" without a metric, counter, or upper-bound diagnostic. | Every timeout-based fall-through must set a counter, log the leak with diagnostic context (size, kind, count), and ideally refuse further admission once a leak threshold is crossed. The audit pattern: find every loop with `Instant::now() < deadline` and check what happens on the `else` / `break` branch — silent-promote-to-leak is the smell. Pair with periodic metric emission so operators can observe leak rates. | A14 memory-safety audit 2026-05-24. Original site `hew-runtime/src/scope.rs::hew_scope_wait_all` (2s timeout silently promoted Stopping actors to leak-until-exit) — module REMOVED in W2.006; `lambda_actor.rs` `drain_stopped` resolved `9958bb89`; `scheduler_wasm.rs` unbounded sleep queue outstanding. |
| `alias-byte-copy-not-semantic-clone` | `ptr::copy_nonoverlapping` (or any byte-level copy) of a buffer that contains owned-heap pointers (Vec/String/HashMap/HashSet/Bytes/Arc/Box/etc.), producing two-pointers-to-one-allocation aliasing. | A byte-copy across an ownership boundary requires a paired **semantic-clone** callback — a `state_clone_fn` / equivalent vtable slot symmetric to any `state_drop_fn` / equivalent already present. If you have `_drop_fn` for the buffer kind, you must have `_clone_fn` too; if neither exists, byte-copy is fine only when the buffer is plain-old-data. The C-ABI convention for "seed bytes" parameters that admit owned-heap shapes is: either reject heap-bearing shapes at the boundary OR require both drop+clone vtable slots be set. | A14 memory-safety audit 2026-05-24. C1 supervisor restart UAF (`supervisor.rs`/`actor.rs::deep_copy_state`) byte-copied owned-heap state; checker-reject defence at `1be15938`; the `state_clone_fn` vtable slot is the architectural fix. Audit `deep_copy_state` and any future C-ABI "seed bytes" param admission. |
| `thread-backed-handle-leak-invisible-to-detector` (historical — see `deferred-reply-channel-single-reaper-typed-drop` row 155 for the current generator-teardown oracle) | Reasoning about whether a leak is "fixed" for a runtime handle that genuinely owns an OS thread, an fd/socket, or any off-heap resource whose context is reachable from a live worker (task/actor scheduler handles, transport connections), using `leaks --atExit` / `detect_leaks` / valgrind exit-success as the oracle. | A `leaks --atExit` clean report does NOT prove such a handle was released: while the worker thread is alive, the context Box stays reachable from the thread's stack, so the detector sees it as live, not leaked — even when no `hew_*_free` ever runs and N threads + N contexts accumulate. The authoritative exactly-once oracle is the **release-symbol drop count in the lowered IR** (`--dump-mir checked`/`elab` for inline `Instr::Drop` + scope/function-exit plans; the LLVM `.ll` for synthesized composite drop thunks), paired with `hew run` as a no-crash/no-double-free negative control. Assert the drop is emitted on EVERY exit edge of the declaring scope — normal back-edge AND `break`/`continue` AND function-exit — because a per-iteration handle declared in a loop body leaks once per skipped/early-exited iteration if any edge is missed, and that loss is exactly the kind `leaks` cannot see. The function-exit LIFO drop alone is insufficient for a loop-body handle: it releases only the final slot content. Does NOT apply to the generator's own suspension state since the stackless-coro cutover: a suspended generator (and a suspended actor `await`/scope-join) parks a heap coro frame (`HewCont`/`cont.rs`), not a live OS thread holding a `*mut HewGenCtx` — `leaks --atExit` CAN see that frame (row 155's extension). | feat/generators-completion (W3.053), on the pre-cutover thread-runtime generator: `ty_contains_heap_owning` missing the `Generator` arm let a `(Generator,i64)` tuple skip its member-drop, and `let g = gen()` in a `while` never freed per iteration — both reported "0 leaks" under `leaks --atExit` while leaking N threads + N contexts; the real fixes (scope-generator drops on block + loop back-edges + break/continue edges, `Generator` arm in the composite drop thunk) are proven by dump-mir drop-COUNT oracles, not the detector. |
| `free-site-provenance-and-asan-coverage` | A free site is classified by a source-embedded marker, an allocator/free-pairing sweep flips producers (e.g. routing C-string producers through a header-aware allocator), or any change alters which `free`/destructor pairs with a given producer. | Verify the marker's *stated* producer against the producer's *actual* allocation site — a marker can mislabel a raw `libc::malloc` producer as header-aware (or vice versa), and a sentinel-guarded free turns that mislabel into a hard abort or an interior free of `base+offset`. The producer's own crate tests are the authoritative pairing source, never the embedded comment. Every flipped free site must be exercised under ASan **including integration-test binaries**: `cargo test --lib` does NOT compile `tests/*.rs`, so an interior-free / allocator-mismatch reachable only from an integration test (or example/bench harness) is invisible to `--lib` ASan runs. Validate allocator/ABI/free changes with full `cargo test -p <crate>` plus `--test <integration>` under ASan, not `--lib`. When one free helper serves both header-aware and raw-libc producers, split it so each call site is unambiguous, and refresh stale public "free with `free()`" doc comments to the post-flip contract. | header-aware C-string flip (`6488edc4`): a marker labelled `hew_stream_last_error` "str-open" but it allocs via raw `libc::malloc`, so the sentinel-guarded free would SIGABRT. `hew-runtime/tests/ffi_boundary.rs` (integration binary, EXCLUDED by `--lib`) freed header-aware `hew_string_concat` results (data = `base+16`) via raw `libc::free` → interior free; caught only by the security review, missed by both implementer and functional reviewer `--lib` ASan runs. Fixed via a `free_cstr`→`free_hew_string` provenance split; validated `cargo test -p hew-runtime --test ffi_boundary` under ASan. **Extension — bridge `-> *mut c_char` returns (`feat/v06-dist-3-codec`, 2026-06-25):** a NEW runtime FFI fn returning a header-aware `malloc_cstring` string (the wire JSON/YAML bridge `hew_wire_cbor_to_text` + the `out_err` of `hew_wire_text_to_cbor`) is the SAME contract — its tests must free via `free_cstring`/`hew_string_drop`, never `libc::free`, or the unit test SIGTRAPs on the interior free of `base+16` (caught by running the new tests single-threaded; the harness's end-of-run reaping surfaced it). The Hew-side `string` slot drops these correctly because codegen types the result as `string` (routed through `hew_string_drop`), and a STATIC-string global stored as a Result `Err` payload is also safe (drop skips it via `is_static_string`). |
| `static-classification-vacuates-refcount-and-sanitizer` | A retain/release (refcount, COW, drop) path short-circuits to a no-op when a *classification predicate* says the pointer is non-owned — e.g. "is this a static/interned/arena/borrowed pointer?" — AND that predicate depends on platform/loader details (image segment bounds, address ranges, tag bits). Also fires whenever a sanitizer run is the validation evidence for refcount/free correctness. | A misclassification that returns "static/borrowed = true" for a *heap* allocation makes clone AND drop both no-ops, so the refcount substrate is silently INERT — and because no clone/drop executes, no double-free/UAF/leak is *possible*, which makes the sanitizer pass **vacuously green**. Green ASan on a refcount change is only meaningful if clone/drop actually executed on the tested allocations. Three mandatory checks: (1) the classification predicate must classify genuine heap allocations as non-static on **every** target platform — pin a per-platform regression test that allocates on the heap and asserts `is_static == false` (and that the static window excludes loader artifacts like Mach-O `__PAGEZERO` / zero-vmaddr segments); (2) before trusting a sanitizer-green as proof, assert the path under test was actually *exercised* — e.g. a positive test that the refcount visibly bumps `1→2` on clone and frees at zero on final drop, so an inert path fails loudly instead of passing silently; (3) treat any prior "green" sanitizer evidence gathered while the path was inert as VACUOUS and re-validate once the path is live. Fail-closed: if the platform window can't be computed, `assert!`/abort rather than defaulting to an all-inclusive (everything-is-static) range. | macOS `__PAGEZERO` bug (fix `09629b6d`): `hew-runtime/src/string.rs` `static_string_bounds()` took `lo=min(vmaddr)` over `LC_SEGMENT_64`; `__PAGEZERO` (vmaddr 0, vmsize 4GB) set `lo=0` → a ~4GB static window swallowed all heap strings → `is_static_string()`=true → `hew_string_clone`/`hew_string_drop` were no-ops on macOS arm64, making ALL prior macOS ASan validation of the refcount path VACUOUS. Fix excludes `__PAGEZERO`/zero-vmaddr segments + fail-closed `assert!` + regression tests asserting heap strings classify non-static and clone bumps rc `1→2`. |
| `leak-on-insert-not-before-dedup` | A "register once per key" side table interns/`Box::leak`s a fresh `&'static` value, OR commits any other irreversible side-effect (leak, global insert, fd dup, counter bump), and the dedup/first-wins decision is keyed downstream of where the irreversible step runs — especially when the registrant fires once-per-*use* (per spawn / per call) but the table dedups once-per-*type*/key. | Do the irreversible step **only on the committing branch**, under the same lock/decision that dedups — pass the value by-move and `Box::leak`/insert inside the `or_insert_with`/vacant arm so a losing or repeat caller drops (frees) its copy instead of orphaning it. Leaking before the `.entry(k).or_insert(v)` check orphans one allocation per repeat call (`&'static`/Copy refs are not dropped by `or_insert`, so the pre-leaked box is unrecoverable). This leak is LATENT: it accumulates silently until a code path reaches a quiescent, clean exit (e.g. a cooperative suspend that resumes and tears the actor down) where a leak detector can attribute it; a blocking/never-quiescing predecessor masks it entirely. When a new clean-exit corpus (a suspend/resume fixture, a graceful-shutdown test) lands, run it under LSan/`leaks --atExit` on a **repeated-key** shape (spawn the same type N times) — the slope (N−1 leaks) is the tell; a single spawn hides it. macOS `leaks` rounds the boxed-str up to a 16-byte bucket while Linux LSan reports the exact byte count, so the two report different sizes for the same object — match by object COUNT and call site, not byte total. | `fix(profiler): leak actor type name once per type, not per spawn` (W60.015): `hew_actor_register_type` eagerly `Box::leak`'d the type name before `register_dispatch_type`'s dispatch-pointer dedup, orphaning one boxed `"Sleeper"` per repeat spawn; surfaced only once the cooperative-`sleep_ms` suspend corpus gave a clean quiescent exit (`many_handlers_each_sleep_then_resume`: 2 leaks / 14 bytes under Linux LSan, 32 bytes under macOS `leaks`). Fixed by taking the name by-value and `Box::leak`ing inside `or_insert_with`. |
| `deferred-reply-channel-single-reaper-typed-drop` | A deferred-delivery channel (ask reply slot, duplex/stream reply) byte-copies a delivered owned payload (String/Bytes/Vec/HashMap/HashSet/Closure, or a record/enum/tuple with an owned leaf) into a buffer the waiter consumes LATER, so the producer's copy and the channel's copy alias one allocation — AND the consume leg can be skipped (await-deadline/timeout, select-loser, explicit cancel, actor-shutdown, or alloc-failure before delivery). | The channel must own a registered typed destructor (a `reply_drop_fn` fn-pointer slot, symmetric to the eventual consume-side drop) and run it as the **single canonical reaper** on EVERY non-consume teardown leg — never-consumed, cancelled-before-delivery, AND alloc-failure — gated on the not-yet-consumed sentinel: consume nulls `value`, so the dtor fires iff `value != null` at final free (consume XOR teardown drops, never both; double-cancel is idempotent because `value` is already null). Codegen is the only place that knows the reply type `R` at each ask site, so it MUST register the dtor fail-closed right after channel construction, before any reply can deposit: bit-copy/user-handle `R` → null (buffer-only free, the prior behaviour), composite `R` → the already-seeded in-place drop thunk, leaf-owned `R` → a synthesised `{ R }`-wrapper drop reusing the canonical aggregate-drop emitter; an owned `R` the classifier cannot map is a hard `CodegenError`, **never a silent null** (a silent null reinstates the exact leak). The producer-side dispatch trampoline must IGNORE the deliver-call's false (not-delivered) return and must NOT free the payload itself — the channel's dtor run is the only drop, else double-free. Mirror on BOTH schedulers (native + WASM) in the same change; a one-sided fix leaks on the other. The authoritative oracle is a deterministic destructor-call COUNTER asserted exactly-once per leg per scheduler (RED→GREEN by neutralising the dtor call), NOT `leaks --atExit` (see `thread-backed-handle-leak-invisible-to-detector`); back it with a low-vs-high leak-SLOPE e2e driver that spawns once and never binds the owned reply (to dodge unrelated consume-side drop gaps) plus a no-double-free probe under the poisoned-allocator triple. Keep the field struct-local — do not fold it into a runtime-handle/reply-table refactor. | fix/reply-channel-ownership (#1739/#1735): `hew_reply` byte-copied a delivered owned reply (aliasing embedded heap) and the never-consumed/cancel/OOM legs `libc::free`'d the buffer with NO typed destructor → embedded String/Vec/HashMap/Closure heap leaked on timeout/cancel/select-loser/shutdown; the declared-actor trampoline also ignored `hew_reply`'s false return, so a naive producer-side free would double-free. Fix: `HewReplyChannel.reply_drop_fn` (native `reply_channel.rs` + WASM `reply_channel_wasm.rs`) run as single reaper on all three legs gated on non-null `value`; codegen `ask_reply_drop_thunk_ptr`/`wire_reply_drop_fn` register `R`'s dtor fail-closed at all 4 ask sites (suspending-ask, suspending-closure-call, select arm, join branch) in `hew-codegen-rs/src/llvm.rs`. Proven by `REPLY_DTOR_CALLS`/`WASM_REPLY_DTOR_CALLS` counter unit tests + `ask_reply_owned_leak_oracle.rs` cancel-slope (pre-fix 20→1168 leaks over 20→2000 iters; post-fix 0→0). Mirror of `alias-byte-copy-not-semantic-clone` (the clone direction — drop+clone are paired); cousins `ffi-ownership-contracts` (reply-channel who-frees), `drop-allowset-from-value-flow` (consume-side sole-owner proof). Out of scope / follow-up: a pre-existing consume-side gap drops bound-but-unused owned match/select-arm bindings late, plus a per-spawn actor allocation leak — both reply-channel-independent. **Extension — generator companion out-slot (`feat/cut-gen-coro`, 2026-06-18):** the SAME single-reaper-typed-drop-gated-on-not-consumed pattern on the GENERATOR side-channel. A `yield` lowers as a MOVE into the companion out-slot during the construction pre-run, and the generic runtime `hew_gen_coro_destroy(*mut c_void)` cannot typed-drop it (it does not know `Y`), so a generator constructed and dropped before its first `.next()` (or any drop while a yielded value is pending) leaked the owned value. Fix mirrors the reply-channel exactly: a `pending` sentinel byte (set from `!hew_cont_done` after the ramp, cleared in `GeneratorNext`'s Some/None arms) + a codegen-registered per-`Y` typed out-drop thunk planted in the companion, run by destroy as the single reaper IFF `pending != 0`; BitCopy `Y` → null thunk, un-wired owned `Y` → fail-closed `CodegenError` (never a silent null). Oracle: `leaks --atExit` here CAN witness it (the value is on the heap, not behind a live worker — contrast `thread-backed-handle-leak-invisible-to-detector`, which applied to the DELETED thread runtime), pre-fix 1 leak/32 bytes → post-fix 0, plus runtime drop-count unit tests (fires once iff pending) + ASan no-double-free. The generic-`void(ptr)`-teardown-needs-a-planted-typed-thunk shape recurs for any runtime-opaque suspension side-channel (generator out-slot, future async-generator/await out-slots). |
| `terminal-transition-before-side-effect-that-spawns-a-racing-terminator` | A teardown path (actor trap/stop, handle close) performs an observable side-effect that can make ANOTHER thread independently drive the same object to a terminal state, and only THEN takes its own terminal-state CAS — with a guard that bails out when the object is already terminal. The canonical smell: `close_mailbox(); loop { if already_terminal { return; } CAS(cur → terminal) }`. The side-effect (closing the mailbox) is itself the trigger for the racing terminator (a worker's "mailbox closed while draining → self-STOP" settle), so the order is a lost-notification race, not a benign reordering. | Take the terminal-state CAS that establishes THIS path as the terminating authority FIRST, before the side-effect that can spawn a competing terminator. Once the object is in this path's terminal state, the racing thread's own `Running → Idle` / `Idle → Stopped` settle CAS fails, so it cannot terminate the object out from under you and steal the notification/teardown work this path owes (supervisor child-crashed notify, link/monitor exit propagation). Run the side-effect immediately after the CAS — it is still correct (new sends are already rejected by the terminal state). The bug is SILENT and order-dependent: when the racing self-stop wins, it reaches a DIFFERENT terminal state via a path that does NOT do this path's notification, the original path reads "already terminal" and bails, and the omission surfaces far downstream as a waiter (supervisor `hew_supervisor_wait_restart`) blocking to its full timeout ceiling — never as a local error. Diagnose by instrumenting whether the notification call ran at all (an EMPTY trace between the waiter's ENTER and its CEILING means the notify never fired, i.e. the teardown bailed at the terminal check), not by assuming the wait/notify condvar lost the wake. Reproduces only under load/coverage that widens the window between the side-effect and the CAS; the fix is validated by the harshest-condition pass (N×100 under load + `cargo llvm-cov` with `--retries 0`), and the matching `retries=N` SHIM is deleted in the same change. | fix/v060-supervisor-restart-wake (#58/#2): `hew_actor_trap` closed the child actor's mailbox BEFORE its terminal CAS; a worker mid-dispatch hit the scheduler `activate_actor` "mailbox closed while draining → IDLE → STOPPED" self-stop, won the terminal CAS ~2.5-8% under `cargo llvm-cov` + load, and the trap then read STOPPED and bailed — dropping `hew_supervisor_notify_child_event`, so the nested supervisor's `wait_restart` reached its 30s ceiling. Fixed by moving the terminal CAS before `mailbox_close` in `hew-runtime/src/actor.rs` (`hew_actor_trap`); proven 200/200 under load + llvm-cov where the unfixed binary failed 5/200, then the `child_supervisor_recovery_recreates_nested_subtree` `retries=1` SHIM removed from `.config/nextest.toml`. Cousin of `monotonic-epoch-single-clock` (both are determinism defects exposed by coverage-instrumented contention); the circuit-breaker single-clock fix (`dda7ea08`) was a sibling symptom on the same test family. |
| `terminal-state-is-not-quiescence-when-published-cross-thread` | A free/reclaim path decides an object is safe to free by classifying its lifecycle STATE (`Crashed`/`Stopped`/`Closed`) as quiescent, AND a DIFFERENT thread can publish that terminal state out from under the thread that owns the object's active critical section (e.g. an external `hew_actor_trap` CAS-ing a still-dispatching actor `Running → Crashed`, erasing the `Running` ownership marker the free path relied on). The owner is still reading the object box / arena / mailbox in its post-operation settle when the free reclaims it. Smell: a quiescence predicate that is a pure function of an atomic LIFECYCLE state (`is_quiescent(state) == state ∈ {terminal…}`), with a terminal CAS reachable from a thread other than the active owner. Symptom is a use-after-free that surfaces FAR from the free — a corrupted/reused node read tripping an unrelated fail-closed guard (here the envelope-mode P5.2 dispatch guard aborting 0xc0000005 on a copy-mode-only test), never a clean "freed twice" at the free site. | The terminal lifecycle state alone is NOT proof of quiescence: it proves no NEW work will start, not that the CURRENT owner has finished touching the object. Gate the free on an explicit OWNERSHIP/critical-section marker in addition to the terminal state — a flag the owner sets BEFORE the publishing CAS that makes the object trap-stealable (i.e. before, not after, the `Runnable → Running` CAS) and clears (Release) on EVERY exit of its critical section via an RAII guard, which the free path waits on (Acquire, spin-until-clear with a bounded deadline → fail-closed: leak/`-2` rather than UAF). Setting the flag AFTER the winning CAS is itself a residual instance of the SAME bug: the object is already in the racing state (`Running`) and another thread's terminal CAS can land in the CAS→marker gap, so the free observes terminal-without-marker and reclaims under the owner. Claim before the CAS so the flag is published the instant the object can be observed in the racing state; on a LOST CAS the owner never owned the object, so it must clear the optimistically-set flag on the early-return path (EVERY failure path clears — otherwise a non-owner leaves the flag set and wedges the free to its deadline). The clear-on-lost-CAS cannot clobber a concurrent winner ONLY because the object is single-owner per epoch (single enqueue per `Runnable` transition + single-consumer deque pop); verify that invariant before using a plain bool, else the loser's clear erases the winner's claim and reopens the gap. The Acquire/Release pair makes observing the cleared flag also publish every write the owner made. This mirrors the existing `terminate_finished` wait. Do NOT try to fix it by having the cross-thread terminator drain/clean the object's queue: the queue consumer is single-consumer (`hew_mailbox_try_recv`), so a cross-thread drain is a second concurrent consumer → corruption, and it does not cover the node already in the owner's hand. Verify the RAII guard is the LAST local dropped (so it clears after all object accesses) AND is claimed BEFORE the publishing CAS (not after the CAS win); verify EVERY CAS-failure path clears the optimistically-set flag; verify a terminal object cannot RE-arm the flag (the activation entry's top-of-fn terminal skip must return before the claim). Distinct from `terminal-transition-before-side-effect-that-spawns-a-racing-terminator` (that row is the ORDERING of one path's own CAS-vs-side-effect for a lost notification; this row is a SECOND thread's terminal CAS invalidating a free path's quiescence assumption). Reproduces only under load/IOCP/coverage timing; prove with the harshest-condition pass (N×100 `--retries 0`) plus a teeth test that races a concurrent free against the owner's settle (trap fires in the CAS→marker gap; the free must wait on the flag) and FAILS under ASan with a heap-use-after-free when the claim is moved after the CAS. | fix/v060-supervisor-restart-wake (#58/#2), `ac39f51f`: after the terminal-CAS-before-mailbox-close reorder, an external `hew_actor_trap` CAS-ed a still-dispatching child `Running → Crashed`; `actor_free_state_is_quiescent` (`hew-runtime/src/actor.rs`) treated `Crashed` as quiescent, so the async supervisor-driven `hew_actor_free` reclaimed the box+mailbox while the owning worker was still in its `activate_actor` settle — UAF surfacing as a corrupted msg-node tripping the envelope-mode P5.2 guard on Windows-IOCP in `child_supervisor_recovery_recreates_nested_subtree` (copy-mode-only test, so no real envelope node could exist). Fixed with `HewActor::dispatch_active` (native + WASM mirror at the same C-ABI offset; layout assert updated) set by an `ActivationOwnership` RAII guard at the `Runnable → Running` CAS and cleared on every `activate_actor` exit; `hew_actor_free_inner`'s quiescence wait now requires `!dispatch_active`. Regression test `activation_owns_actor_across_external_trap_until_settle` (scheduler.rs) fails when the guard is neutered; 100/100 `--retries 0`. The gate's prescribed cross-thread mailbox-drain in the trap was rejected on the single-consumer grounds above. STRENGTHENED by fix/v060-activation-cas-gap (`0eb7ba18`): the initial fix set `dispatch_active` just AFTER the `Runnable → Running` CAS, leaving a CAS→marker gap where the actor was `Running` with the flag still `false`; a trap landing there (`Running → Crashed`) plus the async free observing `Crashed && !dispatch_active` reclaimed the box under the still-running worker — the same UAF in a narrower window. Fixed by claiming the flag BEFORE the CAS and clearing it on the lost-CAS early return (safe-from-clobber because an actor dispatches on at most one worker per epoch). New tests: `activation_claims_ownership_before_running_cas_closes_gap` (races a concurrent `hew_actor_free` against the settle — trips an ASan heap-use-after-free on the flag store when the claim is moved back after the CAS) and `lost_running_cas_clears_optimistic_dispatch_active`; 100/100 recovery + clean ASan/LSan on the lib gate. |

### `ownership-over-locks` — fix lifetimes first, then add the smallest lock surface that remains

- **area**: runtime, concurrency, networking
- **invariant**: Shared-mutable-state correctness comes from clean ownership and causality, not from layered locks. When a protocol writer shares a stream, the lock surface must match the protocol's atomic unit (full frame), not the syscall.
- **why**: A broken lifetime model cannot be rescued by mutexes — at best the locks paper over the next mile of races. Mismatched lock granularity (syscall vs. protocol) admits interleaved bytes mid-frame, which is undebuggable from logs.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `ownership-over-locks` | Shared mutable state crosses threads, actors, or background workers. | Prefer `Arc`, atomics, owned routing tables, and mailbox-carried context, never pass stack pointers across threads, then add the smallest lock surface still required. | PR #784. |
| `split-framer-write-atomicity` | Multiple protocol framers or writers can write to the same socket, fd, or stream. | Identify every write-capable framer over a shared stream, acquire one per-connection operation gate around complete send/read-auto-flush/control-frame operations before any stream write, document lock ordering, and add deterministic short-write coverage that attempts a competing writer. If a close/drop path skips the gate, first remove sibling writers and document that invariant. | PR #1637 (closed #1632). |
| `held-lock-invokes-callback` | A closure is invoked while a global lock (or any non-trivially-scoped lock) is held. | Prefer "extract data under lock, run callback outside" — read what you need, release the lock, then invoke the user closure with the extracted snapshot. Holding the lock across closure invocation invites nested-lock deadlock if the callback re-enters any mutex that another path holds while trying to take this one. The same pattern that `hew-runtime/src/shutdown.rs:401-405` already implements (`std::mem::take` then iterate without lock) is the canonical shape. | A14 memory-safety audit 2026-05-24. Sites: `hew-runtime/src/lifetime/live_actors.rs` `with_live_actor`/`with_live_actor_by_id` invoke `f` while holding the global `LIVE_ACTORS` lock — latent nested-lock deadlock if `f` re-enters an actor mutex another path holds while taking `LIVE_ACTORS`. Canonical safe shape: `hew-runtime/src/shutdown.rs` (`std::mem::take` then iterate without the lock). |
| `bg-thread-mailbox-delivery-toctou` | A background thread (reactor/poller/timer) delivers into an actor mailbox or dereferences an actor pointer it holds across a poll cycle, while that actor can be freed concurrently by teardown. | A by-value liveness check *before* the send is a TOCTOU window — the actor can free between the check and the send. Synchronize detach with delivery via **publish-then-revalidate + an in-flight guard**: the delivering thread publishes the target into a `SeqCst` slot, re-validates the registration is still present *after* publishing (abort if detach already removed it), and the detach path performs the registry eviction synchronously under lock THEN spin-waits on the published guard before returning (so the free cannot proceed while a delivery is in flight). Both guard accesses `SeqCst`; registry accesses lock-ordered; clear the guard on every delivery exit (early-abort and post-delivery). The single-slot guard is sound only if the reactor processes ready fds sequentially. **The detach MUST scrub the actor from EVERY table its registration can occupy, not just the live one.** A registration that lives in a two-stage pipeline — queued in a `pending` add-list, then *promoted* into the live registry by the bg thread on its next drain — is invisible to a teardown that scans only the live registry: the actor frees while still queued, the bg thread promotes the dangling registration with no liveness re-check, and the next readiness event delivers to freed memory. Scrub the actor's `pending` add entries (keyed by stable actor identity) in the same locked detach phase that scrubs the live registry, AND extend the in-flight guard to cover the *promotion* hand-off (publish a promotion guard in the same locked section that pops the add from `pending`, spin-wait on it in detach). Pop the pending queue one entry at a time under the lock so the guard publication and the queue removal are atomic — a bulk `mem::take` re-opens the window. **The re-scrub-after-wait must itself be scrub-then-wait, LOOPED to quiescence — never a one-shot wait-then-rescrub.** A teardown that waits the guard once, re-scrubs the registry, then returns leaves a residual UAF: the bg thread can finish the promotion (clear the guard) and begin a delivery for the freshly-promoted fd in the *same poll cycle* — publishing the delivery guard *after* the wait exits but before the re-scrub — so the detach removes the registration and returns while a send is in flight. The scrub must be ordered BEFORE the wait (so any delivery the bg thread begins afterward re-validates under the lock, finds the registration gone, and aborts), and the loop repeats `wait → re-scrub → re-check` until a scrub observes the key absent from BOTH `pending` and the registry with NEITHER guard set. Termination holds because detach runs synchronously from teardown while the actor is quiescent: no new pending add for the key can appear, so the bg thread can promote only a bounded, shrinking set, and once the last is drained+scrubbed its re-validate fails and it starts no further delivery. **When the readiness edge's whole action is a single atomic state CAS (e.g. a wake that re-enqueues a `Suspended` actor), the publish-then-revalidate guard collapses to a simpler shape: perform the liveness check AND the CAS INSIDE the registry-lock critical section (`with_live_actor`, which holds the `LIVE_ACTORS` lock across its closure) so the check-and-act is atomic — every free path `untrack`s the actor under that same lock before reclaiming the box, so while the closure runs the box cannot be freed, and a stale pointer is dropped not dereferenced.** Only a lock-FREE follow-up that does not touch the actor (push onto the global run-queue) may run after the lock drops, and only because the successful `Suspended → Runnable` CAS already latched the actor out of any racing free (the free path waits for a quiescent state and CASes `Idle → Stopped`; `Runnable` is non-quiescent). Do NOT dereference a raw actor pointer carried on a channel/registration across a teardown edge without this check — nothing nulls such a back-pointer when the referent is freed, and shutdown frees actors in nondeterministic `HashMap` order. **The post-publish liveness RE-validation must ALSO be non-dereferencing for a local actor.** Publishing the `SeqCst` guard does not by itself protect the deref: a detach that runs ENTIRELY inside the snapshot→publish window sees the guard still 0, does not spin-wait, and frees the actor before the delivering thread reaches the check — so a raw `actor_ref_is_alive`-style probe that loads `(*actor).actor_state` is a UAF even though the guard is "in place". Route the local-actor liveness through the same `with_live_actor` membership-under-lock discipline as the CAS wake (a freed actor is reported dead by absence, never dereferenced); reserve the by-value-snapshot probe for REMOTE refs, which carry no actor pointer to deref. **When the readiness edge carries a SEPARATE refcounted object (a read slot, reply channel, or any heap value the delivery deposits into), and the deposit runs lock-FREE after the snapshot, the in-flight guard does NOT protect that object — it gates the ACTOR free, not the sibling's free.** The registration-owned ref + a `Drop for Registration` single-authority release is insufficient: the detach's Phase-1 scrub drops the `Registration` (and its object ref) BEFORE the Phase-2 guard wait, and teardown that destroyed the coroutine first already dropped the creator ref, so the scrub can drop the object's LAST ref and free it while the deposit is mid-flight. The delivering thread must take its OWN independent in-flight ref on the object UNDER the registry lock (in the same locked snapshot that copies the pointer, where the registration's ref proves the object live), and release that in-flight ref on EVERY exit (an RAII guard is the robust shape) — keeping `Drop for Registration` as the authority for the registration-owned ref only. Separately, when attaching a background delivery source to an actor, refuse fail-closed any mailbox policy whose eviction frees a queued node's payload without running the consuming handler (bounded `DropOld`/`Coalesce`) unless the payload carries drop-glue — naive evict-time drop-glue double-frees the handler-consumed happy path. | Reactor delivering socket reads into actor mailboxes, 2026-06-02→06-06. Dekker `DELIVERING_ACTOR` guard + synchronous detach closes the dead-actor-while-registered window (`d7f0d285`; precedent `timer_periodic`). Successive cross-ecosystem reviews peeled each shape: the `Pending::Add` promotion path needed its own `PROMOTING_ACTOR` guard + pending scrub (`9fd1f045`); the one-shot wait-then-rescrub left a residual UAF, fixed by looping phase 2 as scrub-then-wait to quiescence (`7277b66e`); non-blocking `await` made `enqueue_resume` deref a raw freed `caller_actor` back-pointer → routed through the in-`with_live_actor` check-and-CAS (`ef9cf59d`); the resume-mode read-slot snapshot copied a raw pointer with no in-flight retain so the lock-free deposit raced the Phase-1 scrub — `Drop for Registration` as "single authority" WAS the bug, fixed with an independent under-lock in-flight ref + `InflightSlotRef` RAII guard (`6d7d1db9`/`ac01b80a`); read-slot lifecycle symbols moved `stable`→`codegen-stable` (`419c86e7`). Each UAF reproduced under ASan/`MallocScribble` and pinned by a forced-ordering deterministic regression. |
| `lock-protected-lookup-copy-under-lock` | A registry/cache accessor returns `&'static str`/`&T` into a lock-protected allocation and a caller calls `.to_owned()`/`format!`/any retaining copy on the result AFTER the accessor returns (i.e. after the guard has dropped). | A lock-protected lookup that returns a borrow into the protected allocation must perform any retaining copy INSIDE the lock's critical section. Copying after the accessor returns is a lookup-to-copy TOCTOU use-after-free: a concurrent path that frees the backing allocation under the same mutex can acquire the lock in the window between the accessor returning (lock released) and the caller finishing its copy (still reading the freed bytes). "Copies immediately at the call site" is NOT safe — the question is whether the copy is inside the lock's critical section. Route retaining copies through an owned-lookup helper that copies as the tail expression of the accessor closure (so the copy executes while the guard is still live); audit every `lookup_*_by_ptr`-style accessor that returns a borrow for borrow-escape-across-clear; make the `&T` → owned `T` conversion the closure's return type, not the caller's first statement. The `PoisonSafe::access` (and equivalent `Mutex::lock`+closure patterns) shape means the closure return VALUE is computed under the guard but any operation the CALLER performs on that value is post-release — only the tail expression of the closure is inside the critical section. | PR #2107 — `lookup_dispatch_type_owned` copy-under-lock fix; `DISPATCH_TYPE_REGISTRY.access` releases the guard on closure-return so the prior `lookup_dispatch_type(..).to_owned()` call-site copy was post-release. The cross-ecosystem GPT review caught the race two same-ecosystem security passes missed. |

### `monotonic-epoch-single-clock` — a windowed comparison must use the same monotonic epoch that recorded the timestamps

- **area**: runtime, supervisor, circuit breaker, any windowed/recency/duration comparison over monotonic timestamps
- **invariant**: A "is this timestamp within the window?" comparison must derive `now` from the SAME monotonic epoch that produced the timestamps being compared. Two independently-initialized `OnceLock<Instant>` (or equivalent) epochs captured at different moments silently skew under load: a freshly-recorded timestamp may read as "in the future" of a second epoch, causing the window guard to drop it. The structural enforcement is ONE process-wide epoch: a single lazily-initialized `OnceLock<Instant>` that every "duration/timestamp since process start" reads through (`crate::monotonic` in `hew-runtime`), so there is no second epoch to skew against and cross-subsystem timestamps (crash, tracing, supervisor, timers, SWIM) share one zero point by construction. A per-subsystem `static EPOCH` is a latent instance of this defect even before any two are compared — it makes that subsystem's clock independently rebasable. A genuinely instance-local epoch (e.g. a metrics ring whose timestamps are dashboard-relative and never compared cross-subsystem) is the only sanctioned exception, and must be annotated as deliberately local.
- **why**: Fail-OPEN defect — a silently-dropped timestamp makes a windowed count come up short, so a circuit breaker stays closed, a rate-limiter under-counts, or a recency gate passes stale data. Timing-dependent: the skew is usually sub-millisecond (false-green), but under load or coverage instrumentation the two epochs diverge enough to reproduce. Threading `now_ns` from the recording site fixes ONE comparison; collapsing all process epochs to one accessor removes the entire class — a new comparison added later cannot reintroduce the skew because there is only one clock to read.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `monotonic-epoch-single-clock` | A windowed/recency/duration comparison reads `now` from a different monotonic epoch than the one that recorded the timestamps; OR a helper that compares timestamps takes no `now` param and derives its own `Instant::now()`; OR a subsystem declares its OWN `static EPOCH: OnceLock<Instant>` / `get_or_init(Instant::now)` for "duration since process start" instead of reading the shared process epoch — including in a SIBLING CRATE (`hew-std` and friends), where a private epoch is the same defect at one more remove, not a separate concern. | Read every "duration/timestamp since process start" through the ONE process-wide epoch accessor (`hew_runtime::monotonic::{process_epoch, monotonic_ns, monotonic_ms}`, re-exported as `crate::monotonic` inside `hew-runtime`) — never declare a new per-module `static EPOCH`. A crate that already depends on `hew-runtime` (e.g. `hew-std`) reads through the exported `hew_runtime::monotonic`; the dependency edge is the home, so a new clock crate is unwarranted (the cycle that would force one does not exist — `hew-runtime` does not depend on `hew-std`). Pass `now_ns` from the recording site through to the comparison function as a parameter when a single function both records and compares; never re-derive `now` from a second module-level epoch inside the comparison helper. Audit all monotonic epoch sources workspace-wide, not just in `hew-runtime` (`grep -rn "EPOCH\|get_or_init(Instant::now)" hew-runtime/src hew-std/src`): any `static EPOCH` outside the shared module is the smell. The ONLY sanctioned exception is a self-contained instance-local axis (e.g. a metrics-ring `epoch` field whose timestamps are dashboard-relative and never compared cross-subsystem); annotate it as deliberately local. | PR #2039 / a05b6aa0 — circuit breaker failed to open under load (4/200 runs) because `hew_crash_stats_recent_count` used its own `crash.rs` epoch while `circuit_breaker_record_crash` recorded timestamps against the `supervisor.rs` epoch; the skew caused freshly-recorded crashes to read as "future" and be silently dropped; point-fixed by threading `now_ns` from the recording call site into the count function. Root cause removed in 4d84052b (CAP-09): six independent process-clock epochs (`io_time::monotonic_ms`, `swim_driver::real_now_ms` — which falsely claimed to reuse io_time's epoch, `lib.rs` wasm `hew_now_ms`, `tracing::monotonic_ns`, `crash::monotonic_time_ns`, `supervisor::monotonic_time_ns`) collapsed into one `crate::monotonic` `OnceLock<Instant>`; crash's never-zero `+1` and tracing's ns precision preserved at the call sites. The seventh — `hew-std`'s `hew_datetime_now_nanos` private `static EPOCH` (issue #2060) — was folded into the same epoch via the exported `hew_runtime::monotonic::monotonic_ns`, with `now_nanos_shares_the_runtime_process_epoch` (`hew-std/src/time/datetime.rs`) priming the shared epoch, sleeping, and asserting the datetime reading reflects the slept gap (it reads ~0 from a fresh zero point on the unfolded body). The `profiler::metrics::MetricsRing.epoch` was left as the sanctioned instance-local exception (ring-relative dashboard axis, never cross-compared). |

## P1 — Parity, tests, diagnostics, and toolchain trust

### `parity-or-tracked-gap` — every user-facing surface ships in matching shape on every target, or names the gap

- **area**: native/wasm runtime, specs, stdlib surface, REPL/CLI/eval
- **invariant**: User-facing behaviour must match across native and WASM targets, and across CLI/REPL/eval entry points. Spec text and `pub fn` signatures must describe the shipped surface, not aspirational or ABI-typed names. Where parity cannot land yet, it must be a named tracked gap.
- **why**: Surface drift is the cheapest way to ship two compilers under one name. Users who learn the spec, then hit the runtime, then hit the second target should see the same shape every time.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `native-wasm-parity` | A runtime, scheduler, timer, channel, or actor behavior changes. | Implement both lanes or add a named TODO, add contract tests for timeout, cancel, and budget edges, and document intentional divergence where parity cannot land yet. For session-lifecycle hooks: `session_reset` must be called from both `hew_sched_shutdown` paths (`scheduler_wasm.rs` and `scheduler.rs`) so cleanup fires symmetrically. `task_scope` is absent on WASM today (`WASM-TODO(#1451)` at `task_scope.rs:782-783`); runtime cleanup paths that rely on scope cancel or structured concurrency must explicitly account for this gap — actor terminate callbacks are the only WASM-safe teardown path until #1451 closes. New admitted constructs in the sandbox compiler (`hew-sandbox-wasm`) MUST add a `REQUIRED_PARITY_TEST_NAMES` entry in the SAME commit (`hew-sandbox-wasm/src/lib.rs`), with a compiled-and-run parity case under `HEW_SEED=42` asserting matching stdout and exit code; alternatively, pin as explicitly unsupported with a diagnostic in `tests/unsupported-gates.test.mjs`. Security-sensitive native rejections (e.g. `PlatformLimitation` for `crypto.random_bytes` on wasm32) MUST carry explicit parity coverage — a silent sandbox compilation success where native rejects is a security gap, not a NYI gap. | PR #818/#787/#785/#754/#729; PR #1271; grounding doc 2026-05-08 async-cancel×closable investigation. PR #2144 (chore/sandbox parity with native generics + crypto rejection, 2026-06-22): `crypto.random_bytes` compiled without error in the sandbox while native correctly emitted `PlatformLimitation`; three new `REQUIRED_PARITY_TEST_NAMES` entries (`generic_aggregate_eq`, `option_result_methods`, `display_scalars`) locked in coverage so future regressions are caught at CI. |
| `spec-surface-alignment` | A spec example, API signature, or stdlib module uses a removed alias (`int`/`uint`) or mixes explicit widths inconsistently. | Use explicit-width integers (`i64`, `u64`, `isize`, `usize`) in all Hew source. `int`/`uint` are removed and produce a compile error with a suggestion. Verify examples against `hew-types/src/check/registration.rs`, `hew-types/src/check/methods.rs`, and the owning stdlib module; see `docs/stdlib-style-contract.md` for the full contract. | JOURNEY 2026-04-10 docs wire codec lane; alias removal. |
| `shared-user-surface-paths` | Two user-facing entry points do almost the same thing. | Reuse shared file or session execution, align import roots and diagnostic envelopes, and add end-to-end coverage at the public command level rather than only unit-level helpers. | PR #816/#804/#803/#800/#806. |
| `one-construct-one-lowering-shell` | A language construct (generator/`gen`, closure, machine, `await`, **a generic call**) appears in two or more syntactic positions (standalone fn vs actor `receive` handler vs block expression; **a bare-identifier callee vs a module-qualified `module.fn(...)` callee**) and each position has its own HIR/MIR lowering arm OR its own type-checker body-setup arm. | Both positions MUST route the body through the SAME shell — at lowering (push the same enclosing context onto the same stack, wrap in the same IR node; **seed the same monomorphisation side-tables**) AND in the type checker (shape `current_return_type` / `in_generator` identically before checking the body), or the position that forgot a step diverges at that layer while the other works. A direct call to a generic free fn is one such construct: a bare callee parses as `Expr::Call`→`lower_regular_call`→`record_monomorphisation`, but a `module.fn(...)` callee parses as `Expr::MethodCall`→`lower_method_call`'s `RewriteModuleQualifiedToFunction` arm — a DIFFERENT arm that must perform the SAME per-instantiation seeding (insert the `MonoKey`, seed `call_site_type_args[site]`) or the qualified-callee position falls through to the MIR "function call" `E_NOT_YET_IMPLEMENTED` while the bare position works. Extract the shared registration tail into ONE helper both arms call (no third special-case), and make `MonoKey.origin_name` equal the emitted `BindingRef.name` so the registry `mangled_name` and the MIR re-mangling spine agree. A `gen fn` and a `receive gen fn` are the same construct: `lower_generator_fn_body` pushed the declared Yield type onto `generator_yield_tys` and wrapped the body in `HirExprKind::GenBlock`; the actor path (`lower_actor_receive_fn`) did neither, so every `yield` in a `receive gen fn` hit an empty stack ("yield expression has no enclosing generator yield type") and MIR bailed with an UnsupportedNode "separate lane" diagnostic. Mirror the shared shell (new `lower_actor_generator_body`), then lower the handler as a generator (`is_generator: true`, generator-typed MIR return) so it routes through the existing `GenBlock`→`Terminator::Yield` state machine — the handler becomes a `MakeGenerator` shell + sibling `__hew_gen_body_*`. The SAME asymmetry recurred in the type checker and failed OPEN: `check_fn_decl` stores `current_return_type = Generator<Yield, Unit>` (registration wraps a standalone gen fn as `Ty::generator(declared, Unit)`), so `Stmt::Return` extracts the Unit Return component and rejects `return <T>;`; but `check_actor_receive_fn` registered the handler as `Ty::stream(declared)` and stored the bare yield type, so `as_generator()` returned `None`, `return <T>;` was checked against the bare yield type and SILENTLY ACCEPTED (value dropped) while a valid bare `return;` was wrongly rejected.
