Fix: shape `current_return_type` as `Ty::generator(yield_ty, Unit)` in the actor path too, so `Stmt::Return` (Unit) and `synthesize_yield` (Yield) both extract from the same generator shape as standalone. When a construct fails OPEN at typecheck (accepts a dropped value), it is more dangerous than a fail-closed lowering gap — the body emits and miscompiles silently. Where the second position's full semantics can't land yet (here: the consumer-side `actor.gen()`→per-call channel-backed `Stream<T>` dispatch bridge, and generator bodies that read actor state), keep it a NAMED fail-closed gap (NotYetImplemented at the call site, handler stays out of the message-dispatch layout), never a silent miscompile. Prove the producer survives real codegen with `hew build --emit-obj`, not just `hew check` (codegen-front). | actor `receive gen fn` yield lowering + return-type enforcement (v0.5.3): mirrors the root↔imported asymmetry in `imported-impl-method-lowering-parity`. Cross-module generic free-fn direct call (v0.6): the `RewriteModuleQualifiedToFunction` arm registered no monomorphisation, so `module.first([1,2,3])` hit the MIR "function call" NYI while a bare `first([1,2,3])` worked; fixed by extracting `register_free_fn_monomorphisation` and calling it from both arms. |
| `cross-layer-name-gate-agreement` | A checker AND a downstream IR pre-pass (HIR/MIR) both gate on a method or identifier NAME — a reserved-name special-case like `.send` — where the correct behaviour depends on a CONTEXT discriminator (e.g. `await`-position → ask vs bare-call → tell). | A name-keyed gate duplicated across IR layers must agree on the CONTEXT discriminator, not just the name. Fixing one layer while the other keeps the name-only gate leaves a half-fixed feature: the fixed layer now routes correctly but the unfixed layer re-applies the gate by name alone, breaking the context-sensitive case. The layers must agree on both the name AND the resolved classification. When fixing a name-based misclassification: (1) grep ALL IR layers for every gate on that name (`hew-types/src/check/`, `hew-hir/src/lower.rs`, any MIR pre-pass); (2) for each site, verify whether the gate keys only on the name or also on a structural context (e.g. the direct operand of `await`); (3) confirm that the awaited/ask path lowers correctly end-to-end, not just the simple bare-call case. A cross-eco review that catches the checker fix as incomplete is the expected signal — the HIR gate over-applying by name survives a Rust unit test because the unit test drives the checker, not the full HIR lowering path. | PR #2123 — the checker fix (`has_user_send_handler` guard in `hew-types/src/check/methods.rs`) left the HIR `.send` fire-and-forget gate in `hew-hir/src/lower.rs` over-applying by name alone; an awaited ask (`match await d.send(21)`) failed with `E_HIR: no checker-produced rewrite entry for this method call` until the HIR `Await` arm was split out and the leaf gate skipped for the direct await-operand position. Cousin of `one-construct-one-lowering-shell`. |

### `duplicated-boundary-fact-needs-a-pin-test` — a Rust↔Hew duplicated constant, signature, or enum discriminant is not itself a bug — its ABSENCE of a regression test is

- **area**: `.hew` extern blocks vs Rust `#[no_mangle]` signatures, stdlib catalog FFI declarations, status-code/enum-discriminant literals duplicated on both sides of the language boundary
- **invariant**: Any fact that must stay numerically or structurally identical on both sides of the Rust↔Hew source-language boundary (an extern fn's scalar return/param type, a status-code constant, an enum discriminant literal) needs an explicit, executable pin test — being correct TODAY is not evidence it stays correct, because nothing in the build fails when one side drifts.
- **why**: The three sharp bugs in issue #1884 (UUID FFI type mismatch, JWT fail-open poisoned slot, Ed25519 release-mode buffer risk) were all found as "already-drifted mirrors" — each was a duplicated fact with zero regression coverage, not a design defect. Fixing the instance without adding the class-level gate leaves every OTHER duplicated fact in the same file (and every untouched sibling package) equally exposed; the next drift ships silently again.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `ffi-signature-parity-two-beachheads` | A stdlib catalog symbol or a user-facing `.hew` `extern "C" { }` block declares a scalar (`i32`/`i64`/`bool`) return or param type that must match a Rust `#[no_mangle]` runtime function, OR a status-code/enum-discriminant literal is duplicated as a Hew-side `const`/match-arm literal against a Rust-side constant. | There are two structurally DIFFERENT beachheads, not one: (1) the stdlib catalog path, where both the Hew-facing type and the Rust computation converge inside `hew-codegen-rs` — extend `declare_catalog_ffi`'s existing redeclaration-consistency check into an exhaustive test that groups catalog entries by shared runtime symbol and re-declares every group member through the SAME production code path (`declare_catalog_ffi`), never a hand-rolled parallel computation; (2) the user-facing `.hew extern "C" { }` block path, which crosses a REAL build boundary with no shared crate — pin it with an `include_str!`-based textual parse of the `.hew` declaration line/match-arm literal against the Rust-side value, following `uuid.rs`'s `hew_binding_declares_uuid_parse_returns_i32` shape. The textual-parse technique is inherently limited to scalar/literal ABI facts (`i32`/`bool`/`i64`, status-code literals) — it cannot verify `string`/`bytes`/struct/opaque-handle marshalling; that needs a field-order + field-width comparison technique, a larger and still-unbuilt mechanism. When the Hew-side consumer of a duplicated fact is module-private (a private mapping fn, a private struct like `CronNextResult`), the ONLY place that can exercise it directly is an inline `#[test]` inside that `.hew` module — external `tests/hew/*_test.hew` files cannot reach non-`pub` symbols. Do not build a generated/automatic full-surface scanner as a first move (a materially larger mechanism than extending the two existing patterns) — extend onto the highest-evidence packages first and name the remaining surface as a tracked gap. | #1884 (rc1 slice, 2026-07-02): extended beachhead (1) into `catalog_ffi_symbols_agree_across_all_shared_symbol_entries` (`hew-codegen-rs/src/llvm.rs`); extended beachhead (2) from `uuid.rs` onto `sign.rs`/`jwt.rs`/`encrypt.rs`/`cron.rs` scalar pins, `tls.rs`/`cron.rs` status-code literal pins (with inline `#[test]`s in `tls.hew`/`cron.hew`/`encrypt.hew` for the module-private consumer functions), and JWT HS384/HS512 + cross-algorithm-rejection coverage. Every new gate class was proven red-then-green on a deliberately reverted mutation before landing. Sibling of `ffi-abi-width-mirror` (that core is the specific integer-width-mismatch bug family; this core is the general lesson that the ABSENCE of a pin test is itself the defect, independent of which specific fact drifts) and `ffi-symbol-classification` (that core covers NEW runtime exports; this one covers EXISTING duplicated facts with no coverage). Out of scope / follow-up named at closeout: a full 45-package auto-generated scalar-signature sweep, `websocket.hew`/`quic.hew` enum-ification before their status codes can be pinned, and struct-shaped extern marshalling parity (`TlsWriteFfiResult`/`TlsReadFfiResult`) — none built here; each needs its own dedicated change. |

### `test-discipline` — tests assert the durable contract, run in any order, and trust their runner

- **area**: runtime tests, integration smoke tests, regen checks, runner CLI
- **invariant**: Tests must hold under the full suite in parallel (real isolation, not per-module locking that doesn't cross modules), assert the eventual stable invariant rather than a transient sequence, handshake on cross-process readiness, and run inside a runner that fails on parse errors and exposes timeout control.
- **why**: A test that only passes alone, only passes if the scheduler is fast enough, or hides discovery errors is worse than no test — it manufactures false green CI.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `global-test-isolation` | Tests share globals, phase state, supervisor state, or rely on execution order. | Add reset helpers and test-only serialization or mutexes where needed, run the full suite in parallel, and size the test to the actual race or nesting depth of the bug. When a test in module A touches globals owned by module B, expose a `pub(crate) static B_TEST_LOCK` and `pub(crate) fn reset_b_for_test()` from module B and acquire them in A before touching A's own lock; private per-module locks do not serialize across modules. Lock acquisition order must be consistent across all test sites that hold multiple locks simultaneously. | PR #1257; PR #1271. |
| `concurrent-test-final-invariant` | A concurrent or async test observes lifecycle state or cleanup across a race window. | Allow known valid intermediate states, require the eventual terminal state, and bind race windows to named scheduler or timeout constants at the assertion site. When a test dispatch must remain `Running` until a controlling function (drain, stop) has acted on the actor, use a release-flag spin loop (matching the `DRAIN_BUSY_LOOP_RELEASE` pattern) not a fixed sleep. | PR #813/#738/#751; PR #1484. |
| `network-smoke-readiness` | A smoke test launches a server and client or asserts teardown ordering across processes. | Wait for the server to bind or signal readiness before launching clients, loosen teardown assertions to the durable contract, and document intentionally unordered events. | PR #763. |
| `test-runner-trust` | Discovery, reporting, or timeout behavior changes. | Fail on discovery parse errors, distinguish empty-suite modes clearly, keep stable ordering, and expose timeout behavior through the CLI so it can be tested end to end. | Original LESSONS 2026-03-15 `hew test` pass. |
| `regen-checks` | Adding a `--check`, generator validator, or repo-wide drift audit. | Walk the real input tree, regenerate in an isolated snapshot, diff the produced outputs, and make downstream repo roots configurable so worktrees and fixture repos can run the same check. | Original LESSONS remediation passes. |
| `positional-ratchet-content-binding` | A ratchet or expected-failure list is keyed by an ordinal identity such as `fence-N`, `line-N`, or extraction order. | Bind the key to a content fingerprint and fail distinctly when the content changes under the same key; membership-only checks cannot prove the metadata still describes the item. | NYI-E corpus/docs truth sweep (2026-07-02): removing earlier spec fence failures left later positional IDs with stale labels while the doc ratchet stayed green until checksum binding was added. |
| `check-pass-does-not-imply-run-pass` | An example, doc snippet, or test fixture is "fixed" by adding type annotations, pattern adjustments, or other changes that make `hew check` pass. | After any change that flips a previously-failing `hew check` to pass, run `hew run` (or the equivalent runtime smoke for the surface — `hew eval`, `hew test`, downstream consumer) and verify success. If runtime fails, file the runtime/codegen issue immediately and either revert the check-fix or proceed with a clear comment pointing at the runtime bug. Treat new abort/SIGSEGV/SIGABRT signals on the previously-failing input as serious — those are the bug the type-error was hiding. | PR #1602; issue #1600. |
| `preflight-flake-isolation` | `make ci-preflight` reports `hew check must exit zero` failures spanning multiple unrelated hew-cli e2e files (e.g. `build_args_e2e`, `directory_module_demo`, `diagnostic_source_e2e`, `compile_wasm_parity`, `doc_e2e`) that physically cannot share a code path the just-committed diff touches. | Before treating as a regression, re-run each failing test file in isolation with `cargo test -p hew-cli --test <name> -- --test-threads=1` from a fresh worktree of the same tip. If it passes solo, classify as a parallelism flake under nextest's full-load preflight — not a regression. Skip revert. The root cause is contention under full-parallel cargo+test build pressure, not a code defect. Note for the squash worker: do not run preflight while other cargo processes are active on the same worktree's target dir. | 2026-05-23: a worker reported 15 hew-cli failures post-squash; baseline and postfix probes both showed all 5 file groups passing individually with `--test-threads=1`, and a fresh-worktree full-parallel re-run passed — contention under full-parallel cargo+test build pressure, not a code defect. |
| `leak-evidence-is-the-standalone-binary-not-hew-run-rss` | Validating that a compiler-inserted drop actually frees memory by measuring `/usr/bin/time -l` (or `ps` RSS) of `hew run <prog>`, OR concluding "no leak" from a clean exit under the default allocator. | `hew run` JITs/compiles AND links AND executes the program IN-PROCESS, so its RSS is dominated by the multi-hundred-MB compiler (LLVM + the whole pipeline) — a control with zero allocations and a control that leaks per-iteration read the SAME ~142MB on macOS, so RSS-of-`hew run` cannot distinguish a leak from baseline. Measure the leak on the **compiled standalone binary** (`hew compile` then run the artefact directly), and use a precise leaked-bytes oracle — macOS `leaks --atExit -- <bin>` reports exact leak count/bytes; `n iterations → n leaks` is the unambiguous signal. For double-free / use-after-free, the default refcounted allocator can MASK the bug (a refcount that double-decrements may not fault, and the `free_cstring` poison is best-effort, NOT a reliable double-free guard), so run the falsification under **guard malloc** (`DYLD_INSERT_LIBRARIES=/usr/lib/libgmalloc.dylib MallocScribble=1 MallocGuardEdges=1`) — force-admitting the broken case must FAULT (SIGSEGV) there even when it exits 0 under the default allocator. The honest acceptance is: standalone binary + `leaks` for the leak axis, standalone binary + guard-malloc falsification (broken variant faults, fixed variant clean) for the double-free axis. When the new construct has an already-supported semantic twin (e.g. `for x in xs` vs `for i in 0..xs.len() { let x = xs.get(i) }`), run BOTH at matched iteration counts and **diff the leak counts** — an identical count at 1/1000/10000 elements proves the new path adds zero per-iteration leaks and any residual is shared baseline, separating a feature defect from a pre-existing loop-scope-drop limitation without having to root-cause the baseline. | W5.020 (`7547ffc5`): twice misread the 142MB `hew run` compiler-baseline RSS as a leak before standalone-binary `leaks` gave the truth; the escape-exclusion's load-bearing-ness was proven ONLY under guard malloc (force-admitting an escaping composite exited 0 under the default allocator but SIGSEGV'd 139 under `libgmalloc`). feat/for-in-vec-string-drop: the differential-vs-supported-path technique confirmed new for-in element drops are byte-for-byte equal to the range-for `.get(i)` path (identical leak counts at 1000 elements and the 200×50 stress), isolating the residual as the shared loop-scope-drop limitation, not a regression. feat/mir-field-drop-in-place (2026-07-02): a nested-extraction double-free read **0 leaks** under `leaks --atExit` — the corrupted heap state masked the scan entirely — while guard malloc crashed on the second iteration; a clean `leaks` run alone NEVER clears the double-free axis for discharge-path changes. |
| `substrate-tests-the-substrate` | A test asserts an IR/AST/HIR/MIR shape ("`Instr::Foo` appears", "`HirItem::Bar` is present in the lowered items list", "the side-table has N entries", "the lowered output contains symbol `hew_baz`") without ever compiling AND running the program AND checking observable behaviour at the user boundary. Also fires on tests that assert a derived Display/Debug/Default impl reproduces its input, that assert `assert_eq!(Ty::I32, Ty::I32)` (or any variant-of-itself comparison), that assert "a fresh constructor returns a value with no errors," that mock the SUT and assert the mock returned what it was told to return, OR — for a codegen-EMIT helper — that assert only "the intrinsics were emitted + `module.verify()` is clean" without driving the pass pipeline that CONSUMES them and asserting the transformation actually happened. | Replace or augment the IR-shape assertion with a compile-and-run assertion that exercises the new substrate end-to-end: write a Hew program that USES the lowered surface, compile it, run it, assert observable behaviour (stdout, exit code, side effect, runtime symbol resolution). Delete tautological asserts (`assert!(true)`, `assert_eq!(x, x)`, "constructor returns a value", "Display reproduces its input"). For new HIR/MIR variants or new runtime symbols, the gate to land is an end-to-end probe in `hew-cli/tests/eval_e2e.rs` (or equivalent) that would FAIL if the user-visible surface were broken — not just an `*_lowering.rs` test that walks the IR. For a codegen-emit helper with ZERO production callers (it emits intrinsics a later pass lowers), "emitted + verifies" is NOT enough: run the actual consuming pass (e.g. `run_coro_passes`) and assert the transformation (outlines produced, marker consumed, intrinsics lowered, module still verifies) AND drive the produced artefact through its runtime ABI — a helper that only emits is never proven to lower. If you write a test that "passes by construction" (mock returns what mock was told, or the SUT and the test both wrap the same incorrect logic), do not check it in: it manufactures false green. | Recurring class — an IR/check-only test stays green over a broken runtime path: `Item::ExternBlock` shipped unimplemented with ~7261 tests passing, variant-present but never compiled+run (2026-05-22); f1-veciter's checker-only `check_program`-no-errors test was green while `into_iter()` dispatch failed at runtime (2026-05-31); machine `default {}` passed every shape test but reached no MIR consumer and ran broken/empty (2026-06-02); `coro.rs` `emit_suspend`/`run_coro_passes` passed "emit + `module.verify()`" with ZERO production callers — two latent bugs (module-scope `coro-split` no-op, missing `coro.save`) surfaced only when a pass-driving test DROVE the split (2026-06-05), and a single-suspend probe missed the multi-suspend `.resume`-outline yield edge → SIGSEGV until a two-suspend probe drove it (`79c15931`). 2026-06-12 msgpack `BytesTriple` (#1834): the Rust unit test was green (never crosses the codegen→`bytes` boundary) while the compiled `.hew` path returned a garbage `.len()`; sibling `.hew` round-trips asserting `> 0` PASSED on garbage memory — only the exact-boundary `assert_eq(len, 0)` caught it. Corollary: test the COMPILED `.hew` artefact, not just the Rust crate, AND assert exact/boundary/negative values (`> 0` cannot distinguish correct from uninitialised). 2026-06-14 multi-return final suspend (#1904): a single-`Return` actor-handler coroutine compiled fine while a handler with two-or-more `return` paths emitted two-or-more `coro.suspend(is_final=true)` and aborted CoroSplit ("Only one suspend point can be marked as final", exit 134) — the same single-X-probe-green / multi-X-aborts shape as the two-suspend case; the regression test is a compiled `.hew` exec test driving a >=2-return + `await` handler and asserting exact per-path reply values. |
| `exec-test-must-bound-the-child` | A test compiles and runs a `.hew` (or any) program via `Command::output()` / `wait_with_output()` / `hew run` with no per-process wall-clock bound, OR relies on nextest `slow-timeout` as the only protection. | A new runtime WILL produce fixtures that deadlock (actor recv that never arrives), infinite-loop, or emit unbounded output; an unbounded `.output()` hangs the suite until an outer CI timeout (no useful diagnostic) or OOMs buffering the pipe, and nextest `slow-timeout` is output-INACTIVITY-based so an infinite-OUTPUT program defeats it entirely. Route every exec-test invocation through the shared bounded helper (`hew-testutil`): piped stdio drained on SEPARATE threads, an output-size cap with a visible truncation marker, a wall-clock deadline that KILLS the child's process group, and a return type distinguishing timeout-kill from normal exit so a timed-out test FAILS naming the fixture. `hew run --timeout` alone does NOT protect the harness — the parent's own `.output()` drain must be size-capped (it keeps reading-and-discarding past the cap so the child can still reach EOF). Keep a nextest wall-clock backstop as defence-in-depth. Add a negative test that proves the kill fires (infinite-output child killed within a 3s deadline). When a fixture must compile+link before it runs, the wall-clock bound must cover ONLY the run: do the compile+link out-of-band (`hew build` / `hew compile` via `.output()`, backstopped by the nextest envelope) and bound the prebuilt artefact's execution — binding compile+link under a tight per-run deadline makes the bound trip on runner contention, not on a hang. | exec-harness-timeouts lane 2026-05-31 (`caa87515`): `hew-testutil/src/lib.rs`, `hew-cli/src/process.rs` (production-reachable via `hew run --timeout`), `.config/nextest.toml`; grounding `disco-test-hang-hardening-2026-05-31.md`. |
| `real-timing-quarantine` | A test's assertion irreducibly measures real wall-clock or OS-level timing (signal delivery to a process group, a two-process loopback round-trip, real network smoke) and cannot be made deterministic via the simulated-time seam (simtime is in-process). | Route it into the serialized `real-timing` nextest group (`max-threads = 1`) and exclude it from the `lane`/`smoke` fast tiers so it never gates the fast iteration signal; keep its strict eventual-invariant assertion and any bounded setup-jitter `retries`. Do **not** park a test here that CAN be converted to simulated time — fix it at the root instead (de-flake initiative). Do **not** widen an in-test wall-clock budget to silence a contention flake; that masks the signal instead of fixing it. Keep the `make test-real-timing` selector in sync with the group's membership. | test/bounded-exec-and-real-timing-quarantine (2026-06-12, #1858): the machine execute fixtures moved compile+link to `hew build` out from under the per-run exec bound (native exec is contention-immune); the irreducibly-real `bounded_child_timeout_kills_grandchild_process_group` and the two-process loopback-ask pair were serialized into `real-timing` and excluded from the lane/smoke tiers. |
| `test-determinism-pure-of-seed` | A test's PASS/FAIL can depend on wall-clock, machine load, or thread scheduling: it asserts on elapsed duration (`assert!(elapsed < N_ms)`, `started.elapsed() < ...`), sleeps then reads state, OR waits on signal A as a proxy for event B when A and B run on different, unordered code paths. | A test outcome must be a pure function of `(code, inputs, seed)`. (1) Delete every wall-DURATION assertion — assert the typed logical OUTCOME instead (`AskError::Timeout` not `elapsed < 1500ms`); the operation's own timeout + nextest's slow-timeout are the hang ceiling, never a window. (2) A `sleep(N)` used as synchronization is the smell: replace with a blocking read / `join()` / condvar `wait_for(n, MAX)` that returns the instant the event lands — `t.join()` already proves a peer's RST was sent, so no "give it time to arrive" sleep is needed. (3) CRITICAL — a condvar wait is only deterministic if it waits on the **same logical event the assertion checks**. Waiting on a correlated-but-unordered signal is a causality race: observing a monitor `DOWN` does NOT imply the crash log was pushed (the push runs on the crashing worker AFTER the trap/DOWN, on a different path), nor that the circuit-breaker state transitioned (supervisor-dispatch path). Wait on the asserted event itself (poll the crash count / state to its target with a hang ceiling), never on a sibling signal. A poll-to-target with a generous ceiling is a logical wait (returns on reaching the value); a fixed sleep or `elapsed <` is not. Re-runs/`retries=N` never resolve these — they disguise the defect. The only re-runnable fault is a verified physical-runner break (OOM/ENOSPC/VM-death/network-partition). | fix/v060-test-determinism (2026-06-18): `two_process_remote_ask_timeout_..._under_1500ms` asserted `elapsed < 1500ms` on a 250ms ask deadline (deleted — the `AskError::Timeout` outcome is load-independent); `tcp_stream_backing_records_error_on_reset` slept 20ms "to let the RST arrive" after `t.join()` already guaranteed it (deleted — the blocking `next()` read is the wait); `circuit_breaker_trips_on_repeated_crashes` read `hew_crash_log_count()` the instant the monitor DOWN was observed and fast-failed under load (0.019s) because `push_crash_report` (signal.rs `handle_crash_recovery_impl`, AFTER the trap at line 250) had not run yet — fixed by waiting for the crash count to reach its target with a hang ceiling. |
| `loopback-backpressure-payload-exceeds-autotuned-buffer` | A test proves write-side backpressure (a `WouldBlock`/`BackpressureExceeded` outcome) by writing to a loopback peer that never reads, sizing the payload from a standalone-probe measurement of when a single socket blocks, or assumes `SO_SNDBUF` caps the kernel buffer and forces a timeout. | Loopback sockets on macOS and Windows both use optimised in-kernel fast paths that bypass normal TCP send/receive buffer limits, so neither approach is universally reliable: (1) a fixed payload that overwhelms macOS/Linux loopback (≥ 2 MiB) gets absorbed in-kernel by Windows autotuning within the same timeout, making the assertion false-green on Windows; (2) setting `SO_SNDBUF` to a small value (e.g. 4 KiB) on macOS triggers its fast-path (kernel drains the send buffer into the receive buffer faster than the timeout fires), so the write succeeds and the assertion is false-green on macOS. The correct pattern: use a payload-based approach (≥ 2 MiB payload, default buffers, 100 ms timeout) for the Linux/macOS unit test where it is reliable, gate the assertion with `#[cfg(not(windows))]` with a tracked-reason comment, and cover the Windows backpressure path through an e2e fixture that runs through the actor-model runtime (actor handoff overhead changes the latency profile). Bound the wait with an explicit write timeout. Assert the EXACT error variant, not just a non-zero/Err outcome. | feat/io-c1-tcp-write-backpressure (2026-06-25): first probe wrote 1 MiB — absorbed in-process. Bumped to 16 MiB — passed Linux/macOS but still failed Windows (autotuned loopback absorbed 16 MiB). Tried `SO_SNDBUF = 4 KiB` — broke macOS (fast path absorbed 256 KiB in sub-millisecond chunks; total ~300ms with 100ms per-write timeout, but write_all still returned Ok). Empirical probe: macOS loopback with SO_SNDBUF=4 KiB drained 65 KiB in sub-1 ms (loopback fast-path); without SO_SNDBUF override, payload ≥ 2 MiB is reliably rejected (timeout fires on macOS/Linux but not Windows). Fix: `#[cfg(not(windows))]`-gate the assertion with a clear WHY/WHEN/WHAT comment. Cousin of `substrate-tests-the-substrate` (assert exact/boundary values, not happy-path `> 0`/`Ok`). |
| `admission-gate-is-not-runnability` | A parity/conformance suite enforces correctness over a curated SAMPLE of cases while an admission gate (profile allowlist, capability gate, feature flag) admits a much larger surface — and a new construct is judged "supported" because the gate admits it (compiles, no diagnostic), without proving the construct actually runs at parity. | A fail-closed admission gate proves only that rejected programs are rejected; it says NOTHING about whether an ADMITTED construct lowers and executes correctly — the emitter/interpreter can still trap or silently mis-execute (admitted + unparited + wrong is the most dangerous class). Make the coverage set a **ratchet over the admitted surface, not a sample** — and the ratchet must DERIVE FROM THE LIVE GATE, not a hand-kept list. A hand-maintained "admitted constructs" array that is never cross-checked against the real gate is itself a sample: a construct admitted in the gate with no row still passes. Two mechanisms, both required: (1) **behavioural** — every manifest row carries a minimal probe COMPILED THROUGH THE REAL GATE and run on the real VM, and the cross-check asserts the row's declared coverage matches what the gate actually does (admitted-and-runs-clean → pinned parity case; admitted-and-traps → catalogued fail-loud; rejected → asserts the typed diagnostic). A row that lies about the gate fails the build, so the manifest cannot drift. (2) **structural** — an EXHAUSTIVE `match` over every AST variant (Expr/Stmt/Pattern/TypeExpr/ops) with NO wildcard arm maps each variant to a manifest row; adding a parser variant breaks the build until classified, so a construct cannot enter the language without a coverage decision. The self-verifying trap test (COMPILE AND RUN each admitted-but-trapping hole, assert it genuinely does NOT run at parity) goes red the moment a graduation makes it runnable, forcing its parity case. A silent-wrong-answer hole (admitted + runs + WRONG, exit 0) is worse than a trap and CANNOT be catalogued as NotYetRunnable — fix it or reject it fail-closed; if correct lowering depends on a not-yet-landed substrate (e.g. type-aware numeric lowering), reject fail-closed with a typed diagnostic until that lane lands. Hoist the required-case list into one source of truth both the harness and the ratchet reference. Wire the ratchet into the same gate (`make sandbox-parity`) that runs the parity suite. Prove the ratchet has teeth: temporarily re-open a closed hole and confirm the gate goes red. | feat/sandbox-parity-ratchet (SP-3, 2026-06-14): the first cut hand-maintained an `ADMITTED_CONSTRUCTS` array never derived from `profile.rs`, so admitting a construct with no row + no case still passed — the ratchet's purpose was unmet (cross-eco request-revision). Revised to derive from the live gate: every row's probe is compiled through the real `compile_to_sandbox_bytecode` + run on the VM and the verdict cross-checked, plus an exhaustive no-wildcard AST-variant classification (`mod ast_surface`) that build-breaks on a new parser variant. The empirical audit (compile+run each admitted construct vs native under `HEW_SEED=42`) surfaced ~12 admitted-but-trapping holes invisible to the sample — float arith/negate (G1 float class, i64 ops on f64 → trap), bool `!`, scalar/bool/string `match` (lowered as `enum.tag` → `invalid_enum_tag`), tuple, expr `if let`, `as` cast, postfix `?`, `Some`/`None`, struct-pattern arm, `const` ref, array-repeat, map literal, struct `..base` — AND TWO silent-wrong-answer (G1) holes: compound assignment (`x += 5` lowered as `x = 5`, the emitter ignored `Stmt::Assign.op`) and top-level type alias (sandbox ran it, native `E_NOT_YET_IMPLEMENTED`), both now rejected fail-closed. Also: the "unary negate" parity case used `0 - a` (binary subtract), never exercising `i64.neg` — added real `-a`. Specialization of `substrate-tests-the-substrate` for admission-gate + lowering pairs. |
| `nyi-gap-needs-failable-test` | A discovery, triage, or review CONFIRMS a core-language construct that should work but fails closed (`E_NOT_YET_IMPLEMENTED` / not-lowered / "spine"-style or "not yet lowered" reject) — or worse, type-checks AND builds clean then panics/aborts at RUNTIME — AND no test currently exercises it. Also fires when a fix lane deliberately NARROWS a gap to a clean rejection (an honest check-time gate replacing a runtime crash). | A gap with zero coverage is INVISIBLE: the suite ratchet (`scripts/hew-suite-ratchet.sh`) only tracks tests that already exist and fail, so an untested NYI path re-ships silently — exactly how `gen fn counter(n)` param-reads and enum `==` shipped broken. Do NOT leave a confirmed gap test-less. Add a durable FAILABLE test that runs the natural first-use program for the construct, and register it in the matching expected-failures registry (`scripts/hew-suite-expected-failures.txt` / `scripts/stdlib-expected-failures.txt`, or a paired `.expected` under `examples/ux`/`examples/v05/surfaces` for a diagnostic-quality gate) WITH the root-cause + tracking issue. The ratchet then keeps the failure model visible AND fails the gate the instant the gap is fixed (unexpected-pass), forcing the failable test's promotion to a positive regression guard and its removal from the list. For an honest-gate fix that turns a runtime crash into a clean check rejection, the durable artefact is a `.expected` negative test asserting the EXACT spanned diagnostic. Never delete or skip a gap test to green CI; the registry — not agent memory — is the durable record of unimplemented core features, reviewed periodically to track the system's failure models. | 2026-06-16 user directive (negative/NYI tests must exist so failure models stay visible). Gaps that shipped silently for want of one: `gen fn counter(n)` — `lower_gen_block` never wired params/captures, ZERO param/capture generator coverage; enum `==`/`!=` — `reject_record_comparison` omitted `Enum`, leaked to codegen `E_NOT_YET_IMPLEMENTED: IntCmp lhs is not an integer`, no test; v0.6.0 sweep `HashMap<scalar, ManagedRecord>.values()` and `Vec<record>` range-slice — both `hew check`+build clean then runtime `PANIC`/abort, no test; generic-enum literal payload (`Some(0)`) — checker admits, MIR rejects, no test. Cousins: `check-pass-does-not-imply-run-pass`, `substrate-tests-the-substrate`, `admission-gate-is-not-runnability`. |
| `dump-oracle-pins-the-fact-not-the-format` | A test greps the `--dump-mir` / `--dump-hir` / IR-dump output of a compiled program for a single literal that is actually the derived-`Debug` rendering of an IR node — a variant name (`SuspendingChannelRecv`), a struct-field name, or a `{:#?}` fragment — to prove a lowering decision fired. | The dump renderer is a presentation detail, not a contract: a structured/file-check renderer can replace `{:#?}` with a mnemonic form (`SuspendingChannelRecv` → `suspend.channel_recv`) and the grep silently misses a present fact, failing the oracle even though the compiler is correct. The failure looks alarming (deterministic, all platforms, the assert "X must flip") but the lowering is fine — only the string moved. Match the FACT across every rendering the dump can emit (a small `dump_has_<fact>` helper that ORs the Debug variant name and the mnemonic form), keeping each matched token distinct from the non-flipped/blocking sibling (`hew_channel_recv_layout`) so the paired negative oracle cannot false-match. When a renderer change is in flight on another branch, the oracle on `main` must already accept BOTH forms so it stays green as that branch merges. Cousin of `diagnostic-no-debug-payload` (Debug rendering is unstable across refactors) on the test side. | 2026-06-19 (`187955db`): `actor_await_recv_flips_to_suspending_channel_recv` (and its negative twin `main_await_recv_does_not_flip`) grepped the literal `SuspendingChannelRecv`; passed on `main`'s `{:#?}` dump and 600/600 + 20/20-under-load locally, but failed deterministically on all three platforms on the in-flight MIR-filecheck branch whose new `hew-mir/src/dump.rs` renders the terminator as `suspend.channel_recv`. The flip fired correctly on both branches; fixed by matching either rendering via `dump_has_channel_recv_suspend`. |
| `trap-fixture-two-gate` | Adding a new `tests/vertical-slice/accept/` fixture whose correctness proof IS the runtime trap (OOB access, div-by-zero, shift-out-of-range, assertion failure, unwrap-none). | A trap fixture lives in BOTH of the two CI gates: (1) `tests/vertical-slice/run.sh` calls `run_accept_expect_trap <name>` which accepts exit code 132 (SIGILL x86_64) or 133 (SIGTRAP aarch64); (2) `tests/fuzz-oracle/expected-failures.txt` lists the bare filename so the fuzz oracle's `runtime-crash` classification is treated as expected, not a gate failure. A fixture registered only in run.sh passes the vertical-slice gate but fails `make fuzz-oracle` with "UNEXPECTED FAILURES: runtime-crash `<name>.hew` killed by signal N (SIG…)". A fixture registered only in expected-failures.txt makes the fuzz oracle wait for a signal-death that may or may not happen depending on whether the file is in vertical-slice at all. Update BOTH in the same commit; the count comment in expected-failures.txt must match. Arch-portable exit codes: 132 = SIGILL+128 on x86_64 Linux (ud2 trap); 133 = SIGTRAP+128 on aarch64/macOS (brk #1 trap). Python subprocess reports signal deaths as negative returncode (-4 SIGILL, -5 SIGTRAP) regardless of what bash reports; the oracle classifies `rc < 0` as `runtime-crash` — the expected-failures entry is what suppresses the gate failure. | PR #2025 (fix/v060-assignability-correctness): `vec_index_assign_oob_traps.hew` (OOB write `v[1]` on a 1-element Vec) was registered in run.sh with `run_accept_expect_trap` but absent from expected-failures.txt → fuzz-oracle reported `runtime-crash` as unexpected. Fix: added the entry to expected-failures.txt, updated the count comment. |
| `fixture-delete-cross-crate-ripple` | Deleting, renaming, or flipping the accept/reject status of an existing `tests/vertical-slice/{accept,reject}/*.hew` fixture. | A vertical-slice fixture's bare filename can be hardcoded by an unrelated Rust integration test in ANY crate — not just the two known ratchet gates (`tests/vertical-slice/run.sh`, `tests/fuzz-oracle/expected-failures.txt`) — via `repo.join("tests/vertical-slice/<accept\|reject>/<name>.hew")` and a direct `hew check`/`hew run` invocation asserting on that fixture's old behaviour. Before deleting/renaming/repurposing a fixture, `grep -rn '<bare-filename>'` the FULL workspace (excluding `target/`/`.git/`), not just the two known ratchet files, and update every match in the same commit. This matters more than it looks: on the Linux/macOS CI job, `cargo nextest run --workspace` runs BEFORE `make test-vertical-slice`/`make fuzz-oracle`/`make test-hew-ratchet` in the step sequence, so a stray Rust-level reference failing there aborts the job before any of the later `.hew`-level ratchet steps run — the failure reads as "Build & test" red with no vertical-slice signal at all, and a reviewer who only re-runs the `.hew` suites locally will see them pass and misdiagnose the CI red as unrelated (cousin of `red-required-check-is-a-stop-not-noise`: pull the actual failing step's log, don't trust the job summary). | PR #2477 (fix/hashmap-keys-value-type-gate): deleted `tests/vertical-slice/reject/hashmap_keys_managed_record.hew` and updated `run.sh`, but `hew-codegen-rs/tests/exec/hashmap_keys_values_exec.rs::hashmap_keys_heap_bearing_value_rejected_with_one_exact_diagnostic` still hardcoded that path — CI FAILURE on `Build & test (Linux)`/`(macOS arm64)`, root-caused via `gh run view --log-failed` to `Error: cannot read .../hashmap_keys_managed_record.hew: No such file or directory`, reproduced locally byte-for-byte; fixed forward by deleting the stale test (`8c63181bb`). |
| `debugger-gate-per-target` | A debuginfo or codegen-emission lane verifies its output only with static-IR (textual LLVM-IR) assertions — i.e. the proving gate grepping `.ll` dump text but never attaching a live debugger or running `dwarfdump` on an emitted object file. | Static-IR assertions prove emission structure but cannot prove debugger correctness: variable shadowing, payload size, union variant accessibility, and `optnone` coexistence only surface when a live debugger (lldb/gdb) or `dwarfdump`-on-emitted-object actually reads the emitted DWARF. Add at least one live-debugger or `dwarfdump` e2e per debuginfo lane; cfg-guard it to the targets whose debug-info format is exercised AND document the unsupported ones with a tracked follow-on. Specifically: macOS/Linux use DWARF, Windows uses CodeView/PDB; a macOS+Linux pass does NOT cover the Windows debug-info-format gap — track it explicitly. | PR #2114 (fix/v06-gdb-debuginfo): the live-LLDB e2e (`dwarf_debugger_locals_e2e`) caught 3 defects that the static-IR (`dwarf_variable_dies`) suite had passed: (1) shadowed-name scope — inner variable read wrong value because the lexical-scope table was absent; (2) empty-payload union — enum variant with no payload emitted a zero-sized union member; (3) payload byte size — actual payload struct size in bytes was wrong. All three are invisible to `.ll` text grep. Additionally the Windows DWARF-in-PE gap (DWARF embedded in a PE binary vs CodeView/PDB) surfaced at CI in the follow-up PR #2117, confirming a host-pass is non-evidence for the Windows format. |
| `harness-pathquote` | A debugger e2e test (LLDB/GDB) constructs a breakpoint command or debuggee binary path by string interpolation of a worktree-rooted directory path without quoting, OR generates the debuggee object file at a fixed path rather than a `TempDir`. | Quote EVERY path argument in LLDB/GDB command strings — the `--file <path>` source-path argument and the binary path to load — using `format!("{:?}", path)` or explicit shell quoting. A space in the worktree path (e.g. `/Volumes/Extreme SSD/`) causes LLDB to mis-parse the argument as two separate tokens, so the breakpoint never binds and the test false-fails with no useful diagnostic. Generate debuggee objects in a `TempDir` (not a fixed path) so concurrent test runs don't collide. Capture stderr as well as stdout: LLDB's breakpoint-set failure appears on stderr. When a debugger e2e test fails suspiciously, perform the controlled-bisect check: if a full-revert of the diff on the SAME machine (same spaced path) still reproduces the failure, the root cause is the environment (path quoting), not the code. | PR #2137 (fix/v06-gdb-debuginfo canonical harness fix, 2026-06-22): `dwarf_debugger_locals_e2e` failed across all 4 Wave-1 generics lanes (`G1`/`G2`/`G3`/`G13`) running on an extssd worktree at `/Volumes/Extreme SSD/`; the unquoted `--file <path>` argument caused LLDB to mis-parse the path. A full-revert bisect on the spaced path reproduced the failure on `origin/main`, confirming the environment confound — not G13's Display change. Canonical fix: quote + `TempDir` + capture stderr. All 4 Wave-1 lanes rebased onto the canonical fix rather than each carrying their own redundant harness patch. |

### `diagnostic-trust` — diagnostics carry their attribution, count toward exit, and gates reject only what they claim

- **area**: types, CLI diagnostics, link gates, link-rule expansion
- **invariant**: A diagnostic is owned by where it was recorded, not where it was rendered. A visible diagnostic that doesn't increment the failure counter is invisible to CI. A gate that newly accepts targets must still reject the targets it claims to reject.
- **why**: Attribution that drifts during rendering misleads users to the wrong file. Uncounted diagnostics ship green PRs that contain compile errors. Gates that grow acceptance without re-checking rejection silently widen.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `diagnostic-source-attribution` | Diagnostics may be recorded in one module and rendered in another. | Snapshot `source_module` on immediate and deferred diagnostics, tag unattributed diagnostics after each module slice, and add e2e tests that assert filenames and underlines point at the correct source file. | PR #806. |
| `diagnostic-no-debug-payload` | A CLI exit/render site formats a compiler diagnostic with `{:?}` / `{diagnostic:?}` / `{kind:?}` instead of routing through the shared diagnostic renderer (`render_*_diagnostics` / `render_frontend_diagnostics`). Fires especially at a newly-added or "temporary" rejection path that prints a struct directly. | Never `eprintln!("{:?}")` a diagnostic kind/struct on a user-facing path — it leaks internal Rust layout (`MirDiagnostic { kind: NotYetImplemented { construct, site: SiteId(0) }, .. }`) and is unstable across refactors. Route every diagnostic through the one renderer that maps kind→stable code (`E_*`) + a user-facing message; a not-yet-implemented gap must read as a current-compiler-limitation, not as struct fields. Use a stable kind string (`hir_diagnostic_kind_string`-style: `{:?}` truncated at the first ` {(`) for any `code`/`kind` note, never the full Debug. Guard with an e2e test asserting the rendered output (text AND `--format=json`) contains no `MirDiagnostic`/`HirDiagnostic`/`SiteId(`/`owning_pass`/`0x` fragment. The JSON surface reuses the same funnel so both paths stay leak-free by construction. | `feat/json-diagnostics` (2026-06-02, `a760adfc`): `hew compile` + eval native path printed `eprintln!("{} {diagnostic:?}", ...)` at the two MIR-gate rejection sites (`main.rs:169`/`378`), leaking the raw `MirDiagnostic` Debug payload; routed both through `render_pipeline_mir_diagnostics`→`render_mir_diagnostics`. Sibling of `diagnostic-source-attribution`. |
| `link-gate-expansion-test-hygiene` | A `can_link_with_host_tools()` or similar acceptance gate is expanded to accept new target classes. | After expanding a link gate, grep every test helper that constructs a "foreign" target and verify each target remains rejected under the new rules. For Linux same-OS cross-arch, **both** acceptance-path helpers (e.g. `linux_cross_target()`) and rejection-path tests must mirror the host env using `cfg!(target_env = "musl")`; a hardcoded `gnu` triple in the acceptance helper causes spurious failures on musl hosts. | PR #978 Phase 2 / #254 Phase 3. |
| `enforcement-gate-covers-every-symbol-kind` | A new reference-site enforcement gate (visibility, deprecation, capability) keys on a per-symbol side table populated only for *some* item kinds (e.g. `type_visibility` for TypeDecl + Machine but not Trait/Actor/Const). | Populate the gate's side table for EVERY symbol kind the gate claims to govern, in EVERY registration pass (stdlib-source AND user-module), so an unregistered kind fails closed at the *reference site* with the gate's own diagnostic — not by falling through to a late, internal-sounding error (a non-pub Trait/Actor referenced cross-module leaked `E_MIR: unknown type` at the MIR boundary instead of `E_VISIBILITY`). Probe each kind (type/trait/actor/const) with a tiny cross-module fixture before declaring the gate complete; if a kind genuinely routes through a different resolution path with no consult point (const → value/field-access env), leave it on its existing fail-closed message with a SHIM annotation + tracked follow-on, never a fail-open. The diagnostic itself must honor the codebase conventions: the stable `as_kind_str` protocol key (LSP/WASM) stays in the same casing as every sibling arm (CamelCase variant name, not the SCREAMING_SNAKE `E_*` envelope code), and the `E_FOO_BAR:` envelope prefix lives in the rendered message text (matching every other `E_*` diagnostic) so `stderr.contains("E_VISIBILITY")` is a live assertion, not a dead fallback. | #2085 (`feat/v06-visibility-enforcement`): non-pub Trait/Actor cross-module refs leaked `E_MIR: unknown type`; `as_kind_str` returned `E_VISIBILITY_PRIVATE` (SCREAMING_SNAKE) while 60+ siblings return CamelCase; the envelope prefix was absent from the message so the e2e's `E_VISIBILITY` check was dead. Sibling of `diagnostic-no-debug-payload`. |
| `lint-fp-tightening-when-unsafe-to-refactor` | A new `hint`/`warning` lint rule suggests a refactor (e.g. "replace this while-counter-loop with a range `for`") that is only correct under preconditions the static analysis cannot fully verify (non-unit step, conditional increment, compound exit condition, mismatched loop variable). | Encode EVERY safety precondition as a negative `not:` guard or a unifying variable constraint in the rule's AST-grep match pattern — do not leave them as doc-only caveats. Add a non-triggering fixture program for each excluded shape (step ≠ 1, `i = i + k` where k is not a literal 1, conditional increment, compound `&&`/`\|\|` condition, `i` tested but `j` incremented) and confirm the rule DOES NOT fire on them. A hint that fires on an unsafe refactor trains users to apply a breaking change; a false-positive rate of zero for the canonical unsafe shapes is the bar. Severity must be `hint` (advisory) when the correctness depends on data-flow properties the tool cannot model. | PR #2159 (`while-counter-loop` lint for Hew, 2026-06-22): the rule unifies the same `$I` counter across the `var` init, `i < bound` condition, and `i = i + 1` / `i += 1` increment; it explicitly does NOT flag mismatched loop variables, doubling (`i = i + i`), or compound conditions — these are encoded as pattern constraints (same `$I` variable in all three positions, unit literal `1` in the increment). Severity `hint` (advisory) because loop-invariance and exact-unit-step are data-flow facts ast-grep cannot model. |

### `preflight-and-toolchain-trust` — local gates own the last pre-CI signal, with no escape hatches

- **area**: pre-push gate, build, linking, LLVM toolchain, release repair
- **invariant**: The local preflight gate is the canonical pre-CI signal: never bypassed per-branch, never silently slow, never mismatched against the toolchain the project was built with. One build system owns native linkage; release-repair work converges on one branch per outcome rather than fanning new PRs.
- **why**: Bypass hatches normalize red baselines. Slow gates push agents toward bypass. Toolchain mismatch ships subtly wrong binaries. Drip-PR repair makes release readiness untrackable.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `preflight-gate-no-bypass` | A local pre-push or pre-commit gate fails and the change is pushed anyway via an environment-variable escape hatch, `--no-verify`, `SKIP_HOOKS=1`, or a "just this once" bypass — typically rationalized as "offline", "missing local deps", "failure is in `main` not my diff", or "unrelated to this lane". | Never add an environment-variable bypass branch to `scripts/pre-push-ci-preflight.sh`, `scripts/ci-preflight-dispatcher.sh`, or any git hook; never pass `--no-verify` / `SKIP_HOOKS=1` / `ALLOW_SKIP_*=1` on `git push` or `git commit`. Before dispatching a fleet of branches from the root worktree, run `git status` + `git branch --show-current`. When `make ci-preflight` fails: if the failure reproduces on a fresh `origin/main` checkout, freeze further dispatch and fix `main`; if it is only on your diff, fix your diff. Reverts of bad PRs use a new commit and a new PR — never force-push over `main`. | PR #1466. |
| `preflight-perf-discipline` | `make ci-preflight` becomes slow (≥5 min), hangs indefinitely, or always falls back to the comprehensive lane. | Audit `.gitignore` for machine-local artefacts (clangd cache, LSP test artefacts, gate output dirs); add plain-name entries (no trailing slash) for any directory name that may appear as a worktree symlink (`.bin`, `.cache`, `node_modules`, `target`); add `timeout`/`TIMEOUT` properties to every test that can hang; move inherently slow suites into opt-in targets; verify the dispatcher routes a no-diff worktree run into a narrow lane (not fallback) before pushing. | PR #1537; PR #1688; issues #1532, #1538, #1539, #1540. |
| `full-suite-runs-its-prereqs-no-masked-green` | The full workspace test target is taken as the green signal, but it lazily builds link artifacts (native `libhew.a`, wasm32 `libhew_runtime.a`) on first use, and/or runs fail-fast (first failure aborts the rest), and/or is observed through a `make … \| tail` pipe (which reports the pipe's exit code, not make's); OR a per-test build guard gates the artifact build on `path.exists()` rather than on freshness. | Make the full test target depend on its link prerequisites (`test-rust: stdlib wasm-runtime`) so a fresh worktree builds them BEFORE the parallel run — otherwise under parallel load the lazy build blows per-test deadlines (false eval/run-e2e timeouts) AND a missing staticlib fails an early test that fail-fast then aborts, masking every later red. NEVER declare trunk green from a fail-fast-aborted run, a piped exit code, or a per-crate subset: read the actual full-suite `Summary` line ("N tests run: N passed") from a prereq-built `--no-fail-fast` run. A "blocked" verdict whose only failures are eval/run-e2e timeouts under concurrent-agent CPU load is contention (serialize build-heavy gates; re-gate on a quiet machine), not a code defect. **A test helper that builds a link artifact MUST gate on freshness, never on mere existence: `if lib.exists() { return; }` reuses a STALE `libhew.a` after a toolchain swap (rustc/LLVM upgrade) — cargo rebuilt `hew` under the new toolchain but the guard skipped the `cargo build -p hew-lib` that would refresh the archive, linking new object code against old → clang/lld link failure.** Always invoke `cargo build -p hew-lib` unconditionally (cargo's fingerprint makes it a ~0.1s no-op when current and a correct rebuild when the toolchain or sources changed) and assert the artifact exists after. The `check-libhew-fresh.sh` mtime gate is NOT sufficient here: it keys on source mtime only (a toolchain swap leaves source mtimes untouched) and is reached only via `make` paths that run `make stdlib` first — the `cargo test` path bypasses it entirely. | feat preflight-hygiene (2026-06-02, `64954f4e`): `test-rust` lacked the `stdlib wasm-runtime` prereq the narrow `test-compiler-pipeline` already had; the eval_wasm fail-fast had masked two pre-existing reds (a `syntax_data` keyword-list drift and an over-broad unresolved-call test predicate) for the whole session. fix/llvm-22-codegen-std-link (2026-06-14): after the local clang/lld→22.1.7 + rustc→1.96 upgrade, 17 `hew-codegen-rs/tests/*_exec.rs` guards' `if lib.exists() { return; }` reused the pre-upgrade `libhew.a`, failing the std-module link tests; replaced with an unconditional rebuild + post-build existence assertion. Cousin of `preflight-perf-discipline`. |
| `red-required-check-is-a-stop-not-noise` | A required CI check is red and the redness is treated as background noise — "known infra flake", "fails in a step unrelated to my diff", "the test count still shows N passed" — especially when the failing step is an EARLY job step (freshness pre-check, lazy staticlib build, toolchain setup) that runs before the compiled-path test steps. | Treat any red required check as a full stop. An early `make` step that exits non-zero ABORTS every later step in the same job (`check-libhew-fresh` → `vertical-slice` → `test-hew-ratchet` → `stdlib-ratchet` → `sandbox-parity`), so a tolerated red dark-zones the entire downstream suite — those tests never run, they are NOT "passing". A partial "N tests passed" from one runner (e.g. the Rust `cargo nextest` count) is NOT job-green when a later suite behind the failed step never executed. Fix the FIRST failing step to green — it unmasks the next — and never let a required check sit red across sessions; a red infra/freshness step is fixed THAT DAY, not annotated as flake. | 2026-06-12 (#1834): `main`'s required `Build & test (Linux)` was red at `check-libhew-fresh` (Makefile:207, a BSD-vs-GNU `stat` bug) for the whole v0.5 conversion, so `test-hew-ratchet` NEVER ran in CI; a deterministic msgpack `from_json` ABI bug (latent since `32532b71`) sat undetected for a month while "9085 tests passed" (the Rust nextest, which never exercises the compiled `.hew` path) read as green. The fix peeled three stacked masks: check-libhew-fresh → run.sh 512MB-`ulimit` OOM → the msgpack bug. Cousin of `full-suite-runs-its-prereqs-no-masked-green`. |
| `vertical-slice-stale-binary-trap` | Running `make test-vertical-slice` after building `hew` with a `CARGO_TARGET_DIR` override (e.g. a scratch extssd target dir), or after any build that does NOT write into `${ROOT}/target/debug/hew`. | The vertical-slice harness (`tests/vertical-slice/run.sh`) hardcodes `${ROOT}/target/debug/hew` — a `CARGO_TARGET_DIR`-redirected build leaves that path pointing at a STALE binary (the previous build's artefact, or absent entirely). The gate then either runs the old binary and reproduces the pre-fix bug (false failure) or runs an unrelated build (false pass). The `check-libhew-fresh.sh` freshness check backstops source-mtime drift but does NOT catch a redirected build — it only guards the `make` paths that run `make stdlib` first, and a redirected build leaves the checked path's mtime untouched. Build `hew-cli --bin hew` into the DEFAULT `${ROOT}/target` (no `CARGO_TARGET_DIR`) for any run that will be followed by `make test-vertical-slice`; a scratch `CARGO_TARGET_DIR` is fine for `cargo test -p <crate>` (the Rust crate suites do not consult the binary path), but not for the harness. Verify via `check-libhew-fresh.sh` that the binary timestamp is current BEFORE trusting any vertical-slice verdict. | PR #2123 — an apparent fixture failure during the fix review was the stale `${ROOT}/target/debug/hew` binary reproducing the original A178 bug, not a defect in the fix; the redirected build had placed the updated binary in the scratch target, leaving the harness's hardcoded path stale. Cousin of `full-suite-runs-its-prereqs-no-masked-green`. |
| `libhew-stale-on-interactive-run` | Verifying a `hew-runtime` (or `hew-std`/`hew-lib`) source change by directly running `hew run`/`hew build` on a `.hew` program, WITHOUT a `make stdlib` (or `make runtime`) first. | `hew run`/`hew build` link the user program against the prebuilt `libhew.a` native archive — they do NOT rebuild it from `hew-runtime` sources. After editing runtime code, an interactive `hew run` silently links the OLD archive, so the program exhibits the PRE-edit behaviour: a runtime fix appears not to work, or (worse) appears to work non-deterministically when the test races the unchanged code path. This is invisible to `cargo test -p hew-runtime` (which compiles the crate fresh) — only the linked archive is stale. Always run `make stdlib` (rebuilds `libhew.a` via `cargo build -p hew-lib`, a ~0.1s no-op when current) after ANY `hew-runtime`/`hew-std`/`hew-lib` edit and BEFORE trusting a `hew run`/`hew build` verdict. The `make test-*` gate targets depend on `stdlib` so they refresh it automatically; a hand-run `./target/debug/hew run` does not. Cousin of `vertical-slice-stale-binary-trap` (that one is the stale CLI binary; this one is the stale runtime archive). | static-pool restart (2026-06-26): the `SIMPLE_ONE_FOR_ONE` restart arm fix read as a non-deterministic restart (exit 7 vs 133 across runs) under direct `hew run` because the arm edit was not in the linked `libhew.a`; the runtime unit test (which compiles the crate) passed throughout. A `make stdlib` made it deterministically correct. |
| `ci-required-gate-sequencing` | Removing a required CI check from the merge-queue, moving a per-PR check to nightly/scheduled, or path-gating a required job so it skips for some changes. | A required status check is a two-sided contract: the workflow must emit a context with that exact name AND the branch ruleset must list it. (1) ORDER: remove the name from the ruleset's `required_status_checks` BEFORE deleting the emitting job — never the reverse, or open PRs strand on a forever-missing required check. Leave the old job running until one PR proves the reduced required set is accepted, then delete. (2) Path-gate required jobs with STEP-LEVEL no-op (`if: env.RUN_*!='true'` echo step + `if: env.RUN_*=='true'` on heavy steps), NEVER job-level `if:` — a job whose `if` is false reports as skipped/missing, not as a satisfied required context. (3) Path filters fail CLOSED: any path that is not provably docs-only must trip the broadest correctness gate; catch unknown/new crates with `**/*.rs` + `**/Cargo.toml` so a new crate never defaults to no-op; verify with a glob trace over representative change sets that the fail-safe invariant holds before push. (4) Moving a check to nightly is not permission to neglect it — the nightly needs a named same-day owner, or it silently drifts. (5) Keep `scripts/check-preflight-ci-parity.sh` green: the dispatcher fallback lane is the union of every required CI command; a gate edit updates the parity mirror, never weakens it. | CI L6 overhaul (2026-06-19, `feat/ci-l6-overhaul`): `Code coverage` was the flakiest required check (cargo-llvm-cov instrumentation + duplicated `target/llvm-cov-target/` on top of LLVM install exited 100 / ENOSPC on 4 sound PRs where `Build & test` was green); moved verbatim to `coverage-nightly.yml`, removed from ruleset 13115582 (5→4 required), per-PR Windows/macOS deduped from full workspace nextest to build+platform-smoke (full nextest gated to platform/ABI/toolchain paths + the nightly matrix). Cousin of `red-required-check-is-a-stop-not-noise`, `preflight-perf-discipline`. |
| `test-toolchain-match` | A CTest script invokes `clang` or another LLVM tool by bare name via `find_program`. | Pass the project-configured clang (resolved from `LLVM_TOOLS_BINARY_DIR` or `CMAKE_C_COMPILER`) into test CMake scripts instead of relying on PATH-based `find_program`. | JOURNEY 2026-04-12 fix/llvm22-coro-end-return-contract. |
| `build-link-authority` | Embedding, relinking, or packaging the native backend across platforms. | Let CMake author link directives consumed by Cargo, resolve compiler and runtime paths explicitly, fail on cross-arch or toolchain mismatch, and reset staged or generated dirs when packaging rewrites them. | PR #809/#775/#771. |
| `byte-identity-oracle-isolates-fn-bodies` | Proving a behaviour-preserving codegen refactor (a pure dedup — folding N bespoke emitters onto a shared seam, an extract-helper, a move-code commit) emits unchanged code, by `diff`-ing the whole `--emit-dir` `.ll` dump baseline-vs-after, OR by leaning on `test-hew-ratchet` alone for a refactor whose contract is "ZERO output change". | For a pure-dedup codegen change the strongest gate is **byte-identity of the emitted IR**, not just "compiles" or "ratchet behaviour preserved" — but the whole-module `.ll` dump is NON-DETERMINISTIC run-to-run for the SAME binary (global type-decl order, whole-function emission order, and the `@str_lit.N` / `@__hew_const__NAME__N` pool-id suffixes are HashMap-iteration-driven), so a positional `diff` false-positives massively. The real oracle: extract each affected function BY ITS (deterministic) mangled name, normalize the pool-id suffixes, and compare those function bodies in isolation — the INSTRUCTION sequence within a named function IS deterministic. **String-pool symbols (`@str_lit.N`, `@__hew_const_str__NAME__N`) MUST be normalised by initializer CONTENT, not by pool-id number.** A simple `s/@str_lit\.[0-9]+/@str_lit.N/` collapses all pool slots to the same token regardless of the `c"..."` value — a change from `c"foo"` to `c"bar"` passes silently (false negative). The correct approach: two-pass awk — first build a `sym → c"..."` map from global definition lines, then substitute each operand reference with `@_pool_[<content>]`. Symbols with a LONGER name (e.g. `@str_lit.4`) must be substituted before their shorter prefix (`@str_lit`) to prevent partial-match corruption. `@__hew_const__NAME__N` (numeric constants) are safe to collapse by name (`→ @__hew_const__NAME__N`) since the NAME already discriminates identity. SELF-TEST the oracle first by running the SAME binary twice and confirming it reports IDENTICAL (proves it neutralizes module-reorder noise) before trusting an IDENTICAL verdict. Capture BOTH the deadline (`\| after d`) and non-deadline form, and every element-kind variant, of each affected path — one fixture per arm. `checked-mir-verify` is the MIR control (must stay byte-identical when the change is codegen-only). A `test-hew-ratchet` 30s/test timeout on tests UNRELATED to the change (string/bytes/vec/scope) under a pinned core is a CONTENTION false-red (`preflight-flake-isolation`), not a regression — classify by "is the timed-out test even on the changed path?" + the byte-identity proof, and re-run on a quiet box. **Productionised gate:** `make ll-diff` (`scripts/ll-corpus.sh verify`) — compares every function body in the five R4-concern fixtures (layout, suspend, runtime_abi, arith, thunks) against committed goldens for both native and wasm32; `make ll-golden` recaptures. `scripts/ll-byte-identity.sh <baseline-dir> <head-dir>` is the low-level per-dir comparator. `make ll-identity-selftest` (`scripts/ll-identity-selftest.sh`) proves the normaliser's four invariants: (1) content-change caught — swapping `c"hello"` ↔ `c" world"` on @str_lit.4 exits 1; (2) register-perturbation caught — %reg rename exits 1; (3) baseline-identical — file vs itself exits 0; (4) pool-id-reordering-transparent — same content, shifted IDs, exits 0. Run `make ll-identity-selftest` before trusting any `ll-diff` IDENTICAL verdict on a new normaliser. | suspension-consolidation-phase1 (2026-06-20): folding the 5 remaining bespoke `emit_suspending_*` handlers (ask/read/accept/stream_next/channel_recv) onto the shared `emit_suspend_point` seam (the W52.004 RC5 tail-fold). A raw `.ll diff` flagged the untouched `read`/`accept` fixtures as "differing" — pure pool-id/decl-order noise (proven: same binary twice diffed ~18k lines). The fn-body-isolation oracle (`.tmp/suspension-consol-ir/compare.sh`) reported all 14 carrier fixtures IDENTICAL across all 5 ports + `checked-mir-verify` byte-identical (29×2) + wasm32 fail-closed intact + 9 wasm-exclusion units green. The first ratchet run showed 19 "timed out after 30s" — every one a string/bytes/varint/vec test, NONE a suspend carrier, starved by a 15h-orphaned (PPID=1) `ffi_boundary` spinner at 98% CPU; a contention false-red, not a regression. |
| `same-outcome-repair-window` | Successive CI or release failures keep surfacing on the same release artefact, tag, or end-to-end outcome. | Define the outcome key first, search the last 14 days of open and merged PRs for that outcome plus meaningful file overlap, push follow-up commits to the open PR when one exists, otherwise reuse or open one consolidation branch named for the outcome, reassess before the branch exceeds roughly 8 commits or +600/-300 lines, keep unrelated subsystems out of the repair window, and require an auditable hotfix justification before splitting emergency work away from it. For release-class work, do not stop at green PR checks; wait for the full tag/release validation tied to that artefact. | PR #1620-#1631. |
| `private-ghas-scanner-gates` | A private GitHub repository adds CodeQL, dependency-review, code scanning, or other GitHub-native security scanners to required PR CI. | Before landing scanner workflows, check repository visibility and `security_and_analysis`/GHAS availability with the GitHub API; if GHAS-backed features are unavailable, keep PR checks green by skipping or soft-failing only the unsupported scanner step, preserve the rest of the job as fail-loud, and record a follow-up to remove the tolerance once Dependency graph, code scanning, or GHAS is enabled. Restrict push-triggered CI to `main` when PR branches already run `pull_request` checks so duplicate push runs cannot pollute the PR rollup. | hew-registry PR #15. |
| `ci-path-filters-cover-gate-inputs` | A required CI workflow uses path filters or conditional jobs to decide whether heavy build/test gates run. | Treat path filters as part of the release gate, not as an optimization-only detail: enumerate every repo path that can change compiler/runtime/test/generator/sandbox/release-gate behaviour, include workflow/action files themselves, and add a machine-checkable sample-path oracle that proves representative gate-sensitive files set the heavy-job condition true while docs-only paths still no-op. Include root manifests and generated-table inputs, not just source globs. | v05-integration `6125238e` (`ci(workflows): fail closed on gate-sensitive paths`). |
| `corpus-reformat-proving-gate` | A lane reformats committed `.hew`/source files with the formatter it is changing — i.e. the formatter change touches `fmt.rs` or any escape/emit logic AND the repo contains checked-in `.hew` sources. | The proving gate for a corpus reformat is `make hew-fmt-check` (the formatter run over the on-disk corpus), NOT `cargo test`. Property/round-trip tests construct inputs in-process and never read the on-disk files; a non-idempotent committed file passes them but fails the formatter's own check. Run `make hew-fmt-check` as part of the branch's local gate before the PR-gate review, not just CI. | PR #2102: 3 committed `.hew` files (`examples/curl_client.hew`, `examples/grep/grep.hew`, `std/bench/bench.hew`) passed all `cargo test -p hew-parser` property/round-trip tests but failed `make hew-fmt-check`; the corpus files were reformatted to fix the idempotency gap. |
| `mir-hir-lowering-proving-gate` | A lane changes MIR/HIR lowering or block/expression typing — any pass that affects how expressions lower to MIR terminator or instruction shape, how block divergence is typed, how `!`/`()` propagates, OR any supervisor/actor/MIR-lowering change that re-shapes the dumped MIR (new/removed blocks, trap→recoverable, changed terminators). | Add `make checked-mir-verify` (the golden MIR corpus) to the lane's local proving gates and run it before push. This gate is Linux-only in CI and is NOT covered by `make test-vertical-slice` or `make test-hew-ratchet`; it cross-checks the emitted MIR text against committed golden files so unexpected lowering drift is caught before CI runs. Expected golden drift (a correct re-typing or restructuring, e.g. `block_diverges` re-typing `()` → `!`, or a fungible-ref reshape) must be advanced in-lane: (1) run `make checked-mir-golden` to regenerate the goldens; (2) git-diff the goldens to confirm the MIR delta is intentional and not a miscompile; (3) commit the updated goldens in the same lane before push. **On macOS `checked-mir-verify` cannot run (Linux-only gate), so `make checked-mir-golden` + committing the regen IS the local proxy — it is the macOS implementer's substitute for the verify step.** Any unexpected drift is investigated before the lane is declared ready. The gate is cheap to run locally and prevents a class of Linux-only CI red that has no macOS signal. | PR #2115 (feat/v06-error-prop-return-letelse): `block_diverges` correctly re-typed 3 MIR golden bodies from `()` to `!` after the `block_diverges` fix landed, but the local gate set did not include `make checked-mir-verify`, so the golden drift was not advanced before push — Linux CI went red on the MIR golden mismatch while macOS was green (the gate is Linux-only). PR #2127 (fix/supervisor-fungible-pid): the fungible-ref MIR reshape for `supervisor_stop` (new re-resolve path, removed liveness trap block, changed terminators) drifted `supervisor_stop.{raw,elab}.mir`; the in-lane macOS gate (ratchet + vertical-slice) passed clean but the Linux `checked-mir-verify` step failed; fixed by running `make checked-mir-golden`, confirming the golden delta matched the intentional lowering change, and committing the regen (`65b54053`). |
| `ffi-symbol-classification` | Adding a `#[no_mangle] extern "C"` fn to `hew-runtime`, or a new codegen-emitted runtime-ABI symbol (e.g. `hew_cont_*`, `hew_ser_*`, `hew_de_*`, `hew_xnode_*`). | Every such export MUST be classified in `scripts/jit-symbol-classification.toml` (tier: `stable` / `codegen-stable` / `internal`) AND `make lint` must pass before the lane is declared ready. `cargo test` does NOT catch an unclassified export; an unclassified symbol causes a `make lint` FFI failure that cascades into every test that links or evals a native binary (hew-cli native-link/eval failures via a `support/mod.rs` harness panic). After adding runtime exports: (1) classify each symbol into the appropriate tier in the TOML; (2) run `make lint` (not just `cargo test`) to confirm the `verify-ffi-symbols` check is green; (3) confirm no hew-cli eval/link tests newly fail. | Slice-3 `hew_cont_*` exports and #31 `hew_ser_*`/`hew_de_*`/`hew_xnode_*` (25 unclassified symbols → `make lint` FFI failure + 13 cascading hew-cli native-link/eval test failures; fixed by classifying as `codegen-stable`). |
| `cfg-gated-platform-build` | cfg-gating runtime code on a platform with libc-symbol differences (flush/stdio/etc.), e.g. `#[cfg(target_os = "macos")]` vs a non-Darwin branch that calls `libc::stdout`; OR an always-compiled runtime function (a `#[no_mangle]` FFI export, a helper called from shared codegen) hard-references a target-gated module path (`crate::supervisor::…` where `supervisor` is `#[cfg(not(target_arch="wasm32"))]`). | The non-host cfg branch MUST build the non-host target too. A host-only build or a host-only review passes the Darwin branch while silently accepting a non-Darwin branch that uses a symbol absent on another target (e.g. `libc::stdout` is unbound on `wasm32-wasip1`). Prefer a single portable form (e.g. `fflush(NULL)` via `libc::fflush(std::ptr::null_mut())`) over per-platform symbol spelling. Gate: run `cargo build -p hew-runtime --target wasm32-wasip1 --no-default-features` for any cfg-gated runtime change before declaring ready. **Lint dimension:** cfg-gated code is invisible to host `cargo build`/`clippy` AND to host review — both compile the host arm and silently accept the foreign arm. A cfg-active *lint* defect (e.g. `dead_code`, `allow_attributes_without_reason` inside `#[cfg(target_os="freebsd")]`) is caught by cross-target clippy: `cargo clippy --target <foreign-triple>` lints the foreign arm on the host. **Execution dimension:** link-step and test-runtime behaviour inside a foreign cfg (a test's bare-`clang` link flags, `accept()` ECONNABORTED, sysctl/argv) is NOT catchable by host cross-build/clippy (no foreign sysroot, can't run the foreign binary) and requires on-box verification on the real target before declaring ready. **Test-build dimension:** a `#[cfg(test)]` helper that references a `#[cfg(not(target_arch="wasm32"))]` module breaks `cargo test --target wasm32-wasip1 --lib` (E0433) yet escapes BOTH the non-test wasm build (`make wasm-runtime` / `cargo build --target wasm32`, which never compiles test code) AND host `cargo test --lib`; gate such helpers `#[cfg(all(test, not(target_arch="wasm32")))]` (add a wasm32 companion stub if wasm test call-sites need it) and run `cargo test -p hew-runtime --target wasm32-wasip1 --no-default-features --lib --no-run` (witnessed #1228 M1 `7482f9f8`: `RuntimeTestGuard` was `#[cfg(test)]` over the `cfg(not(wasm32))` runtime modules → 11× E0433, green on `make wasm-runtime` + host `--lib`). | `flush_stdout` non-Darwin branch used `libc::stdout` (absent on `wasm32-wasip1`) → host build and Darwin-only review passed; wasm32 build failed; fixed to portable `fflush(NULL)` (`a12c5c14`). FreeBSD portability (v05-integration `a7086a9c`, 2026-06-05): a `#[cfg(target_os="freebsd")]` test helper returned `&[]` for link flags (needed `-lpthread`/`-lm`) and `#[allow(dead_code)]` lacked a `reason` — host preflight (8779/8779) AND host review both passed; only on-box FreeBSD `cargo test`+`clippy` surfaced the link failure and the `allow_attributes_without_reason` warning. feat/v06-dist-9-explicit-links (2026-06-27): a new always-compiled `#[no_mangle]` runtime export `hew_actor_exit_unhandled` (called from the shared dispatch trampoline both targets emit) hard-referenced `crate::supervisor::hew_trap_with_code`, but `supervisor` is `#[cfg(not(target_arch="wasm32"))]` → `make wasm-runtime` failed to compile the wasm32 runtime archive ENTIRELY, so every wasm32 program (not just actor programs) lost its runtime; the full Linux workspace gate caught it via two non-actor WASM e2e tests while host build + native review passed. Fixed by dispatching to the per-target module (`crate::supervisor` native / `crate::trap_code` wasm32 — both export the identical `hew_trap_with_code(i32)` symbol). |
| `runtime-authority-proves-on-compiled-corpus` | Changing how a runtime authority is installed/accessed, a fail-closed boundary, OR any codegen that emits runtime init/teardown calls (de-globalization, `RuntimeInner`, `hew_sched_init` placement, the drain epilogue, install-before-use ordering). | The bug class is "a COMPILED program touches a de-globalized / fail-closed authority before it is installed" — INVISIBLE to `cargo test --lib` (no compiled program runs) and UNDER-COVERED by `hew-cli eval_e2e` (single fragments, not the node/distributed/observe corpus). The proving gate is the COMPILED `.hew` EXECUTION corpus: `make test-vertical-slice` + `make test-hew-ratchet` + `make stdlib-ratchet`, plus a full `examples/` run for node/distributed programs, enumerated with fail-fast OFF so ALL trap sites surface at once (CI fail-fast hides the count). A change can be green on `--lib` (1853) + eval_e2e (98) + two drop-safety reviews + a cross-eco review and still trap N compiled programs. | #1228 M1 (`3111fb98`): the `RuntimeInner` de-globalization made `rt_current()` fail-closed; the explicit-install migration was "proven" on `cargo --lib` + eval_e2e and shipped THREE onion layers of compiled-program traps — eval_e2e `std::observe` (25 tests) → vertical-slice `remote_pid_tell` node tell → 7-program entry-install — each caught ONLY by the compiled execution suites. Fix hoists `hew_sched_init` to the `main` prologue gated on `module_uses_runtime`. Cousin of `red-required-check-is-a-stop-not-noise`, `full-suite-runs-its-prereqs-no-masked-green`. |
| `exec-differential-gate-needs-deterministic-programs` | Building an O0-vs-O2 (or any two-config) differential exec gate, OR extending the existing `scripts/o2-differential.sh` corpus. | The gate's corpus MUST consist of programs whose stdout is **deterministic under repeated execution** — same binary, same input, same stdout every time. Programs with concurrent actor/thread behaviour produce scheduler-dependent stdout ordering and non-stable thread-ids that differ between runs of the SAME binary, producing false divergences that mask real ones. Classify programs BEFORE adding them: (1) run the same binary twice with no O2 involvement — if stdout differs, the program is non-deterministic; (2) for programs that MUST exercise concurrency, normalize or sort output before diffing (e.g. `sort -u` the stdout lines), OR assert only the final result not intermediate actor output; (3) when a divergence is flagged, re-run both configs from the SAME binary invocation to distinguish true codegen-difference from scheduling noise. The "same binary twice produces IDENTICAL stdout" self-test is the determinism oracle (mirrors `make ll-identity-selftest` for IR; the exec equivalent is `./prog > a.txt && ./prog > b.txt && diff a.txt b.txt`). Non-deterministic programs belong in the runtime integration corpus (`test-hew-ratchet`), not the differential-exec gate. | RC9 -O2 pipeline (#2103, 2026-06-21): `scripts/o2-differential.sh` covers `tests/hew/` — the corpus was validated over the full O0 vs O2 run with 0 divergences because it is entirely deterministic (pure computation, no actors). The extension plan for closures + enums + hashmaps noted that collision-heavy hashmap iteration order can vary between runs of the same binary; sorting output before diffing is the mitigation. |
| `preflight-base-ref-on-branch` | Running `make ci-preflight` while the working directory is ON the integration branch (e.g. `v05-integration`) rather than on a feature branch that diverges from it. | Pass `--base origin/main` explicitly: `scripts/ci-preflight-dispatcher.sh --base origin/main`. The bare on-branch invocation diffs the branch against itself → "No changed files detected" → the dispatcher exits as a no-op false-pass.
