The real gate needs a base ref so the dispatcher can enumerate the actual changed files and route to the right lanes. | This session (`a0fb4a1e`): bare on-branch `ci-preflight` was a no-op; the gate required `--base origin/main` to classify the diff correctly. |
| `release-job-must-checkout-for-repo-files` | A GitHub Actions `release`/`publish` job reads files from the repository (release notes via `body_path`, a version manifest, a changelog, SBOM, or any repo-relative path) but only downloads build artifacts from earlier jobs. | Every CI job that reads repo-relative files MUST include `actions/checkout` (pinned SHA, `ref: ${{ env.RELEASE_TAG }}` or equivalent) as its FIRST step, before any artifact download. A job that skips checkout and passes a repo-relative path to an action will silently publish an empty body / missing manifest — the action finds no file and uses its zero-value default with no error. Post-tag validation: after each release tag, open the GitHub release page and verify the body is populated; a missing body is the signal that the checkout was absent. Pin the checkout at the same action SHA all sibling jobs use so drift is visible in diff. | v0.5.1 release body was empty because the `release` job lost its `actions/checkout` step during a CI refactor; the `body_path: docs/releases/v0.5.1.md` file was never present in the workspace. Body was set manually post-publish; recurrence prevented by PR #1899. |
| `windows-lld-link-toolchain-coexistence` | A Windows build adds or changes the linker tool, or the build system recipe that produces the `hew` CLI binary alongside the `hew.lib` / `libhew.a` runtime staticlib. | Keep `lld-link.exe` as the Windows MSVC linker — it ships in the SAME LLVM archive as `clang.exe` (co-presence guaranteed by the mandatory LLVM 22 prerequisite) and avoids the `vcvars` environment that breaks `llvm-sys`'s version probe. The `make hew-native` target MUST build BOTH `hew-cli` AND `hew-lib` in one invocation; `cargo build -p hew-cli` alone does NOT produce `hew.lib`, so `hew build` silently fails to link user programs. Replace the terse missing-`clang` link error with an actionable diagnostic naming the required tools, the LLVM release, PATH setup, and the vcvars footgun. Keep the linker pin in `.cargo/config.toml` with a documented rationale — it is not dead config. | PR #2149 (`fix(build): make Windows source builds link-ready`, 2026-06-22): `cargo build -p hew-cli` succeeded on a clean Windows checkout but `hew build` failed to link — `hew.lib` was never produced; `make hew-native` fixed by building cli+lib together. `lld-link` pin retained (LLVM archive ships it; vcvars breaks `llvm-sys`). New cross-platform test `windows_missing_clang_message_names_required_tools_and_provisioning` passes on macOS and covers the Windows diagnostic. |
| `debuginfo-by-objformat` | Adding or changing debug-info emission in `hew-codegen-rs/src/llvm.rs` without verifying whether the object format (PE/COFF on Windows vs ELF on Linux vs Mach-O on macOS) requires a different debug-info format. | Select the debug-info format from the object format implied by the target triple, not hardcoded DWARF: set the `"CodeView"` LLVM module flag for PE/COFF targets (`x86_64-pc-windows-msvc`, `aarch64-pc-windows-msvc`) and emit `/pdb` in `hew-cli/src/link.rs`; default to DWARF for ELF and Mach-O. A macOS/Linux DWARF pass does NOT cover the Windows CodeView/PDB gap — `hew build -g` emitting DWARF-in-PE produces a binary WinDbg/VS cannot debug. Verify on each platform: `dwarfdump`/`llvm-readobj` for DWARF targets, `cdb`/`llvm-readobj --codeview` for the Windows PE target. | Issue #2117 (2026-06-22): `hew build -g` emits full DWARF-in-PE on Windows because `"CodeView"` LLVM module flag is never set in `hew-codegen-rs/src/llvm.rs` (only `"Debug Info Version"=3`); WinDbg/VS cannot consume DWARF-in-PE. Root cause pinned empirically on a Windows 11 dev host; 3-part fix (CodeView flag + `/pdb` in link.rs + cdb validation) tracked for rc1. Coordination-ledger S151. Cousin of `debugger-gate-per-target`. |

### `user-surface-correctness` — the public CLI behaves the way users expect, on the binary they actually run

- **area**: REPL, formatter, observability, release binary
- **invariant**: User-facing surfaces flush their output at submission boundaries, preserve every comment they round-trip, and never corrupt input. Tracing fires at scheduler boundaries with context.
- **why**: A REPL that buffers, a formatter that drops doc-comments, and a release binary that crashes on exit destroy user trust faster than any compiler bug — they are visible immediately, on the first install.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `repl-piped-stdout-flush` | An interactive REPL or shell accepts user input and produces output per submission, and is invoked with stdin/stdout piped (non-TTY). | After each user-submitted statement or expression evaluation in the REPL loop, call `flush()` on stdout before reading the next submission. Flush unconditionally in both isatty and piped paths — the cost of a flush is negligible compared to the user-visible breakage when missed. | PR #1553 (closed #1542, #1547). |
| `formatter-comment-flush-audit` | A new block-shaped construct (enum variant, struct field, match arm, extern fn, else-if branch, etc.) is added to the formatter, OR comment-positioning anomalies appear in round-trip tests. | For each top-level AST construct that can contain comments, ensure `flush_comments_before(span.start)` runs before emitting each element, set `prev_source_pos = span.start`, format the construct, then `flush_comments_before(span.end)` (or the next element's start). Add a round-trip fixture test with leading and trailing comments on each construct type. Anchor on a real `Span` field on the AST node — not a `find_keyword_after` heuristic — so identifier-content collisions don't misanchor. | PR #1535 (closed #1529, #1534, #1536). |
| `formatter-field-roundtrip-coverage` | A new semantic field or variant is added to an AST node the formatter emits (a child clause, a fused field, a boolean discriminator like `is_pool`), OR a formatter's per-node emitter omits a field the parser populates. | The formatter must emit **every** semantically-load-bearing field of each node it formats; a dropped field is fail-OPEN and **invisible until a round-trip test exercises a value in that field** (the existing fixture may pass while a sibling field silently vanishes). For each formatted node, cross-check the emitter against the AST struct field list, and add an `exact_roundtrip` fixture that populates each optional clause and each boolean-discriminated form (e.g. both `child` and `pool`). For `HashMap`-backed fields, sort keys before emitting so the round-trip is deterministic and idempotent. A boolean like `is_pool` that selects a leading keyword is especially easy to drop — the node still formats, just with the wrong keyword. | `feat/supervisor-flat-reliability-fields` (2026-06: `format_child_spec` silently dropped `wired_to` and always wrote `child` regardless of `is_pool`, leaving `fmt_supervisor_decl_roundtrip` red; fixed by emitting `pool`/`child`, `wired_to` (sorted), `shutdown`, and the explicit `strategy` default, plus fixtures exercising every clause). |
| `tracing-boundaries` | Observability exists but data is incomplete, causality breaks, or activation is awkward. | Emit begin and end in the dispatch loop, carry trace context in mailbox payloads, and tie activation to the operator-facing profiler or UI switch. | Original LESSONS observe pass. |

### `process-discipline` — how foundational PRs are reviewed, audited, and validated

- **area**: orchestration, dispatch briefs, agent prompts, multi-agent coordination
- **invariant**: Foundational changes (FFI ABI, runtime ABI, codegen lowering, checker authority, msgpack seam) are reviewed cross-ecosystem from the start; audits hunt with multiple grep patterns; plans that name a helper expect the implementer to call it; behavioural regressions count even when tests pass; LSP queries supplement cargo for the validation surface they actually cover.
- **why**: Same-ecosystem review on foundational work consistently misses material defects that an opposite-ecosystem reviewer catches first-pass. PRs that re-litigate the same gap across 3 revision cycles are evidence the rule was applied implicitly only after pain — encoding it durably saves the next foundational lane from running the same loop.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `first-pass-cross-ecosystem-foundational` | A PR touches FFI ABI, runtime ABI, codegen lowering, checker authority, or the msgpack seam — i.e. the foundational bucket. | Dispatch a cross-ecosystem reviewer simultaneously with the implementer (or before, as a plan-review), not after the implementer claims ready. Implementer writes the PR body for a rigorous opposite-ecosystem reviewer; ship the diff, then re-review. The orchestrator never marks gate `READY` on foundational work without an opposite-ecosystem signal in hand. | PRs #1717, #1720, #1721, #1723 each took 3 cross-ecosystem cycles in 2026-05-09 because same-ecosystem accept missed sentinel-as-callee bugs, broken bound paths, plumbed-but-not-consumed metadata, and fail-open guards.<br><br>Drop-completion tranche (2026-07-02): 7 same-family stage-verifies each individually accepted their stage; GPT cross-eco (fresh rebuild both sides, independent MIR-dump proof) found a live P0 double-free on an idiomatic shape (nested composite extraction) on its first pass, plus a second pre-existing leak of the same family on the promote-time re-hunt. Zero of the 7 same-family verifies caught it, and plain `leaks --atExit` reads 0 on the broken case (masked) — this is the strongest cross-eco catch of the program to date: a shippable double-free invisible to both in-family review AND to plain leak-scanning, caught only by an adversarial cross-ecosystem pass forcing Guard-Malloc. |
| `audit-completeness-via-multiple-greps` | A dispatch brief asks an agent to "find every instance of X" — bug-class audit, callsite enumeration, surface inventory, etc. | Require ≥3 distinct grep patterns covering the smell from different angles, explicit per-match listing with file:line, and a negative-check ("did I miss any sibling shape?") before classifying any match. Sample-of-N or "the obvious cases" returns are incomplete. | PR #1723 audit cited 8 unguarded actor FFI functions; cross-ecosystem found 5+ more (`hew_actor_try_send`, `actor_send_result_internal_reply` helper, WASM mirrors). The first audit's grep matched "fn hew_actor_set_*" and missed the helper-function class entirely. |
| `plan-prescribes-helper-implementer-honors` | A plan recommends routing through an existing helper (`emitFieldDropsForUserStruct`, `nullOutDropSlot`, `cabi_guard!`, etc.) to avoid reinventing structural logic. | The implementer's worker-return must explicitly cite calling the named helper. Reinventing the helper's logic inline is a revision-required defect even if tests pass — cross-ecosystem will catch it as "diverges from established compiler/runtime path", and the bespoke implementation will skip cases the helper handles correctly. Dispatch briefs must state: "your code MUST call `<helper>`; if you decide bespoke is necessary, return blocked with rationale before writing it". | PR #1717 actor state-drop initially reimplemented field-drop logic instead of routing through `emitFieldDropsForUserStruct`. Cross-ecosystem flagged 3 BLOCKERs (sentinel handling, nested user-Drop recursion, bypass of canonical path) that were one-line fixes via the helper. |
| `behavioral-regression-not-just-test-pass` | A change to error-handling, FFI surface, fail-closed boundary, or any path where the user observes failure semantics. | "Tests pass" is necessary but not sufficient. Validation must include an explicit behavioural-regression check: "did this change ANY error semantics, including silent fallback paths?" Adding a null-guard that turns a SIGSEGV into a silent `Err(SomethingElse)` is a regression even though the program no longer crashes — the user-visible diagnostic class shifted. Implementer's worker-return must answer "did this change observable error/diagnostic behaviour and is the new behaviour the right semantic?" before declaring `implementation-clean`. | PR #1723 FFI null-guards turned spawn-OOM SIGSEGV into silent ActorStopped. Cross-ecosystem flagged it as fail-open; revision-3 replaced silent absorption with a panic on null spawn. |
| `lsp-first-cargo-confirmation` | An implementer or reviewer is about to spend 5+ minutes on a full `cargo` workspace build to verify a checker or stdlib `.hew` change. | Most checker/stdlib edits validate faster and more precisely with the LSP: `findReferences` to confirm callers, `goToDefinition` to confirm a binding's type, `hover` for inferred shape. Run targeted `cargo test -p <crate>` for the specific crate(s) touched. Reserve full `cargo` workspace builds for: (a) Rust runtime / FFI changes, (b) the final pre-push gate, (c) cross-crate refactors that the LSP cannot trace. Each isolated worktree should keep a **separate `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=<worktree>/target`** so concurrent agents do not queue on a shared Cargo lock (this remains correct even with sccache). Layer on **`RUSTC_WRAPPER=sccache`** as the shared compilation cache; `cargo.lock`-fingerprinted object files are content-addressed and safe across worktrees. `sccache --start-server` must be running; if it is absent the build proceeds without acceleration. Do not set `CARGO_TARGET_DIR` globally in `.cargo/config.toml` — agent cwd drift would route all worktrees into a single directory and cause the very lock contention the per-worktree convention avoids. | 60+ minute artifact-lock waits during 2026-05-09 multi-worktree fan-out; per-worktree `CARGO_TARGET_DIR` + shared `sccache` (content-addressed, safe under concurrent use) resolved it. |
| `end-to-end-before-layer-thickening` | A parser/checker/HIR producer gains a new field, side-table, or attribute and passes layer-local tests while downstream consumers (MIR, codegen, runtime, LSP) are assumed to "pick it up later"; OR a sub-slice adds a consumer-side discriminator (drop kind, IR variant, codegen arm, lowering branch) before the producer that feeds it is wired and exercised against a real fixture. | New language/runtime concepts MUST land producer → MIR → codegen → runtime end-to-end in one coherent change (or an explicit staged sequence with documented per-stage preconditions), even when intermediate layers only passthrough. Both directions block: (a) a producer-side field with no downstream consumer wiring is hidden debt — at review, grep every downstream layer; absent consumer at any stage = block; (b) a consumer-side discriminator must land in the same slice as the producer that emits it, gated by a producer-emit test on the exemplar fixture — before dispatching a consumer slice, verify the producer surface exists (grep the function/field, run the fixture through the stage); if absent, return `blocked`, do not dispatch. At plan time enumerate every layer the concept traverses (HIR/MIR/codegen/runtime/observe/LSP) and pick a staging strategy first. At triage, when a TODO says "producer landed, consumer follow-up", verify the consumer was actually wired; if not, treat as a live bug not a stale follow-up. Adding a field to a widely-constructed side-table output (`TypeCheckOutput`) also breaks every EXPLICIT struct literal of it (`Struct { .. }` without `..Default::default()`) in sibling crates' test modules — `cargo test -p hew-types` is green while `hew-analysis`/`hew-cli` fixture literals fail to compile; before declaring ready, `grep -rln --include='*.rs' 'TypeCheckOutput {'` and clippy every constructing crate (`hew-analysis`, `hew-cli`), not just the producer crate. | PR #103 (cycle_capable_actors — HIR producer with no MIR consumer; codegen threads only `max_heap_bytes`); PR #138 (TypeCheckOutput batch). Consumer-before-producer instances: MIR R-escape consumer with no HIR producer calling `check_program`; codegen R-escape consumer with no MIR producer emitting `CallRuntimeAbi`; `TypeCheckOutput` added to `lower_program` before any consumer used it. Tail Ok-coercion lane (2026-06-15): the new `tail_ok_coercions` field broke 10 explicit `TypeCheckOutput` literals across `hew-analysis` test modules; caught by the pre-commit clippy gate, fixed alongside the producer. |
| `falsification-probe-before-substrate-dispatch` | A planner names a substrate-reform lane that moves a registration table, marker enum, or canonical lookup across crates — e.g. "move BuiltinTypeRegistration down into hew-types", "extract the X table from hew-hir into shared crate". Cross-crate substrate moves are the trigger, not in-crate refactors. | Dispatch a falsification probe BEFORE the substrate lane: cite the destination crate's `Cargo.toml` dep graph, grep for the symbols the lane will need to call from the destination, and assert that the dependency direction is feasible. If the probe finds a dep cycle (destination would need to import a crate that already depends on it), STOP and reshape the plan into staged data-move-down phases before any implementation dispatch. The reshape goes into the plan doc as a numbered phase split, not a TODO comment in the brief. | Cluster A Slice 1 (2026-05-22): a falsification probe found `hew-types` cannot depend on `hew-hir`, but the brief told the implementer to move `BuiltinTypeRegistration` from hew-hir into hew-types. Reshaped into a 3-phase data-move-down lane (enum in hew-types → dispatch-site conversion → HIR adapter populating `Ty::Named.builtin`); the ~20m probe prevented hours of mid-edit cycle discovery. |
| `probe-build-tool-mechanism-before-plan` | A plan proposes a build-system/test-harness restructure that depends on an ASSUMED mechanism of the tool itself — Cargo test autodiscovery, `#[path]`/mod-inclusion interaction, `autotests`/`[[test]]` semantics, linker/artifact dedup behaviour — rather than a dependency-graph feasibility question. | Before writing the plan, run a throwaway empirical probe against the REAL tool: a scratch crate or `cargo metadata` count that exercises the exact mechanism claim ("does leaving the leaf file in place after adding `#[path]` compile it twice?"), not a reading of documentation or a plausible-sounding assumption. Cite the probe's exact output (target/binary/test counts, before and after) in the plan's Evidence section. If the plan's own evidence section tests an ADJACENT mechanism (mod-path resolution) but not the one the plan's mass-effect depends on (leaf autodiscovery), the plan is unverified — implementers finding this MID-EDIT is a wasted lane, not a caught bug: STOP and re-probe before dispatch. | U135 Rev 1 (2026-07-02): plan Evidence §8 tested mod-path resolution but not leaf-file autodiscovery; the implementer's empirical probe found Cargo compiles `tests/*.rs` autodiscovered files TWICE independent of `#[path]`-mod inclusion — measured 87→93 binaries / 672→1130 tests, INVERTING the plan's stated goal. Blocked cleanly (no commits, probes deleted) rather than pushing a doubling. Rev 2 re-verified via fresh Cargo probes BEFORE redispatch (a scratch probe reproduced the Rev-1 doubling then proved the physical-subdir-move fix), and the fresh probe surfaced a SECOND latent mechanism gap the Rev-1 reading missed (mod/`include_str!` paths resolve relative to the file's own directory, requiring a depth fix across 77 files) — landed 296→26 binaries, multiset test-fn equality proven per crate. Escalated from disk-hygiene to CI-blocking (S720): the undisproven Rev-1 mechanism, had it shipped, would have made the Linux CI 60-minute-timeout ceiling (`#2378`, tests passed 10825/10825, canceled in teardown) a recurring failure on every future PR. |
| `lane-delta-against-real-origin-main` | Scoping a PR diff, assessing scope-drift, or reviewing a lane's changed files when the reviewer's (or implementer's) local `main` ref may be stale — e.g. the local branch was forked many commits ago, other PRs have merged since, and `git fetch` was not run. | Always measure the lane delta against the REAL `origin/main` (`git fetch` first, then `git diff origin/main..HEAD` or `git diff origin/main...HEAD`), not the local `main` ref. A stale local `main` makes every intervening merged PR's changes appear in the diff as false scope-drift: the two-dot `main..HEAD` trap shows files from unrelated merged lanes as if they belong to this lane, inflating the apparent change set and producing phantom scope-violation findings. Run `git fetch origin` before any scope-size or changed-files assessment during review or gate work. | PR #2102 re-review: local `main` ref was at `5bd1e325`, 50+ commits behind the real `origin/main` at `803877bf`; the naive `main..HEAD` diff showed 23 files including a fork-block diagnostics feature and an -O2 LESSONS row (both already on `origin/main`); the true delta vs `origin/main` was 12 files, all on the fmt/escape/grammar surface — no scope violation. |
| `plan-anchors-survive-drift-not-line-numbers` | A plan or dispatch brief cites a code location to direct an implementer to a change site. | Anchor every site by file path + symbol name (function/ type/const) + a short greppable fragment of the actual surrounding code, not a bare line number. Line numbers are acceptable ONLY as an approximate hint alongside a real anchor, never as the sole locator — they drift the moment any commit lands between plan-authorship and dispatch, and an implementer re-deriving the real location from a stale number is exactly the "un-pre-made decision + hunting" the plan-quality bar exists to eliminate. Keep the anchor prose dense, not long: a landmark that doesn't change implementer behaviour (restating what the symbol obviously does) is waste against the token/ time-efficiency bar. | U137 (slepp directive, 2026-07-03): "ensure code landmarks and files are identified, but not necessarily bare line numbers in case those drift... optimized for efficient token and time use." Encoded into `lane-plan` SKILL.md (code-location discipline block + 2 dispatch- readiness checklist items). Evidence base: every review round in the prior session flagged drifted line anchors as a revision-round cause; three lanes needed a revision round that a landmark-anchored first-pass plan would have avoided. |
| `no-orchestration-tokens-in-source` | A dispatch brief supplies a lane ID (e.g. `L7`, `G8`), a Q-tag (e.g. `q185`, `Qa`), a PCA reference (e.g. `PCA-8`), a distribution-work lane code (e.g. `DIST-4`), a follow-up tag (e.g. `F1` in a doc), or a `.tmp/` orchestration path to an implementer, and the implementer echoes it into a committed comment, string literal, or `reason=` attribute. | Run `make leak-scan` (or `scripts/lint-orchestration-leak.sh --scan-commits`) before every push — it scans ALL tracked text files and commit-message bodies for `PCA-\d+`, `wire-fleet`, `wire-l\d`, `L7/L8/L9`, lowercase `q###` Q-tags, `Qa`-style short Q-tags, `.tmp/(orchestration\|plans\|worktrees)`, `DIST-\d+` lane codes, and `F[1-9]` in `*.md` files. The same check runs in CI (GitHub Actions lint job with `fetch-depth: 0` for full history) so no PR can bypass it. Orchestrators must not pass lane IDs, Q-tags, or DIST-N codes in briefs at all where they would be echoed into code; use plain descriptions ("the errors-as-values feature") instead of internal task identifiers. To suppress a specific pattern in a commit message, add `Leak-scan-allow: T<N> <reason>` (e.g. `Leak-scan-allow: T4 L7 is OSI layer-7 networking`) — only that T-number is suppressed; other patterns still fire in the same commit. Opt-outs are greppable: `git log --all --grep='Leak-scan-allow:'`. Accepted: `HEW-DIST-SPEC` + `§N` references (the public spec doc), `F<n>` in `*.rs`/`*.hew` (work-item sub-finding labels), `F<n>` in LESSONS.md evidence cells. | PCA-8, wire-l1 (`L7`), g8 (`G8`), wire-l2 (`q185`, `Qa`) — four consecutive work items leaked orchestration identifiers into committed source; each was caught only at review, adding a revision cycle. A later work item leaked `DIST-N` lane codes and `F<n>` follow-up tags across ~58 source comments, caught only at the PR gate; also a `LESSONS.md` ledger-tag leak (`Q56`, `Q120`) slipped through because `LESSONS.md` was excluded from the scan. T9 (`DIST-\d+`) and T10 (`F[1-9]` in `*.md`) were added and the two ledger-tag leaks cleaned. |

---

## P2 — Architecture, cleanup, and maintenance decisions

### `dedup-with-policy-boundary` — share mechanics, stop deduplication where semantics diverge

- **area**: parser, runtime helpers, type-checker traversals
- **invariant**: Helpers that look identical but diverge at one semantic edge should share scaffolding (parse, decode, structural recursion) but keep per-owner policy at the call site. Centralise the walk; do not centralise the decision.
- **why**: Premature unification flattens away exactly the policy that mattered, then re-grows it as flags or branches that recreate the duplication with worse cohesion.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `dedup-semantic-boundary` | Multiple helpers look identical but differ at one semantic edge. | Extract common parse, decode, or update scaffolding while leaving lossy conversion, interpolation-only escapes, auto-numbering, and other owner-specific semantics at the call site. | Original LESSONS C string, parser escape, wire parser, and adze-cli passes. |
| `collection-traversal-owner` | Vec, HashSet, and HashMap admissibility rules repeat the same structural `Ty` recursion. | Extract one recursive walker that delegates named collection nodes to the existing validators, and keep `validate_concrete_collection_types` calling each collection lane explicitly instead of relying on a single short-circuiting pass. | JOURNEY 2026-04-09 checker collection capability dedup lane. |
| `ty-recursion-owner` | A checker helper is only recursively rebuilding or scanning `Ty` values without checker state. | Compare candidate helper bodies for semantic identity first, then move the shared traversal onto `Ty` and delete leftover wrappers or duplicate walkers in checker-local modules. | JOURNEY 2026-04-10 refactor/ty-subst-dedup lane. |

### `architecture-cleanup-discipline` — scope decisions before structure decisions

- **area**: cleanup sweeps, integration vs rewrite, generator ceilings, lockfile resolution
- **invariant**: Before deleting an apparently-dead surface, re-classify it across docs/tests/specs/completions/workspace. Before rewriting a working module, prefer a thin integration owner over new abstraction layers. Generators have a ceiling — they emit mechanics, not semantics — and resolution algorithms must be restartable, not single-pass.
- **why**: "It looks unused" misses non-production callers; "let's rewrite this" loses working invariants; "let's autogenerate this" produces façades that look right but encode the wrong public name or return type. The cheap path is structural; the right path is semantic.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `dead-surface-sweep` | A flag, helper, crate, placeholder, or tool looks unused. | Classify production callers separately from self-tests and placeholders, then sweep docs, completions, specs, and workspace entries before deciding the surface is still real. | Original LESSONS dead-helper, dead CLI, QUIC, and export-tooling passes. |
| `integration-over-rewrite` | Existing modules already cover most of a new runtime or protocol feature, but the wiring between them is missing. | Add one orchestrating owner that composes the existing transport, cluster, registry, or runtime pieces, keep handshakes and protocol records fixed-shape, and land the work in focused slices that can still be tested independently. | Original LESSONS audit integration lessons. |
| `ffi-stub-generator-ceiling` | Adding or evaluating a generator that produces Hew façade stubs from `#[no_mangle] extern "C"` Rust sources. | Treat `extern "C"` block emission as zero-gap for modules with only `*mut c_char`/`*const c_char` and `i32` returns; treat public name, docstring, and return-type annotation as semantic gap requiring hand-edit. Modules with opaque handles (e.g. `json`, `compress`) exceed the generator ceiling regardless. Mark generator-emitted `// INTERNAL-ABI:` lines the same way `json.hew` does when the ABI type diverges from the user surface. | PR #1249. |
| `resolver-restartability` | Dependency resolution or lockfile staleness logic changes. | Revisit packages when constraints tighten and compare manifest requirements against direct locked dependencies instead of raw package-name sets. | Original LESSONS resolver and lockfile lessons. |
| `pregate-subset-must-not-be-rerun-additively` | A preflight has a fast "smoke/subset" tier preceding a full tier, and the smoke profile is defined as `default-filter: 'test(...)'` over the SAME test binaries as the full profile (i.e. "full minus a few exclusions"), so it re-executes nearly the whole full body a second time. | A fail-early pre-gate must be a CURATED MINIMAL ORACLE — a strict, explicitly-enumerated subset that adds distinct early signal (fmt/clippy/a handful of fast deterministic fixtures), never "full minus exclusions." Keep the full profile (`--profile ci`) as the coverage signal; keep the smoke profile (`--profile smoke`) as the early-exit signal. Prove the invariant `smoke ⊆ ci` AND that the full profile still runs every test exactly once: diff `cargo nextest list --profile ci` before/after the trim (must be identical) and confirm the smoke `filter-match: matches` is disjoint from, not a sub-sampled version of, the full test set. A smoke profile that is effectively "ci minus a few" doubles preflight time with no incremental value and defeats the purpose of the fast tier. | PR #2146 (`test-perf-rc1-stages-1-4`, 2026-06-22): `[profile.smoke]` was defined as the ci profile minus eval/real-timing exclusions (~9742 tests), re-running almost the entire ci body twice; stage 1 trimmed it to 1 oracle test, eliminating the duplicate body while keeping `make test`/`--profile ci` as the merge signal; `cargo nextest list` pre/post confirmed no coverage loss. Cousin: `admission-gate-is-not-runnability`. |
| `cfg-split-unify-structure-split-source` | A runtime data-structure (timer queue, work-queue, allocator pool) or shared algorithm is implemented as TWO SEPARATE cfg-gated bodies — one for native, one for wasm32 — rather than as a single shared struct with cfg split only at the I/O or clock boundary. Also fires when two Rust source files carry copies of the same algorithm with divergent correctness. | Parallel cfg-split reimplementations silently diverge: one copy can degrade to O(n²) while the other stays O(1); one accumulates bug fixes while the other stays stale. The correct pattern is ONE shared struct with cfg split ONLY at the time/IO source boundary — two small cfg-gated accessor functions that return the same type, not two separate struct bodies. When a native struct is already correct, lift it as the shared implementation and cfg-split only the wall-clock or I/O primitive it calls; delete the wasm-specific parallel struct. The same rule applies intra-crate: two Rust source files carrying copies of the same algorithm are two live authorities — identify the correct version, make it canonical, and delete the copy. Parallel implementations are especially dangerous for wasm targets because wasm32 CI runs build-only (no exec), so behavioral divergence in the wasm path is invisible until a correctness regression surfaces on the wasm runtime. | PR #2177 (`refactor(runtime): unify the WASM timer path onto HewTimerWheel`): wasm32 `SLEEP_QUEUE` + `PERIODIC_QUEUE` (two sorted-Vec O(n²) linear scans) were a separate parallel reimplementation; replaced by the shared `HewTimerWheel` struct (the existing native impl) with cfg split at `now_ms_for_wheel()` only — two small cfg-gated fns in `hew-runtime/src/timer_wheel.rs`. Cousin of `retire-in-lane-or-fail-loud` (both are about having two live paths for one decision). |

### `migration-completeness` — a replacement is not done until the predecessor is gone or fails loud

- **area**: runtime ABI/symbol families, codegen lowering, checker dispatch tables, IR-ladder lowering, serialization
- **invariant**: When you introduce a new authority for a decision (a symbol family, an ABI, a resolver, a lowering arm, a type carrier, a dispatch table), the SAME change must either delete the predecessor or make every remaining caller of it fail loud (`unreachable!`/diagnostic). Two live authorities for one decision is a defect, not a milestone — never "land the new path, retire the old one later."
- **why**: A superseded-but-reachable path silently serves stale data, disagrees with the new authority, and degrades into wrong code or memory corruption. Every parallel authority left alive is a future UAF, ABI mismatch, or fail-open hole waiting for the wrong caller to reach it. This is the P0 `checker-authority` failure generalised to every layer: once an authority loses its monopoly, two paths disagree and silently produce wrong output.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `retire-in-lane-or-fail-loud` | A change adds a superseding implementation (e.g. a `_layout` symbol family, a typed handoff, a descriptor-driven resolver) while the legacy path still compiles and is reachable. | Retire the predecessor in the SAME lane. If retirement must be staged (real downstream caller can't migrate yet), make the legacy entrypoint `unreachable!("<reason>")` or emit a diagnostic so exercising it fails noisily, AND file the retirement as a tracked, gated lane. Never leave both paths silently callable. | W4.045: HashSet drop/clone kept wiring legacy `hew_hashset_free`/`hew_hashset_clone` onto `hew_hashset_new_with_layout` handles after the `_layout` migration → 48-vs-16-byte stride → `libc::free(garbage)` heap-corruption UAF. The legacy family was never retired (D1/D2 = W4.050, still pending). |
| `enumerate-authorities-before-claiming-done` | A migration/consolidation lane is about to be declared complete. | Before claiming done, grep every caller/registrar of the decision workspace-wide (symbol name, ABI shape, dispatch-table entry, string identifier, lowering arm) and prove exactly ONE live authority remains. A planner MUST list all current authorities for the decision in the plan's Surface inventory; a reviewer MUST verify zero superseded paths remain reachable before accept. | bytes `BytesTriple` passed 4 ways (by-ref / by-value / 3-scalar / data-ptr); partial unifications left survivors — W4.041 ARM64 `to_string` returned `""` (by-value arm survived); `fix/bytes-read-abi` left the read side half on `*mut HewVec` so every `conn.read()` returned 0 bytes. Root cause: a 16-byte `{ptr,i32,i32}` by-value is classified into THREE registers on ARM64 but Rust `#[repr(C)]` uses the two-register pair, so a spilled return/non-first arg loses the len eightbyte (only "works" when SROA elides the slot). W4.046 converged on `[2 x i64]` returns + by-pointer consumer args, gated on a migrated-producer allowlist. 2026-06-12 (#1834): the migration was NOT complete — `hew_msgpack_*_hew` were left in NEITHER allowlist, and the assumed "legacy = loud fail-closed" was FALSE: codegen reinterprets a non-allowlisted `-> bytes` HewVec pointer as a triple → `from_json("{bad}").len()` read garbage, passing `len()>0` round-trips but failing the `==0` invalid case. Corrections: (1) the enumerate-step must grep EVERY `_hew` extern returning OR consuming `bytes`, not just the migrated set; (2) codegen must GENUINELY fail closed (CodegenError) on a `-> bytes` extern in neither list, so the next missed migration is a build break not latent UB (tracked follow-up). |
| `no-fail-open-fallback-after-authority` | A downstream phase keeps a `.unwrap_or(default)` / bare-name / sentinel fallback for data a newly-total authority now guarantees. | Once an authority is proven total, DELETE the fallback — do not keep it "just in case." A surviving fallback re-creates a second authority and masks the authority's real gaps as silent defaults (the fail-open hole). If totality is not yet proven, instrument with an assert-net first (see W4.047 Phase 1), then delete once the corpus proves no firing. | 7 HIR `.unwrap_or(Unit)` holes in `hew-hir/src/lower.rs` survived after the checker became type-authoritative → leaked `Ty::Var` silently coerced to `Unit` with no diagnostic; W4.047/B6 flips them to hard errors. |
| `new-suspend-carrier-register-every-membership-list` | Adding a new `Terminator::Suspending*` carrier (a new actor-context wait that parks on `coro.suspend`). | A new suspend carrier must be added to EVERY membership predicate, not just the exhaustive `match` walkers the compiler forces. The `match`-based walkers (model `successors`, `dataflow::build_preds`/`successors`, lower's source/escape/drop walkers, the codegen terminator dispatch) fail to COMPILE if you miss one — safe. But the carrier's coroutine-ness is decided by `matches!(...)` PREDICATE lists that silently accept an omission: `terminator_is_suspend_carrier` (hew-mir, the MIR `is_coroutine` authority), `is_coroutine_function` (hew-codegen-rs, decides the LLVM coro prologue), and the actor-trampoline `handler_suspendable` scan (hew-codegen-rs, decides park-vs-direct-call). Miss `is_coroutine_function` → the carrier reaches codegen with no coro state → fail-closed (loud, recoverable). Miss `handler_suspendable` → the trampoline DIRECT-CALLS a function lowered as a coro ramp expecting the handle → crash/UB (silent). Also wire the wasm-exclusion scan (`uses_wasm_excluded_symbol`) so the native-only suspend substrate fails closed at compile on wasm32, and the `ExitPath::Suspend` arm in the drop-plan builder. Grep `SuspendingSleep { .. }` workspace-wide before claiming done — every hit is a list the new carrier must join. SEPARATELY, a NEW runtime symbol the carrier's codegen INTERNS (`intern_runtime_decl`) needs its own registrations: the codegen signature-table `match` arm (a missing arm fail-closes at codegen-time with the MISLEADING "the symbol is on the MIR_EMITTER_RUNTIME_SYMBOLS allowlist but no codegen arm wires it" message even when the symbol was NEVER on the MIR allowlist), `scripts/jit-symbol-classification.toml` (the host-ABI freshness check, `make verify-ffi`), and the MIR allowlist (`runtime_symbols.rs`) ONLY if MIR `push_runtime_call`-emits it (codegen-interned arbiter symbols like `hew_await_cancel_*`/`hew_task_scope_completion_observe` are NOT MIR-emitted, so they stay OUT of the MIR allowlist). | cut-select-waitset (`feat/v060-cut-select-waitset`, 2026-06-18): adding `Terminator::SuspendingSelect` required the two codegen `matches!` predicate lists (`is_coroutine_function` + `handler_suspendable`) plus the wasm-exclusion scan in ADDITION to the compiler-forced exhaustive walkers; the `matches!` lists do not error on omission. feat/v060-scope-deadline (2026-06-18): wiring `SuspendingScopeDeadline`'s codegen added the runtime symbol `hew_task_scope_completion_observe`; the missing `intern_runtime_decl` signature arm fail-closed at codegen with the misleading MIR-allowlist message — three registration sites (signature table + jit toml; NOT the MIR allowlist for a codegen-interned symbol). Mirror of the cut-task-sleep carrier set (`SuspendingTaskAwait`/`SuspendingSleep`). Instance of `migration-completeness` for an authority-SET duplicated across crates rather than a single retired predecessor. |
| `widen-operands-not-result-when-tightening-int-coercion` | A change removes or tightens an implicit integer coercion (e.g. same-sign widening) and adds explicit `as` casts at the now-required sites. | Migrate EVERY site, not a sample — compile the full stdlib + examples corpus and fix each `cannot implicitly convert`; never claim "zero migration needed" without the corpus compile. At each arithmetic site cast the OPERANDS to the wider type BEFORE the operation, never wrap the result: `(b as i64) * N`, not `(b * N) as i64` — the latter still overflows in the narrow type before the cast, exactly the bug the implicit widen silently hid. A trailing `as Wide` is correct only for a plain value passthrough with no intervening arithmetic. | A373 (`a194892c`): removing implicit i32→i64 widening surfaced `wire.hew` `decode_header` computing `b3 * 16777216` in i32 — wrapped for payloads ≥128 MB; fixed by widening operands. The first migration attempt claimed zero-migration and broke 23/62 stdlib files; caught at review. |
| `deglobalize-reads-stay-tolerant` | Moving a process-global table/registry/counter into `RuntimeInner` (or any per-instance owner) behind a fail-closed resolver (`rt_current()` panics when no runtime is installed). | A process-global is ALWAYS present (lazy-`LazyLock`/`const`-`None`), so its READ and TEARDOWN paths silently tolerate "no runtime" — an empty table yields nothing to notify/sweep/read. The fail-closed resolver does NOT preserve that: it ABORTS on every no-runtime-reachable caller, a behaviour change a cutover must not make. Classify EVERY call site: reads, death/teardown sweeps, and host scrapes (reachable from `hew_actor_trap` without a runtime guard, or a host scraping metrics before `hew_sched_init`/after teardown) route through the TOLERANT resolver (`rt_current_opt()`-backed, returns `None`/no-ops with no runtime); only register/mutate sites — which genuinely require the owning runtime — keep the fail-closed resolver. Build the tolerant `*_opt` resolver and a non-materialising `with_*_opt` read helper alongside the fail-closed one; audit `grep`-wide for every reader/sweeper. PROVE with a no-runtime unit test per tolerant path (calls the read/sweep with NO guard, asserts no abort) AND a runtime-installed test (asserts the per-instance state still records — the deglobalization works). The CI proving harness is `cargo nextest` (process-per-test): a `cargo test --lib` single-process run aborts the WHOLE binary on the first un-tolerated path, masking later ones — `--no-fail-fast` under nextest surfaces them all at once (peel the onion). | PR #2045 (deglobalization): two independent commits each fail-closed a former-global READ — `c012b03a` moved the monitor table behind `rt_current()`, so `hew_actor_trap → notify_monitors_on_death` SIGABRTed "no runtime installed" on the no-guard supervisor-cascade trap test; `ec1f9f85` moved the user-metric registry but missed `metrics::read_u64` (the `observe.read` path), so a host metric read with no runtime SIGABRTed. Same fix both: route the read/sweep through a tolerant `*_opt` resolver, keep register/mutate fail-closed. The sibling reads `render_snapshot`/`self_metrics`/`session_reset_metrics` were already routed correctly — `read_u64` was the missed one. |
| `checker-type-rename-is-lockstep-across-string-name-matches` | Renaming or splitting a checker-produced builtin TYPE (a new `BuiltinType` variant the checker emits for a surface, e.g. lambda-actor `Duplex` → `LambdaPid`) when downstream IR layers route on the type's STRING NAME (`ResolvedTy::Named { name, .. } if name == "<Type>"`). | The two-level design separates the user-visible checker type (used for surface/method dispatch) from a MIR Place/discriminator (used for ABI/drop routing). Place-keyed routing (drop kind, runtime symbol) is ROBUST to the rename; string-name `match` arms are NOT — each one silently stops matching the renamed type and the surface mis-lowers or fail-closes. Before claiming done, grep `name == "<OldType>"` AND `"<OldType>"` workspace-wide and migrate every site that handled the renamed surface in the SAME lane: the HIR `ResolvedTy` builder for the binding, every MIR routing/defence `name == "..."` arm, and the codegen `resolve_ty` name set (so the new-named local still materialises its handle pointer). Keep the OLD name only where it still names a genuinely-distinct surface (e.g. raw `Duplex` channels stay `Duplex`). Seed the new type in the HIR resource type-class table so drop elaboration recognises it. PROVE both halves: an accept fixture types/runs the surface (correct runtime symbol) AND a negative fixture rejects the now-removed surface (a raw channel method on the actor handle). | NTC-04 (`feat/v06-lambdapid`): lambda actors surfaced as the internal `Duplex<M,R>`; introduced user-visible `LambdaPid<M,R>` (ActorPid family, no channel `.recv`/`.send_half` surface). The checker emit + HIR `actor_lambda_handle_ty` + two MIR `name == "Duplex"` sites (captured-handle dispatch, closure-capture defence) + codegen `resolve_ty` all needed the rename in lockstep; the MIR `Place::LambdaActorHandle` drop/ABI routing (`hew_lambda_actor_send`/`_release`) was untouched (Place-keyed). Same lane fixed a pre-existing profiler-OFF build break (`fix(runtime)`): a crate's `default-features = false` dep on `hew-runtime` masked a `signal.rs` unconditional call to profiler-gated `actor_registry` fns — invisible under workspace feature-unification, surfaced only in the isolated `cargo nextest -p hew-codegen-rs` build. |
| `grammar-mirror` | A keyword, operator, or surface construct is added, removed, or renamed in the Hew language — touching `hew-parser/src/parser.rs` or `hew-lexer/` — without mirroring the change in the reference grammar files. | Every keyword/surface change must update BOTH `docs/grammar.ebnf` AND `.tmp/Hew.g4` (the ANTLR reference grammar) in the SAME commit. The hand-written Rust parser is the runtime source of truth, but both grammar files are published reference artifacts used by tooling, syntax highlighters, and downstream language integrations; drift between them and the parser causes tool consumers to misrepresent the language silently. Run `make grammar` as a mandatory local pre-push step for any surface change. Until `make grammar` is CI-enforced, tag the grammar update in the commit message so reviewers can confirm both files moved. File a follow-on if CI enforcement of grammar consistency is not yet wired. | PR #2157 (`refactor(parser): remove the wire keyword surface in favor of #[wire]`, 2026-06-22): `make grammar` ran only in LOCAL preflight, NOT CI — the canonical `Hew.g4` update was CI-unvalidated (gate substituted a static dangling-ref analysis; the Hew.g4 is a reference artifact, the hand-written parser is the runtime authority). Follow-up `add-grammar-ci-job` filed; coordination-ledger S167. |

### `analysis-scope-discipline` — match query scope to walk scope

- **area**: analysis, LSP, completions, parser tail position
- **invariant**: When the lookup is sub-body scoped, the walk that follows it must be sub-body scoped too. When the query targets a wrapper expression around a nested block, descend only into the child that covers the cursor. Tail position is a contextual property, not a node-shape property.
- **why**: Scope mismatch is a silent class of LSP/analysis bug — the right answer for the wrong region. The features look correct on small inputs and bleed siblings on larger ones.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `sub-body-scoped-traversal` | A multi-body item (Actor, Impl, TypeDecl, Trait) is queried by sub-body name and the result is fed into a whole-item traversal. | Replace `any(sub.name == name) && walk_item(container)` with a helper that finds the named sub-body and calls `collect_calls_in_block` on it alone. Add regression tests for same-container sibling non-bleed. | PR #967. |
| `completion-transparent-containers` | The cursor sits inside wrapper expressions around nested blocks. | Centralize wrapper descent helpers and update them whenever new pass-through expression nodes are added. | Original LESSONS 2026-03-25 completion fix. |
| `tail-position-context` | Tail-call or tail-expression analysis changes across blocks, match arms, or wrapper expressions. | Carry an explicit tail-position flag through match arms and nested containers instead of marking every trailing expression as tail position. | Original LESSONS 2026-03-25 tail-call fix. |
| `block-walker-completeness` | A new field is added to the `Block` AST node (e.g. `trailing_expr`), OR a block-shaped construct gains a new variant that carries child expressions. | After adding any field to `Block`, grep all `block.stmts` (and equivalent) walks across every crate with `rg '\.stmts\b' --type rust -g '!target/*'`; for each hit, verify the walker also visits the new field. Confirm `ast_visit.rs`, `calls.rs`, `inlay_hints.rs`, `references.rs`, `completions.rs`, `hover.rs`, and every HIR/MIR lowering block-walk are updated. Serialiser and enrich block-walkers that already call `walk_block_children` require no change — audit only direct `stmts` loops. Add a test that exercises the new field from each sub-system's entry point (LSP hover, completions, call hierarchy). | Commits `4bdb151b` (parser: classify tail-position if/match as trailing expression), `5a9fa76d` (analysis: completions + hover), `de382e51` (analysis: `collect_calls_in_block` at `hew-analysis/src/calls.rs:104`). `calls.rs` was the only site that silently dropped tail-position calls from the LSP call hierarchy; `scan_expr_for_stack_hints` omitted `Expr::IfLet` until `ab5fdeb6`. |
| `monomorphization-site-key-scope` | A MIR lowering arm handles a call to a polymorphic function nested inside a wrapping expression (fork-block, select-arm, task-spawn, closure, actor-receive body) and needs to look up the call's concrete type arguments in `call_site_type_args`. | Key `call_site_type_args` on the INNER `Call` expression's site (the polymorphic callee's HIR source site), never on the outer wrapper's site (the `ForkBlock`, `SelectArm`, spawn aggregate, etc.) — the wrapper site has no entry in the side-table, so keying on it silently falls through to the fail-closed guard (NYI or wrong monomorphization) regardless of whether the concrete instantiation was registered. The wrapper site is the aggregate's position; the `Call` site is the callee's registration key. Add a compiled-and-run acceptance fixture for each wrapper shape (fork, select, spawn) that exercises at least two concrete type arguments and asserts the mangled symbol names match the expected instantiations. | PR #2160 (`feat(runtime): spawn generic free functions as tasks via monomorphized adapters`, 2026-06-22): `lower_fork_block_task` keyed `call_site_type_args` on the outer `fork_expr.site` instead of the inner `call_expr.site`; the fork site had no entry, so the fork-block path always fell through to the fail-closed guard even when the mono was registered. One-line site correction. Instance of `analysis-scope-discipline`: the query scope (fork wrapper) must match the registration scope (inner call). |

### `wire-contract-test-presence` — adding a wire field is not enough; lock down its presence and population

- **area**: WASM analysis JSON, other public wire boundaries
- **invariant**: When a structured field is added to a WASM-boundary or public wire struct, it is not done until tests assert both field presence (even when empty) and field population for known-triggering inputs.
- **why**: Public wire shapes are observable contracts; a field that exists in the type but is never asserted in JSON tests will silently disappear when a downstream change drops it.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `wasm-diagnostic-json-contract` | A new structured field is added to the WASM analysis JSON (e.g. `notes`, `suggestions` on `WasmDiagnostic`). | After adding any field to `WasmDiagnostic` or `AnalysisResult`, add: (1) a field-presence test that checks every diagnostic in both the parse-error and type-error paths, (2) a population test for each field using a Hew input known to trigger a non-empty value. | JOURNEY 2026-04-11 test/wasm-diagnostic-notes-suggestions; PR #967. |

### `actor-surface-no-ask-verb` — actor request-reply is signature-driven, not keyword-driven

- **area**: language surface, actor model, spec review
- **invariant**: Hew's actor call surface is signature-driven dispatch. A `receive fn` returning `R` is a request-reply; one returning `()` is fire-and-forget. No caller-side keyword (`ask`, `.ask()`, `!`, `?`) is needed or permitted. `ask` is not lexer-recognised at any position in edition 2026; the select-arm actor discriminator is shape-based (`<actor>.<method>(<args>)` at HIR lowering), not a keyword (§4.11.1).
- **why**: Pre-2026 editions mirrored Akka classic (`.send()`/`.ask()`). The 2026 rewrite eliminated both for named actors: the checker derives tell-vs-ask from the callee's `receive fn` return type, and `LocalPid<A>`/`RemotePid<A>`/`LambdaPid<M,R>` are already distinct nominal types that mark the mailbox boundary. Reintroducing a verb at the named-actor call site would regress per-method type checking and break the signature-driven invariant without adding expressiveness.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `reject-ask-revival` | A PR proposes restoring `.send()`, `.ask()`, an `ask` keyword, or any other explicit verb at a **named-actor** (`receive fn`) call site. | Reject the proposal for named actors: request-reply is `await <ref>.<method>(<args>)` returning `Result<R, AskError>`; fire-and-forget is `<ref>.<method>(<args>)` returning `()`. Cite §2.1.1 (actor surface) and §4.11.1 (select arms) — `ask` is not lexer-recognised in edition 2026; the actor select-arm discriminator is the method-call shape, not a keyword. Carve-out: `.send()` (and `.ask()` on `RemotePid<T>`) IS the canonical verb for the generic `Pid`/`LocalPid<T>`/`RemotePid<T>` trait surface (`std/builtins.hew`) and for `LambdaPid<M,R>` lambda-actor handles (5697ea208) — those are a different, verb-based dispatch path, not a named-actor call site. Do not reject a PR that only touches that surface. | 2026-05-15 actor ask surface review; PR #1782 (2026 rewrite); PR #1804 (sealed select, shape-based actor arm). |

### `structured-concurrency-scope-fork-split` — `scope` is the lifetime boundary; `fork` is the child-start verb

- **area**: language surface, structured concurrency, parser/HIR/codegen seam, spec review
- **invariant**: Hew's structured-concurrency surface is two non-synonymous keywords. `scope { ... }` opens the lexical-lifetime boundary; child tasks spawned inside are joined automatically at the closing brace. `fork name = call(...)` (or bare `fork call(...)`) inside a scope body is the only child-start verb; it is rejected outside a scope. The legacy `scope |s| { s.launch / s.spawn / s.cancel }` surface and the `fork { ... }` block form are both removed and must not be reintroduced; lifecycle hooks attach via actor-method attributes (e.g. `#[on(start)]` / `#[on(stop)]`), not via scope methods.
- **why**: Early Hew conflated the lifetime boundary with a lifecycle-method API (`scope |s|` with `s.launch / s.spawn / s.cancel`). Type-checking, HIR lowering, and C++ codegen all carried the cost: an extra parser state field, a desugar branch in `parse_expr`, three dead AST/IR variants, and a C++ MLIR op pair (`ScopeLaunchOp` / `ScopeCancelOp`) that only the legacy surface emitted. The 2026 ratification removed it entirely (no external consumers; in-tree migration). Reviving any part of it — a `fork { ... }` block form, an `s.launch / s.spawn` method, a unified `fork-is-also-scope` keyword — would re-conflate the two roles and reintroduce the seam.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `reject-scope-fork-collapse` | A PR proposes renaming `scope { ... }` to anything else, reintroducing `s.launch` / `s.spawn` / `s.cancel` methods on a scope handle, restoring the `scope \|s\|` binding form, restoring `fork { ... }` as a block opener, or collapsing `scope` and `fork` into a single keyword. | Reject. `scope { ... }` is the lexical-lifetime boundary; `fork name = call(...);` inside a scope is the child-start verb. They are not synonyms. The legacy `scope \|s\| { s.launch / s.spawn / s.cancel }` surface was removed in the rip+rename PR and must not be revived; lifecycle hooks attach to actor methods, not to scopes. Cite HEW-SPEC-2026 §4.2 (Scope), §4.3 (child tasks), and the §4.9 historical note. | rip+rename PR landing this lesson (TBD); HEW-SPEC-2026 §4.2 / §4.9 historical note; `hew-parser/src/parser.rs` `Token::Scope` branch (rejects `\|s\|`) and `Token::Fork` branch (rejects `fork {` block form). |


### `bisect-oracle-trust` — a bisect verdict is only as good as its oracle's layering and determinism

- **area**: toolchain trust, debugging discipline, build system
- **invariant**: A git-bisect verdict is valid only when the oracle rebuilds every artifact layer the test consumes and is deterministic for the defect class under investigation.
- **why**: The Hew test path layers a compiler binary over runtime/stdlib archives; an oracle that rebuilds only the compiler tests old runtime bits, and a UAF-luck-dependent test flips with heap layout — either one makes bisection converge on innocent commits with full confidence.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `bisect-oracle-layers-and-determinism` | Reaching for `git bisect` where the failing test links layered build artifacts (compiler + libhew runtime + stdlib archives), or where the failure is allocator-layout/timing dependent (UAF luck, contention flakes). | (1) The oracle script runs the FULL layered build (`make hew runtime stdlib`), never a single layer. (2) Before trusting convergence, re-test the named first-bad commit AND its parent manually with fresh full builds; if either flips, the defect is state-dependent — abandon bisection and switch to mechanism isolation (elab `drop_plans` dumps, MallocScribble, lldb on the artifact). (3) Treat two bisect runs agreeing as NO additional evidence when the oracle is luck-dependent — they replay the same deterministic path over the same noise. | inc-4 csv regression (2026-06-10): two consecutive bisects converged on an innocent scheduler commit; manual boundary re-test was green on both sides; true cause was an interior-alias free whose visibility depended on heap layout (see `drop-allowset-from-value-flow` W5.025 extension). |

### `terminator-collapse-feasibility` — enumerate carrier CFG edges and target-IR vocabulary before planning a desugar or fold

- **area**: MIR design, codegen lowering, suspension carriers, structured-concurrency IR
- **invariant**: Before planning to collapse N carriers into a single terminator, or to desugar a terminator into lower-IR statements, confirm (1) every carrier's CFG-edge arity matches the target variant's arity and (2) the target IR's vocabulary can express the source control flow. Byte-identity is unachievable when those two conditions are not uniformly met.
- **why**: A carrier with extra successor edges (e.g. Select has per-arm branches; a ScopeDeadline body has a timeout exit) cannot fold into a no-extra-edge variant without a new IR design. Discovering the mismatch after implementation forces a rework to a side-table or multi-edge variant, undoing the desugar plan entirely.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `carrier-cfg-edge-check-first` | A plan proposes collapsing N carriers/variants to a single terminator, or desugaring a terminator to lower-IR statements. | Enumerate every carrier's CFG successor count and the target variant's successor count BEFORE writing implementation code. If any carrier has extra edges the target lacks, keep it distinct or design a separate multi-edge variant. Also confirm the target IR's op vocabulary covers all source control-flow patterns (rc-forks, arbiter switches, fn-pointer constants). When codegen ramps are irreducible, prefer a side-table over a lossy fold (the `await_deadline_ns` side-table is the precedent). Byte-identity oracle (`make ll-diff`) is the acceptance gate — plan for it rather than learning it post-hoc. | Suspension Phase-2 grounding (2026-06-20): the MIR-desugar plan was not byte-identity-viable; 2/12 carriers (`SuspendingSelect`, `SuspendingScopeDeadline`) have extra CFG edges; the plan was re-based to a `SuspendKind` side-table for the 10 pure carriers. |

### `ll-crlf-normalization` — tests string-searching compiler IR output must normalise CRLF on Windows

- **area**: test harness, portability, toolchain trust
- **invariant**: LLVM's `print_to_file` emits CRLF line endings on Windows. Rust's `std::fs::read_to_string` is binary (no translation). Any test that string-searches the emitted `.ll` for `"\n}\n"` or similar newline-delimited markers will silently miss on Windows, causing the extractor to return the entire file tail instead of the intended function body, and downstream assertions will fail on unrelated content.
- **why**: The bug is latent on Linux/macOS (where `.ll` uses LF) and on `origin/main` as long as no compiled-in stdlib function emits `unreachable`. It becomes visible the moment a new stdlib function (e.g. overflow-trapping constructors) adds `unreachable` outside the targeted function body.

| id | trigger | apply | evidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `ll-crlf-normalize-at-read` | A test reads an emitted `.ll` (or any LLVM text output) and then uses `find`, `contains`, or slicing anchored to `"\n"`. | Normalise immediately after `read_to_string`: `.replace("\r\n", "\n")`. Do it at the single read site so all downstream extractors see LF-only text. | PR #2277 (CAP-07): `machine_exec.rs` `step_function_body` extractor returned the full file tail on Windows because `"\n}\n"` did not match `"\r\n}\r\n"`; duration overflow-trap `unreachable` outside the step body then falsely tripped the `has_default` assertion. |
